Now then… In that case, cards, billiards, and dartboards. I’ll need to make another set of these before the day comes.

+++

# **185 – Merchant Miriam**

“It’s about time, isn’t it?”

As I was lining up the items to take with me by the entrance, Grace asked.

“Yeah. It’s probably about the right time.”

“I hope the discussion goes well,” said Ashley.

“Yeah. But well, since it’s Alfred’s introduction, I don’t think it’ll be too troublesome. I don’t have any other plans, so I’ll be back by dinner at the latest even if it runs late.”

“Understood. We’ll spend today relaxing at home as well.”

“Lately, I’ve been doing embroidery too. I’m planning to learn a new stitching method from Grace,” said Claudia. Marlene would probably be joining them too. They were exchanging cheerful smiles.

“Sheila-chan and I will probably practice our instruments. Since Cyrille-chan is good with the bagpipes, I thought we could try playing together.”

“…Bagpipes, huh. With a Centaur, that would make quite the picture.”

Miss Cyrille is a Centaur girl. She seemed to have been eagerly listening to Irmhild and the others’ performances in the recreation room, so I thought she might be interested, but since Irmhild was originally from the Labyrinth Village, they apparently hit it off quickly and she joined their circle.

“Sheila was looking for an instrument, right? Have you decided?”

It seemed Sheila also wanted to play with Irmhild and had been looking for an instrument that suited her.

“Yeah. I decided on drums.”

I see. Indeed, since she’s dexterous, she’ll probably improve quickly once she gets used to them. Adding percussion would likely broaden their musical range too.

Maybe it would be interesting to make a full drum set while we’re at it. Probably, Sheila would be able to handle it.

“Sheila-chan improves so quickly.”

“She’s really accurate,” said Seraphina, perched on Irmhild’s shoulder. Seraphina might also spend today listening to their practice.

“Before meeting Theodore, life didn’t have much leeway, so I couldn’t really think about things like this. I’m grateful.”

“Yeah.”

Hearing Sheila thank me so directly like that, I lightly scratched my cheek.

“I will proceed with the staff training. I believe the beginning is crucial,” said Cecilia.

So Cecilia is handling the servant training. Since the Labyrinth Village residents lived self-sufficiently, they have almost no issues with household chores like cooking, laundry, and cleaning. So apparently it won’t be too much work. In that sense, Mihaela mentioned it felt similar to when Grace joined.

It seems both Mihaela and I plan to provide some self-defense training for the Labyrinth Village residents as well. Apparently, it’s so they can protect themselves if they encounter trouble when going into town in the future. It’s certainly necessary, so I’ll let them proceed with that.

I use Levitation to load the billiards table, dartboards, and other items I prepared by the entrance into the carriage.

The alarm device, carbonated drink maker, shaved ice machine, and such are supposed to be prepared and brought by Alfred.

“—Well then. I’ll be heading out for a bit.”

“Yes. Have a safe trip.”

Seeing me off, everyone watched as I boarded the carriage. The Golem driver set the carriage in motion toward the North District.

The meeting place with Alfred is a room in the Commerce Guild assembly hall.

The assembly hall is a sturdy-looking stone building. I stopped the carriage in front of the assembly hall and used Levitation to float the necessary luggage inside. Since a familiar carriage was parked there, Alfred had probably already arrived.

This is apparently a place where master craftsmen and merchants gather when something comes up to hold discussions.

“I’m Theodore Gartner, scheduled to have a meeting here today.”

“Yes. I’ve been informed.”

An elderly man nodded. He seemed to be not the receptionist but rather the assembly hall manager.

He offered to guide me to the meeting room, and when I floated the items I brought with Levitation, he looked somewhat surprised.

“Ah. Theo-kun, you’re here.”

When shown into the room, Alfred smiled. Talcott, his bodyguard, was with him too. Then there was one person I hadn’t met before. Probably, she was Alfred’s acquaintance.

A woman with an eyepatch. She had more the air of an adventurer than a merchant.

“Pleased to meet you, Ambassador. I’m Miriam.”

“Nice to meet you. I’m Theodore Gartner. I look forward to working with you today.”

After introducing ourselves, we shook hands. Apparently, I was the last to arrive.

“Hmm. Was I late?”

“No, you’re still a bit early for the appointed time. Miriam-san also arrived early, you see.”

…I see. Well, it’s good that things can proceed smoothly.

“Miriam-san is a merchant… and she hopes to eventually establish a base in Termwills. It’s fortunate she happened to be back in Termwills now. Otherwise, this discussion would have been much later. It was also Miriam-san who found Viola injured after being attacked by monsters during her travels and entrusted her to a master blacksmith acquaintance in Termwills. I got to know her when I was looking for skilled craftsmen.”

Ah. So they became acquainted through the connection with Viola. She seems well-connected and likely understands adventurers. She probably has connections with the Adventurer Guild too…

I understand why Alfred is introducing her to me.

“I’ve accumulated considerable funds through merchant work, so I’ve been thinking about opening my own shop soon. Doing merchant work while fighting off monsters and thieves with adventurers forever would require more lives than I have. Though the lifestyle itself is enjoyable,” said Miriam half-jokingly—but the impression that she’s close to an adventurer probably isn’t mistaken. The feel of her hand during the handshake suggested it, and her movements too. She likely has martial arts training.

Being on good terms with adventurers… she probably has considerable understanding of friendly monsters as well.

“Is that so. Well then, I’d like you to take a look at the items I’ve made.”

From my perspective, I want someone trustworthy who can handle sales, business operations, accounting, etc., to get the things I make into distribution.

Considering the connection with Viola and the fact that she helped her and took care of her afterward, that aspect should indeed be fine.

Well, there are various other factors like whether she understands what I make or if her thinking aligns with my goals. Anyway. I’ll have her look at the items I brought while letting her try them out and interact, I suppose.

“You put a block of ice here, and when you turn the handle… it becomes like this.”

I operated the shaved ice machine, put the shaved ice in a bowl, added syrup, and handed it to Miriam.

“…Thank you.”

Miriam brought the shaved ice to her mouth with a spoon. She had a very serious expression.

I wonder how it feels. We played with the cards, darts, and billiards just enough to get a feel for them, then proceeded with presentations of the alarm device and food-related items. At first, Miriam seemed impressed, but gradually she spoke less and her expression grew more serious.

“Did you say… the Ambassador made these?”

“Regarding the Magic Tools, Alfred and Viola helped give them form.”

She seemed to be thinking deeply about something, but suddenly Miriam looked up.

“This is amazing… This is truly amazing! I’ve been to many places and handled various items, but this is the first time I’ve seen so many new products at once! And to think the Ambassador made them!”

Saying this, she suddenly leaned forward.

“C-could you really let me handle these!?”

“Y-yes. I was hoping to find someone who understands their value, but…”

“P-please, I’d like to request it! I want to devote my entire being to this task!”

Ah—… Seems there’s no problem. Miriam’s eyes are shining like a child’s.

I expected merchants to be more about feeling each other out, but she seems to be a somewhat different type than I imagined. She had a cool first impression, but apparently has a surprisingly childish side too.

“Please calm down, Miriam-san.”

“Ah… my apologies.”

Alfred intervened there, and Miriam released my hand and timidly sat back in her chair. Perhaps thinking she made a spectacle of herself, she seemed to shrink a little.

“What do you think, Theo-kun?”

When Alfred prompted me, I gave a wry smile.

“Yeah. If Miriam-san is willing, I’d like to ask her.”

“Really!?”

“Yes. We’ll work out the details from here on. I look forward to working with you.”

“Thank you…!”

We shook hands again.

“Glad things worked out,” said Alfred with a smile.

“Well, I thought it would since it’s Alfred’s introduction. But I had one more surprise prepared—seems the decision was made before I could show it.”

“…What did you bring?”

“Well, I’m going to make it now.”

I took out a bag of sugar from my luggage. A demonstration would probably have more impact.

“Sugar…?”

“Yes. You do this with it…”

I nodded to the tilting-headed Miriam. Using Fire Magic to heat and melt it, then Wind Magic to spin it up, making it thread-like and winding it around a wooden stick.

The melted sugar, stretched like thread, wrapped around the stick—completing the cotton candy.

The principle itself is simple, and making it into a Magic Tool shouldn’t be too difficult, I think. Well, there might be several aspects to refine regarding materials, shape, etc.

“And so, like this, you can eat the sugar like cotton. You could probably change its appearance with coloring too.”

When I showed it to everyone, they all had wide eyes.

“This is…”

With a somewhat cautious manner, Miriam accepted the cotton candy from me.

She tore off a small piece and put it in her mouth. She nodded repeatedly, her eyes widening while her mouth formed into a smile. Quite a good reaction.

“I’ll have to think about how to turn this into a Magic Tool when I get back to the workshop,” said Alfred with a wry smile.

+++

# **186 – Merchants and the Past**

Miriam seemed to have plenty of work – securing a storefront, developing sales channels, finding craftsmen for tool production, and so on.

“…What should we do? It’d be difficult for us to consistently deliver manufactured goods.”

“We have other priorities ourselves,” Alfred noted.

Alfred and Viola were occupied with developing communication devices and dealing with demon-related work. Therefore, for sales purposes, they needed to secure artisans for production.

“Regarding that matter, I believe we can have artisans introduced through the Commerce Guild. We’d hire them to work here… Well, I’ll select those who are trustworthy. Of course, ordinary artisans wouldn’t be able to handle the core components of magic tools.”

“Magic tools inevitably become quite expensive when sold… and we probably won’t be delivering large quantities, so I think we can manage.”

“If it comes to that, I’ll help out too,” Talcott offered.

Alfred gave a wry smile and nodded.

Now then. The Commerce Guild apparently had agreements among its members covering various matters – sales prices, profit shares, confidentiality of technical information, product quality control, training successors, and so on.

Ignoring these would apparently result in being ostracized by the Commerce Guild and losing access to their services.

Not that being expelled meant you couldn’t do business at all, but being isolated would create various inconveniences in production, procurement, and sales.

Although I’m not a Commerce Guild member myself, if there are established rules, I don’t mind following similar arrangements with Miriam. From my perspective, as long as I can distribute items I make without too much trouble, that’s sufficient for supplementary income.

After roughly deciding what needed to be settled, I thought that would conclude our discussion. But then Miriam said something somewhat unexpected.

“What do you think about engraving decorations or… designs onto the products to indicate they’re creations of the Ambassador?”

“Designs?”

“I enjoy rare and novel things, so I recently visited the theater. I’ve also heard about the Boundary Theater’s philosophy. I was thinking that while selling products, we could incorporate that philosophy into the designs. What do you think?”

…I see. If the products become popular and people have opportunities to learn about the design’s origins, it would automatically serve as enlightenment activity. It would also function like a brand logo – not a bad idea. As long as we maintain strict quality control, it should work to our advantage.

“That’s an interesting proposal. I’ll give it some thought.”

“Thank you. Then once I’ve decided on the store location, I’ll visit again to report. Let’s see… probably by the day after tomorrow, I’d say.”

Considering the convenience of communication with me and Alfred, she seemed planning to establish her store in the Eastern District. Well, once it opens, I suppose she’ll be our neighbor.

“Understood. I’ll prepare the designs by then. Here’s my address.”

I wrote my address on paper and handed it to Miriam. From her, I received a paper with the location of the inn she’s currently using for contact purposes.

With our discussion wrapped up like that, we left the assembly hall. Miriam’s steps through the corridor were light, and even to an observer, she seemed highly motivated, almost elated.

Well… having high motivation is nothing but beneficial from my perspective. Alfred and I exchanged glances and shared wry smiles.

“—Oh my. Isn’t that Miriam?”

Just after leaving the assembly hall, a man called out to Miriam.

“…Dexter.”

Miriam slightly furrowed her brows.

“So you’re back in Termwills. What are you doing in a place like this?”

The man called Dexter gave a thin smile.

“None of your business. Would you mind leaving me alone?”

“Is that so? While you’ve been wandering around playing at being a traveling merchant, I’ve settled down in Termwills and been making quite a profit.”

Dexter shrugged his shoulders as if showing off his attire.

…Indeed. He was dressed in fine, well-tailored clothes like a noble or something.

But somehow, from his expression down to every mannerism, he lacked refinement. He didn’t have the martial elegance in his movements like Miriam did.

Somehow, he gave me a similar impression to Byron or others like him.

“…Excuse me. Let’s go.”

Miriam seemed to have decided to ignore Dexter, walking together with us toward where the carriages were parked.

Miriam’s carriage appeared to be a covered wagon for traveling merchant use. My carriage, Alfred’s carriage. And then… this gold-plated one with tacky decorations must be Dexter’s carriage. Truly lacking in taste.

“What was that about?”

I asked while glancing sideways at Dexter, who was still watching us with a thin smile.

“Someone I met when I was traveling with a merchant caravan in the past… Well, various things happened back then. I turned down a proposal he made, and ever since, he’s been like that whenever we meet. Since I’m rarely in Termwills, it hasn’t been much of an issue until now.”

But if she establishes a store in Termwills, the situation would likely change.

“…Is there a possibility he might harass you going forward?”

“Even so, he is technically a Guild member, so I doubt he’d directly interfere with business…”

“The old-timers in charge have old-fashioned values and particularly dislike things like bribery,” Alfred added in explanation. “Being a mutual aid organization, he’d likely be targeted by the Commerce Guild if he tried.”

“My apologies for my past indiscretions. If this causes you trouble, we could reconsider this arrangement—”

“No. I think someone like Miriam-san would be hard to find even if we searched. I wouldn’t reconsider over something like that.”

When I answered, Miriam quietly bowed her head.

“He could hide his connection and have underlings do the harassing… that might be possible… right?” Alfred said.

“I do have self-defense training… I think I can handle that sort of person.”

Saying this, she took something out from her luggage. It appeared to be Miriam’s weapon.

A whip… and clearly a combat whip at that. The tip was made of metal, looking quite lethal.

“…I see. In any case, if you encounter any difficulties, please consult with us.”

“Thank you.”

Miriam bowed deeply, then got into her covered wagon and returned to her inn.

“What do you think?”

“Seems troublesome. That type tends to be persistent.”

Alfred’s expression darkened. Well, maybe I should look into his movements a bit.

After that—I returned home after spending some time at the workshop developing ideas for magic tools… specifically the cotton candy machine, and writing down spell formulas.

Regarding cotton candy, I’ve heard that when using tools, you need coarse sugar or else it scorches or clogs. We settled on preparing materials using ordinary methods first, then adjusting the magic tool accordingly.

“I know Dexter.”

When I told everyone about the day’s events during dinner, Sheila said this.

“Oh?”

“I often see him in the Western District. Sometimes he causes trouble with his followers, so his reputation is quite poor. I once saw him hitting one of his subordinates.”

“…Is that so? I heard he’s also a Commerce Guild member… what business is he in?”

“I’ve heard he’s in trade. Seems he owns ships too. If rumors are acceptable, I have some information.”

Sheila said this while preparing the fish on her plate. She cut the fish meat, neatly removing it while keeping the bones connected.

“I’ll listen. It might be useful.”

“Probably not the kind of story Theodore would expect to hear though… A while back, he tried to forcefully pick up a traveling merchant and got thrown out brutally before being kicked out of a tavern. This story is famous – whenever complaints about him come up in taverns, this always serves as the punchline.”

“…Ah. You haven’t heard anything about that traveling merchant wearing an eyepatch or something like that?”

When I asked, Sheila tilted her head as if searching her memory, then looked straight at me and nodded.

…Yeah. Confirmed. That must be what Miriam was being vague about.

Indeed, it’s not really appropriate business conversation… nor the kind of story to tell me or Alfred. Miriam has proper sensibilities.

As for Dexter… is he resentful about being rejected, or does he hold a grudge about being thrown out?

“Should I gather some information?” Sheila offered.

“That might be good… Information alone gives us an advantage and makes his movements easier to predict.”

Whether Dexter causes trouble or exercises restraint, it wouldn’t hurt to investigate various things.

+++

# **187 – Inside the Thieves Guild**

“…It didn’t work out.”

Sheila had shown her usual quick footwork when she immediately went out to meet a trusted informant after we agreed to gather information… but when she returned late at night, she looked somewhat apologetic. Her ears were drooping.

“What do you mean it didn’t work out?”

“The informant just said they couldn’t do it and to read between the lines.”

“Read between the lines, huh… So Dexter is involved, then.”

One of the Thieves Guild’s rules is not to leak information about its members. If an informant can’t provide information… the conclusion to be drawn is that Dexter must be a member.

…Well, if members’ identities were completely unknown to each other, they wouldn’t be able to interact either.

In that case, if Dexter holds a fairly high position in the Thieves Guild—say, higher than Sheila—then it makes sense why he wouldn’t give Sheila information.

The implications would differ depending on whether it was to protect Sheila’s position and safety or because he’s an executive, but since he seems to have some interaction with informants, he probably was concerned about Sheila’s well-being.

Now then. That would mean Dexter is wearing two hats—both thief and merchant. And considering what being a trade merchant implies—

“…There’s a slave trader in the Thieves Guild, right?”

“There is. They’re apparently executive-level, but no information reaches the lower ranks.”

Sheila seems to understand what I’m getting at.

That was the reason Sheila didn’t rely on the Thieves Guild when Irmhild was captured by Cardiff and the demon Linette. Sheila was quite wary of that executive.

In other words, the Thieves Guild isn’t completely unified either.

As for me… I suspect Dexter might be that slave trader. Though honestly, someone like him being an executive seems a bit cheap. He’s probably just an errand boy for the executives at best.

However… just because someone is a slave trader doesn’t automatically mean it’s illegal.

Slavery is handled differently in each country. In Verdgar’s case, only criminal slaves are subjected to forced labor.

For debt slaves—those who become slaves to pay off debts—the employer must pay them wages. Naturally, they can save money to buy back their freedom, and it’s also forbidden to sell Verdgar-born debt slaves abroad.

Debt slavery is essentially the same as apprenticeship, so if the master unjustly harms them, they’ll be punished accordingly.

The role of slave traders in Verdgar… well, personnel placement is the closest comparison. That is, if they’re conducting legitimate business.

Regarding monsters, capturing friendly monster species for slavery is prohibited within Verdgar. Many friendly species are powerful as monsters, making them poor enemies to make, and more importantly, adventurers tend to avoid such practices.

Claudia has long sent messages through oracles to shrine maidens, guiding policy toward friendship with monsters, which has been significant. With that background, Verdgar was originally a country tolerant of monsters, but King Melvin has clearly taken a protective stance, pushing things even further.

“Can you tell me much about the Thieves Guild’s internal affairs, Sheila?”

“…For Theodore, I can share some things.”

This is risky for Sheila too. Considering her position, it’s probably better not to take this information to King Melvin to discuss countermeasures or anything like that as an internal matter.

“Originally, the Thieves Guild was a mutual aid organization for sharing techniques. But it also serves as a coordinator for people in the shadows.”

The Thieves Guild is, well, similar to chivalrous outlaws.

After how my previous life ended, I have a strong aversion to thieves, burglars, robbers, and such, but the Thieves Guild isn’t as villainous as the name suggests. They provide skills to those without, establish rules, and maintain some order and balance in the underworld.

They give skills to young people without abilities or orphans with nowhere to go—some go on to succeed as adventurers. Having trained and experienced scouts or thieves directly affects a party’s survival rate. It’s not something that can simply be eliminated.

“But since the previous Guild Master died, there’s been some internal conflict. A faction wanting to maintain traditional ways, and a faction believing they should expand into various areas without strictly adhering to the rules. Currently, the latter is dominant. That slave trader executive is probably with them.”

“I see.”

Operating without rules to make money would indeed be more profitable. It’s common for those with ample funds to gain more influence.

My assessment is… Dexter is probably with the latter faction too. Even if he is a slave trader, who knows how much he follows the rules?

It seems we can’t just find Dexter’s house, stake it out with Caduceus, gather information, and call it a day.

“There were apparently conflicts over this, but I was still young then… and, well, I was placed in an orphanage during that turbulent period, so I don’t know much.”

…That makes sense. I was in a similar situation.

“Sheila-chan…”

“Hm. I’m fine.”

Irmhild spoke up, but Sheila smiled back slightly.

Well then… This isn’t something that can be solved by just crushing the Thieves Guild. Even so, Dexter’s faction is unnecessary.

Among their rules, there should be ones prohibiting killing during theft and stealing from the poor. I think those are proper rules. A faction that disregards them gaining power probably won’t lead to anything good.

What about the BFO Termwills quests related to the Thieves Guild?

If I recall correctly—after a major conflict in the Thieves Guild caused numerous casualties, there were calls to strictly enforce the rules.

I don’t know when that was, but it’s probably different from the conflict Sheila mentioned. If we act now… I feel we might achieve a softer landing.

So regarding the rule-disregarding faction, it seems best to gather information, smash them, and steer the Thieves Guild back to its original form.

In the process, we can also get information on Dexter, and if he’s using the methods I imagine, we’ll crush him too.

“Anyway, sorry I couldn’t be more helpful, Theodore.”

Sheila turned to me and said this.

“No, it’s fine. Do you know anyone who might tell us about the conflict?”

“…There’s one person. They might belong to the Thieves Guild too, but I haven’t confirmed it… If we’re acting on speculation, it shouldn’t violate the rules.”

“Good.”

Sheila grinned, and I smiled back. Well, Sheila has already revealed to me that she’s a Thieves Guild member, but given the relationship between adventurers and the Thieves Guild, I had my suspicions, though I never asked. Sometimes it’s better left unsaid.

“Who are they?”

“Um… the madam of a brothel. She was apparently my mother’s friend, but she kept me away from that world and placed me in an orphanage.”

…From what I hear, she sounds quite decent.

It’s highly likely she’s a Thieves Guild member. Still, she seems clearly on Sheila’s side and probably knows the situation well. If she’s on the rule-following side, we can operate on the assumption she could be an ally.

Even though it’s a brothel… it’s not like we’re going there as customers. Let’s go meet her. And at this point, we should also inform Miriam and gather information on Dexter.

The legal compliance of slave traders will probably relate to my future work as Otherworld Ambassador too.

+++

# **188 – To the Brothel**

I informed Grace and the others of my destination as we sat around the low table in the Japanese-style room.

Somehow, I felt strangely nervous. It’s not like I had anything to feel guilty about, but given the nature of the place…

I was just going to gather information, and considering my age, it shouldn’t be a problem.

“If we walk through the Western District with this group, we’ll definitely get harassed. It would be better if everyone didn’t come along,” Sheila said.

Well… she had a point. Since I was going for negotiations, it was best to avoid any trouble.

“Understood. Since it’s the Western District, please be careful on your way,” Grace nodded quietly. When our eyes met, she smiled at me.

Here I am with four fiancées. I thought I’d get more comments about my relationships with women…

“It’s fine,” Claudia chuckled, perhaps reading something from my expression. I suppose it meant they trusted me… Yeah, this actually makes me more focused than if they were warning me.

Not just Claudia, but Ashley was also smiling at me. Somehow… I felt a bit embarrassed and scratched my cheek. Marlene seemed to not really understand what a brothel was.

“When are you going out?”

“Miriam-san is supposed to come to the house. Probably after we talk about Dexter then.”

“She’s opening a shop in the Eastern District, right?”

“That’s what she said. But… Dexter might have been investigating Miriam-san’s movements to some extent. I think the shop needs some security until the situation calms down.”

Even if he doesn’t openly interfere with business… he might do things like throwing stones or setting fires.

“Then Lavigne and I will handle security,” Ashley said.

“I’ll go too,” Irmhild added.

Ashley and Irmhild, huh. Both should be fine when it comes to defense and detection.

“Please have Caduceus accompany you two. I’ll stay in my released form and behave myself,” Grace said.

So that would leave the home group as Grace, Marlene, Claudia, Seraphina, plus Cecilia and Mihaela.

It’s unlikely that anyone from the Thieves Guild would directly storm my house… but we do have residents from the Labyrinth Village, so we shouldn’t neglect defense.

“Understood. If anything happens, contact me using the communication device.”

“Since we’ll be splitting up tomorrow… shall we spend today relaxing together?”

“Yes.”

Ah… aside from everyone trusting me…

Given the nature of where I’m going, I want to spend more time together with everyone. I think that would make them feel more at ease.

So after bathing, we moved to the bedroom early and spent time snuggling close. Grace and Claudia leaned their heads against my shoulders, while Ashley and Marlene lay down with their cheeks against my chest and lap.

As I combed their hair with my fingers, a soft fragrance tickled my nostrils. The flowing texture of their hair was wonderful.

I then performed circulating ki. When doing circulating ki with multiple people, there’s this feeling of being enveloped in something warm together that’s quite comfortable. I also feel like the effect might be slightly enhanced.

“…It’s warm,” Grace said with her eyes closed.

Marlene reached out her fingers and gently stroked the area around my bangs.

I closed my eyes too. The soft sensations and fragrance. Body warmth and heartbeats. The flow of everyone’s magical power. A floating sensation like dissolving and drifting in lukewarm water. In such a warm and comfortable time, we gradually fell asleep.

——The next day. The date when Miriam said she would come to discuss finding a shop.

“Master, Miriam-san has arrived,” Cecilia informed me of Miriam’s visit as I was leisurely drinking tea after breakfast.

I headed to the newly created reception room on the first floor of the Western-style mansion.

“Ambassador, hello.”

“Good morning, Miriam-san.”

As we sat at the table, Claire the Arachne, dressed in a maid uniform, brought a tea set and poured tea for us.

“Thank you.”

“Yes.”

Following proper etiquette, she smiled, bowed, and left the room.

There were some slightly awkward parts in her procedure, but it shouldn’t be a major problem. She’ll likely be handling guests like this in the future too, and Miriam was a very good first guest to practice with. She seemed pleased by the novelty of having an Arachne servant.

“Have you decided on a location for the shop?”

“Yes. This is the address.”

Miriam happily handed me a paper with the address written on it.

“Just across the street? That’s right under our nose.”

“That’s right. I think it’s quite a good location… By the way, I heard this mansion is also magic construction?”

“Yes. Does something seem strange about it?”

“No, not at all. The architectural style is unique, but it feels calm and dignified. I’ve seen another magic construction before, and you could tell it was one at a glance. The walls had seams showing and such…”

Miriam looked around the room and let out an admiring sigh.

“This mansion is wonderful. No, I’m impressed. I can’t see any of those seams or unnatural aspects.”

I see. If the control is poor or there’s insufficient magical power, you can’t form everything at once, so you need to proceed by creating parts and then extending them. Those would probably appear as seams. Miriam’s observational skills and experience seem quite substantial.

“Thank you.”

I smiled wryly at Miriam’s shining eyes. She really does love rare things.

“Once you successfully open your shop, why don’t we have a banquet? It would also serve as publicity.”

“That would be helpful.”

“Please stay over at that time.”

“Yes! Definitely!”

As I said this, Miriam’s expression became even happier. I’d like to show her around today, but we still have unresolved issues.

“I would have liked to show you around the house now, but unfortunately I have business to attend to afterward.”

When I changed my expression and tone, Miriam seemed to notice. She adopted a serious expression and straightened her posture.

“Something concerning about Dexter has come up. To be direct, I suspect that Dexter is a Thieves Guild member and that rather than being a trade merchant, he’s actually a slave trader.”

“That… isn’t an impossible story,” Miriam said, her expression darkening. She might have recalled Dexter’s titles and such.

“The Thieves Guild seems to be having internal conflicts… To put it simply, they appear to be divided between the traditional faction that tries to follow reason and a faction that disregards such things.”

“If Dexter is like that… he would probably consider reason to be a nuisance.”

We seem to share similar views on that point.

“I see it the same way. The work of the Otherworld Ambassador isn’t widely known, but it includes serving as a bridge with friendly monsters. When I hear that a Thieves Guild member posing as a trade merchant is doing well, I feel the need to investigate to some extent.”

“I see… By telling me this, are you saying——you want to hear about Dexter?”

“That’s right. I’m planning to go to the Western District to hear detailed information about the Thieves Guild’s internal conflict, and I was hoping you could also tell me about him.”

At my words, Miriam nodded.

“Though I should say, I don’t know much about that man. I didn’t want to get involved with him.”

“I understand.”

We both smiled wryly at each other with that exchange.

“But about him suddenly doing well… let me see. I remember when he returned from his trading trip, he showed me some plant seedlings, saying he would make a fortune with these… talking big.”

“Plant seedlings… of what?”

“They were seedlings I’d never seen before. And then after that, we had a bit of a… argument, so I didn’t get to hear the details.”

Miriam’s wording was quite euphemistic. Anyway, it probably connects to the sequence of events where Dexter, having gotten hold of what seemed like a profitable lead, became full of himself and made advances toward Miriam, only to get thrown out.

“But I remember the color, shape, and other characteristics quite well. If I had paper, I think I could draw it.”

“That would be helpful.”

Plant seedlings, huh. If Miriam doesn’t know them, they must be quite rare. Ah… that’s a case of leaving it to the experts. I have someone in mind who I should ask about this. I’ll go to the Royal Castle later.

I gave Miriam paper and a pen to draw the seedlings. When she showed me the finished drawing, it was quite well done. The characteristics were also listed in bullet points, making it very easy to understand. With this level of quality… maybe we can trace it.

“…Um, if you’re going to the Western District, may I accompany you? Of course, I’ll make sure not to interfere with your work.”

“What do you mean?”

“I believe the Ambassador is a magician and has considerable martial arts training, but the Western District has many troublesome types who don’t understand such things. Having someone like me along might help avoid trouble.”

“That… would be fine.”

In other words, she’d serve as an escort. Certainly… Regardless of Miriam’s personality, her appearance gives the impression of being quite battle-hardened.

It would also be problematic if she were attacked when she’s alone after we separate, so we might as well go together this time.

So, to avoid standing out, I changed into clothes that weren’t noble-style, and we set out. Accompanying me were Sheila and Miriam. We went on foot without using a carriage.

Our destination was the street lined with brothels in the Western District. The sight of prostitutes leaning their cheeks against the railings of second-floor windows, looking languid, was probably a scene you could only see in this area.

That said, since the sun was still high, there weren’t any major problems.

Sheila had her face hidden by a hood and gave off the atmosphere of being quite familiar with the Western District, while Miriam had the appearance of a mercenary rather than a merchant.

There were some drunks who whistled at us, but when Miriam reached for the whip at her waist and gave them a sharp glare, they shrank back and retreated.

…Clear demonstrations like this are necessary in such situations. Nobody carries a weapon like a whip just for show or on a whim. They could tell at a glance that she was probably skilled and that getting hit would be terrible.

“That brothel,” Sheila indicated.

It was a particularly impressive building among the brothels. Rather than one of the cheap inns around, it had the air of a high-class brothel.

We passed through the brothel’s door and stepped inside.

The curious gazes of dressed-up women lounging on luxurious sofas pierced through us. Certainly… we weren’t ordinary customers.

As expected, the interior was also splendid. Ornate yet decadent. That was the impression.

“What business do you have with our establishment?” asked what appeared to be a receptionist girl in a dress, probably unable to determine if we were customers given our group composition of women and what appeared to be a child.

“I want to speak with Isabella. Please tell her Sheila is here,” Sheila answered, removing her hood.

“With Isabella-sama…?”

“An acquaintance.”

“…Understood. Please wait a moment.”

The receptionist girl went up the stairs toward the back of the second floor. Even when hurrying, she maintained her elegance—that seemed to be thoroughly ingrained.

After a short while, a slender woman in a wine-red dress came down from the second floor.

She blended in with the brothel but… was different in character from the others.

“My, my. Long time no see, Sheila,” the woman said, holding a pipe in one hand, and laughed happily.

+++

# **189 – Fate**

“It’s been a while, Isabella. The reason I came today—”

“Now, now, no need to rush. I’ll at least serve your companion some tea.”

Sheila’s words were cut off with a hand gesture as Isabella indicated the inner room with her pipe.

We moved together and settled into the room, and tea was brought almost immediately.

“So? It’s a nice establishment, isn’t it?”

Isabella said to me.

…How should I put it—the fact she specifically addressed me gives the impression she’s probing.

If she knows my background, then she’s probably observing my reactions.

“…I didn’t expect such a high-class establishment. Though I’m not quite sure about the clientele,” I replied. Being seen as overwhelmed by the atmosphere would put me on the defensive.

That said, this is the unsafe West District. It’s true that the location seems poor for a high-end shop.

“Hehe. I’ll take that as a compliment. Well, for the wealthy patrons who need it, we provide carriage service for pickup and drop-off.”

I see. Even if they come discreetly, they’re still wealthy individuals who need escorts. And since the Thieves Guild backs this place, no fool would dare lay a hand on the carriages.

According to Sheila, Isabella does her best to protect the prostitutes from other establishments as well. That’s probably why she’s in the West District, and if that’s true, she’s undoubtedly on the side that follows the Thieves Guild’s code.

Considering Sheila doesn’t know Isabella’s position, the scale of this establishment, and the extent of Isabella’s influence, I infer she holds a fairly high position within the Thieves Guild.

“Well, let’s keep the small talk to a minimum and get to the main topic. The reason you came today—you don’t seem to be a customer, nor do you want to work here…”

Isabella looked over our faces. I briefly exchanged a glance with Sheila and took the initiative to speak.

“My name is Theodore Gartner. I came here today in my capacity as the Otherworld Ambassador—I have some questions I’d like to ask.”

“Hohh.”

Isabella let out a slightly impressed sound.

There’s nothing to hide. I should assume Isabella is aware of Sheila’s current situation.

Even if not, this is a brothel—a place where information easily gathers through rumors and casual conversation. It’s better to operate under the premise that Isabella knows my identity to some extent.

“Oh my. I’ve been remiss in introductions. I am Isabella. I run this Dream’s End Pavilion. What could an esteemed personage like the Ambassador possibly want to ask of someone like me?”

“…Both of you. Could you step out for a moment?”

Sheila and Miriam nodded and left the room. Then I began.

“About the conflict within the Thieves Guild. And if possible, information about a merchant named Dexter as well.”

I threw a straight pitch, but Isabella didn’t flinch. At the very least, she showed no trace of it in her expression or demeanor.

“Hmm. Why do you think I would know such things? What did you hear from Sheila?”

“I asked Sheila if she knew any well-informed individuals who might be sympathetic to her. But this is a brothel. It’s a place where various stories gather from all sorts of customers. I thought you might have heard something through rumors, so I asked Sheila for an introduction.”

At my words, Isabella’s smile deepened.

“If I provide information, what might I receive in return? Information doesn’t come for free, you know.”

“I can’t make any promises from me personally. However, there may be those who take advantage of the situations created by my actions. It’s similar to the relationship between the kingdom, the Adventurer Guild, and the Thieves Guild, I suppose.”

Creating favorable conditions for rebuilding the Guild is the “return I can offer.” But I don’t voice that explicitly.

It wouldn’t be good for either side if someone close to the king and the Thieves Guild were seen as mutually dependent. The acceptable range is limited to mutual utilization within unspoken understandings.

For example, just as the Adventurer Guild benefits when the Thieves Guild produces individuals with special techniques. The kingdom also gains from maintaining public order at low cost, which is why they don’t eliminate them. Conversely… it also means that if their actions become too egregious, that tolerance has its limits.

“I see, I see. Then, Ambassador, why are you seeking information about the Thieves Guild and such?”

“I heard through rumors… that those who disregard codes and laws are involved with slave traders, which is problematic for an Otherworld Ambassador who advocates coexistence with friendly monster species. Although… I do think the Thieves Guild itself is necessary, given my connections with the Adventurer Guild as well.”

Isabella stared intently at my face, but eventually let out a small sigh.

“—Really. That girl is quite the handful too. I’d heard the rumors, but she’s quite the little fox.”

Her phrasing avoids giving anything away… but the “that girl” Isabella mentioned is probably Sheila. In which case, the “little fox” would be me. Well, not that I mind.

Still, she hasn’t explicitly stated Sheila’s code-breaking. If asked, both Sheila and I would simply deny it. I merely came here relying on Sheila’s connections and my own deductions. That’s all there is to it.

“Well, I understand the situation. In that case, I might be willing to share some rumors myself. After all, the Ambassador has consistently been helping Sheila and that girl’s friends, it seems.”

…So she did have information about us.

“These are just rumors, mind you?”

After that preface, Isabella continued.

“I’ve also heard the rumors that after the previous Thieves Guild Master passed away, a new faction began to gain influence. They’re rapidly building power with ample funds, gathering ruffians and arming them… expelling or harming those who oppose them, and their arbitrary behavior has been increasing year by year.”

“But there must be resistance to that, right?”

“Oh, I’m sure there is. In fact, there have been several small-scale clashes. The current situation is that it hasn’t escalated into a full-blown, open conflict yet. But in my estimation, it’s only a matter of time. Even patience has its limits, you know.”

I see. So they’re currently at the stage of focusing their efforts on the internal power struggle within the Guild.

Still… if things continue like this, it’s only a matter of time before they become brazen in the open. Once that happens, a full-scale conflict would be unavoidable.

“Who is believed to be the central figure of this faction?”

“The slave trader Randolph. He’s the man backing Dexter, whom you mentioned earlier, Ambassador. Dexter himself was originally an insignificant underling, but somehow he managed to ingratiate himself and became favored by Randolph.”

“—What about the relationship between the timing when Dexter started being favored and when Randolph’s funds became abundant?”

“…Whether there is one—I can’t say for sure, but they were close in time, I think?”

Isabella, who had been answering smoothly, showed a slight hesitation there, as if thinking before answering. Apparently, she had viewed Dexter as just one of the many hangers-on following Randolph. Indeed, from Isabella’s perspective, someone like him would seem limited in capability.

Now then… I need to proceed more carefully from here. Using Wind Magic to block sound, I continue the conversation so that Sheila outside the room can’t hear.

“I have a few more questions—”

“Ah. At this point, feel free to ask anything you like. Go ahead, don’t hold back, ask away.”

I smiled wryly at Isabella, who seemed to have grown tired of maintaining appearances, and proceeded to ask further questions, paying particular attention to the timeline.

Combining Miriam’s account with Isabella’s… the conclusion emerged that Randolph rapidly gained power after Dexter brought back the seedlings.

The problem is… the timing when Dexter brought back the seedlings was before the Guild Master died. And around the same time, Sheila’s parents also passed away.

“By the way, were Sheila’s parents connected to the Thieves Guild?”

At my words, Isabella glanced toward the door. She’s still concerned about Sheila, it seems.

“I’m using Magic to prevent sound from leaking out.”

Hearing that, Isabella gave a small shrug of her shoulders and answered.

“They were the Guild Master’s escorts. They were in the carriage with the Guild Master when it slid off a cliff, and that was the end of it.”

…I see.

“You can tell just by looking at that girl. Both of them were highly skilled. She was seen as having inherited their talent, and that assessment probably wasn’t wrong, was it?”

“No.”

“You can’t guarantee some fool won’t try to use her if she remains in the tumultuous Guild interior. Even if not, I’m taking care of the previous Master’s daughter, you see. Having a group of tragic children all together is a bit too picturesque and troublesome.”

“So, rather than from the brothel… you distanced her from the Thieves Guild.”

“Yes. And yet she comes back here on her own… foolish girl. I haven’t even told her about her parents’ background… Is this what they call fate, I wonder?”

Isabella spoke regretfully and let her pipe smolder.

…I’ve learned most of what I wanted to know. Now it’s just a matter of gathering evidence according to the outline that’s become clear.

+++

# **190 – Seedlings and Hunting**

After finishing my conversation with Isabella, I left the brothel—the Western District—behind.

Though I needed to head to the Royal Castle and had things to discuss with Sheila, my first priority was to escort Miriam to the location in the Eastern District that would become her shop.

The eaves were bathed in sunlight. It wasn’t exactly a large house, but it was tidy and had a rather nice feel to it. Hmm. If it were to become a shop, it might just suit my tastes.

“It looks like it’ll make a good shop.”

“Thank you.”

Miriam bowed her head.

“And about the design matter… I came up with this. It was a bit of a mess, so I apologize for the delay in handing it over.”

I took out a stone medallion I’d made with Earth Magic. It depicted a mermaid with wings, extending her hand as if offering a handshake with a gentle smile. Being a logo, it felt quite stylized.

“…I see. Seeking mutual friendship, then.”

“If there seems to be a problem, I can think about it a bit more. What do you think?”

“No. I think this is a good design. It might be nice to display it as a signboard.”

“A signboard? Then I’ll make something that can be hung from the eaves.”

“Really? Thank you!”

Miriam bowed her head. Well, with the logo decided…

“Ashley, has anything unusual happened?”

“Nothing so far.”

I asked Ashley and Irmhild, who were on guard duty at the shop, but they shook their heads.

Hmm… So Dexter hasn’t made a move yet.

“Miriam-san, will you be staying here from today?”

“Yes. I’ve checked out of my lodging, so I plan to sleep here from now on.”

“Understood. Given the matters with Randolph and Dexter, I’d like to station some people here for security as well. Is that alright? I’ll make sure the situation settles down quickly.”

At my words, Miriam looked somewhat apologetic.

“I feel bad relying on you so much… If there’s anything I can do to help, please let me know.”

“Understood. That said, this is a shop I’m involved with too, and it’s part of my work as well. So please don’t worry too much about it.”

“I appreciate your consideration.”

The one holding a grudge against Miriam is Dexter, not the Thieves Guild itself. Still, I doubt he’s the type to draw such distinctions, which makes him a troublesome opponent to deal with individually.

“Well then. I’m planning to head to the Royal Castle now… I’ll mobilize Caduceus, so Sheila, could you stay here for security too?”

“Got it.”

“Later, I have some Guild-related matters to discuss.”

“Mhm.”

Sheila nodded while looking straight at me.

I then headed straight for the Royal Castle. When I showed my face at the North Tower, Rosemary was, as usual, facing an Ancient Document at her desk. She must have been deciphering it.

“Ah. You’ve come.”

“Yeah. There’s something I wanted to ask about. This is a little gift.”

“It’s not… cotton, is it? It has a sweet smell.”

When I handed her the cotton candy, she analyzed it with a rather serious expression.

“Is this… sugar melted and spun into threads like yarn? Between this and that bubbly drink you showed me before… you come up with interesting things, don’t you?”

And she was right, too. Well… I suppose this is Rosemary’s area of expertise. Rosemary pinched off a piece of cotton candy with her fingers, put it in her mouth, and shared her impression.

“It melts away so easily. I don’t dislike sweet things, but it makes me want some tea too.”

So we moved to the table, sat facing each other, drank tea, and continued our conversation.

“Today, it’s not about the usual topics… I wanted to ask about this.”

I showed her the drawing of the sapling I’d received from Miriam. Rosemary covered her mouth with her feather fan, stared intently at the drawing for a while, and then finally spoke.

“I feel like I’ve seen this in a document before, but perhaps it’s not that one?”

Rosemary stood up and brought over a book.

She compared the information on the paper with that in the Ancient Document and nodded.

“Just as I thought. Slugthrow’s Tail. Medicine made from its sap has analgesic and hallucinogenic properties. It also has the effect of making one forget their anxieties. I hear a certain minority ethnic group uses it in rituals as well… but it says here that they pass down a warning orally that it shouldn’t be used indiscriminately because if you use too much, there’s a backlash when the effects wear off.”

“And if they don’t stop using it?”

“Here, it’s expressed as being led away by fairies and never returning. Poison and medicine are two sides of the same coin.”

…So it’s that kind of thing, as expected.

“The fact that you have something like this means… there’s someone bringing this into Termwills, I suppose?”

“I’m going to track them down and smash them to pieces. I wanted to know what would happen when it grows from its sapling state. It would be a problem if I couldn’t identify it.”

“…Then I’ll write down its characteristics for you.”

I’d already obtained information from Isabella about Randolph and Dexter’s base, as well as the ship owned by the two. I’d already set Caduceus in motion.

All that’s left is to locate the cultivation site and crush it. Ideally, eradicate the cultivated Slugthrow’s Tail roots. It would be preferable to capture Randolph or Dexter alive to extract information about their clients and trade partners.

Caduceus is currently at Randolph’s mansion, the primary target. Isabella said that if we end up hostile, we should be careful since he seems to have gathered people suited for rough work… but in this case, it’s actually better to explore the heavily guarded locations.

“…I see.”

Randolph’s mansion—underground in the inner garden. There’s a water channel leading to it, with a skylight above. It’s just like a greenhouse. Plants matching the information obtained from Miriam and Rosemary.

A whole field of Slugthrow, huh? Also discovered a section where they’re holding slaves captive. Naturally, this is improper treatment even for debt slaves. Really… they’re causing all sorts of trouble.

“What is it?”

“Nothing. Sorry for the rush, but I’ve got a lead so I need to get moving. First, I have to report this.”

“Is that so? Just like with me, you’re not giving any time for information gathering, I see. I’d like to discuss other matters too, but it does seem better to prioritize that one.”

“Well… I’ll come back soon to hear about those too.”

I’m also curious about the information I can get from the two Silvatorian magicians.

“—And so, there’s a possibility that saplings like this are being brought into Termwills.”

When I reported about Slugthrow’s Tail in the salon, King Melvin made a sour face.

“Slave traders and mind-bending drugs…”

“I have a lead on Randolph’s methods… but I cannot reveal the source of the information itself. There are circumstances regarding the provider’s origins.”

“…Hmm. A resident of the Western District, then?”

“It seems they aren’t a unified front either. I ask for your leniency.”

“I understand.”

King Melvin gave a wry smile at my words. He changed his wording, but he seemed to have inferred it was related to the Thieves Guild.

“It’s a drug not widely known to the public, but how is this handled?”

“For the sale of new drugs, one must submit a notification and disclose their efficacy before selling them. Therefore, arbitrarily selling an unknown drug like this is illegal. Of course, such a drug would likely be prohibited even if a notification were submitted. That said… if it’s an item we’ve never seen before, enforcement becomes difficult in some aspects…”

…I see. So there’s no loophole prepared where changing the composition slightly makes it permissible regarding distribution.

“I’d like to mobilize the soldiers, but…”

“Is there a problem?”

“I have a notion about this medicine made from Slugthrow’s Tail. There are stories of a similar drug circulating in a distant country.”

“…Ah. So it’s difficult to openly mobilize the Knight Order under the pretext of drugs and make arrests publicly.”

“That’s right. Cutting off the supply is an urgent matter, no doubt… but thinking about the subsequent communications and compensation gives me a headache.”

The reason Randolph doesn’t distribute it domestically—is it because if he handled it in Verdgar, he’d be reported by rival factions? That’s probably where his title as a trade merchant comes into play.

But I have no intention of being lenient enough to overlook it just because we know it’s there.

“Even from the angle of his connection to slave traders, Randolph has problems. If it’s about maintaining relations with the Labyrinth—”

“Hmm… That would be a reason for the Otherworld Ambassador to act.”

I finished reporting to King Melvin and obtained his permission. I contacted my companions via the Communication Device, and on the way to Randolph’s mansion, I told them what I’d learned about Slugthrow’s Tail.

“Well… drugs like these are just nasty by nature. It’s a different kind of nastiness from Magic Potions.”

And so, it somewhat turned into a lecture about the dangers of drug-like substances.

“I see…”

“It’s not that the plant itself is evil. The fact that Miriam-san didn’t know about it probably means it’s rare. And if it’s not widely known, it’s more convenient to keep it that way. So for now… our policy is to destroy all the plants in Termwills.”

“Understood.”

Since we were all going to storm the place and smash it, Miriam ended up accompanying us. The shop was just the building; the interior and furniture weren’t in yet. If we were attacked while we were away, in a worst-case scenario, I could rebuild it using Magic Construction.

Because we were on a combat footing, my home was locked from the gate to the door, and everyone could evacuate underground. That way, if my house were ever breached, they could retreat to the Labyrinth Village at any time.

“…Sheila.”

“What?”

“I want to talk about Sheila’s parents. Is that okay?”

Sheila looked at me and nodded quietly.

“Sheila, do you know what kind of work the two of them did?”

“…I don’t know. They didn’t talk to me about work. Even if I asked, they wouldn’t tell me. But… thinking about it now, I wonder if that’s because it wasn’t normal work. Like, the Thieves Guild or something.”

I see… So Sheila herself has some idea that her parents belonged to the underworld, to some extent.

She probably doesn’t imagine they were at the level of bodyguards for the Guild Master, though…

“I was told that one day, Father and Mother died in a carriage accident. Isabella and the others never told me the details, so I stopped asking, but…”

Sheila closed her eyes, paused for a moment, then looked straight at me.

“No matter what it was, I always wanted to know. If it’s related to what’s happening now, even more so. If Theodore heard anything, I want you to tell me.”

…Yeah, that’s right.

“—We’re going to investigate that right now.”

I told her about the work of Sheila’s parents that I’d heard from Isabella.

“Looking at the information from a bird’s-eye view and speculating… Randolph might have been involved in the accident involving Sheila’s parents. The timing of him obtaining the saplings is too close.”

At my words, Sheila’s eyes widened.

He got the Slugthrow saplings from Dexter, and Randolph’s ambitions grew. So he tampered with the carriage of the previous Guild Master, who was unifying the Thieves Guild, and killed him. That’s the background.

“This is still just speculation on my part. We won’t know for sure unless we squeeze Randolph, but—I support revenge if that’s the case, and I’ll help too.”

“…Okay.”

Sheila nodded quietly. Looking around at my companions, they were all nodding as well.

I believe that about her parents is something Sheila wants to know and should know. That said, even when telling her, I have to be careful she doesn’t rush off alone.

That’s why I made sure it wasn’t asked about at Isabella’s place… and why I can tell her now is because we’re all on our way to Randolph’s place together.

So from here on out, it’s not a battle. It’s just hunting down some pests. Not acting alone, but crushing them thoroughly and surely, all together. I absolutely refuse to allow a situation where we suffer losses from Randolph’s counterattacks.

Now then—we arrived near Randolph’s mansion in the Western District. I’d heard his description from Isabella, and confirmed that Randolph was at home.

“What’s the plan?”

“We could charge in head-on, but… if they escape and take the Slugthrow with them, or if remnants remain, that would be problematic. If we’re doing this, it has to be thoroughly, leaving not a single one.”

I placed my hands on the ground. Concentrated my mind. Not performing circulation, just expanding the range and reach of my Earth Magic as much as possible. This preparation takes time. I can’t do it once combat has started. That’s precisely why this is the opening move.

The building’s structure, the size of the grounds—already grasped.

“Let’s go.”

From where my hands touched, stone walls swelled up, completely enveloping Randolph’s estate. In an instant, Randolph’s mansion was isolated from the outside world.

Now they’re rats in a trap. Well then—let’s go smash them to pieces.

+++

# **191 – Assault**

“What’s going on?! What’s happening!”

“Bring lights!”

We cut through the chaotic mansion courtyard with ease. Since we’re using Night Vision Magic, we can see the enemy’s movements perfectly.

“Flame Absorb.”

The flames from the hastily brought torches and lanterns were being absorbed by the Counter Spell of Flame. The surroundings returned to darkness, preventing them from relying on numbers to attack us.

We put those who couldn’t even establish a proper defense posture to sleep or knocked them down and restrained them. But more than the others, our primary target was Randolph. I knew where he was too.

“According to Isabella, Randolph himself is quite the combatant. He’s secretive so he doesn’t show it often, but… there he is!”

Randolph was in the middle of trying to escape to the underground floor through a hidden door in the courtyard with his guards.

“Who the hell are you people?! You know who I am, don’t you?!”

When Randolph spotted us from a distance, he flew into a rage.

He wasn’t carrying any light sources. Meaning, there must be a magician in their group using Night Vision Magic too.

“—You should recognize my face and know exactly why I’m here.”

Sheila removed her hood, showing her face to Randolph. He tried to glare at her, but after staring intently at her face, his eyes widened.

“You… Bartolo and Lucia’s daughter—”

He muttered with a stunned expression, then clamped his mouth shut as if realizing his mistake.

“Don’t tell me you don’t know about the carriage incident.”

This was Sheila’s trap. A psychological attack. Hearing her words, Randolph—perhaps realizing he couldn’t hide what his attitude had already revealed—snorted defiantly.

“Hah! So you’re digging up that moldy old story now. After coming this far, don’t think you’ll be leaving here alive!”

He roared like that. The fur on Sheila’s ears and tail bristled sharply.

—The reason that would trigger the future conflict was also like that. It should have been called “betrayal against the former Guild Master.” While disregarding the rules could be interpreted as betrayal, and those elements probably served as groundwork for the rebellion… the actual trigger for the conflict was likely different.

Due to the nature of the Thieves Guild organization, specific names rarely came up even within BFO. But either the former Guild Master’s daughter or Isabella. Or perhaps—Sheila, one of them noticed Randolph’s actions. That was probably the starting point.

This time, caution toward Dexter served as the beginning, but once things started rolling, even Sheila would eventually figure it out. After that, it was just a matter of letting things run their course.

I didn’t know who would lose their lives in the conflict. Both sides would suffer numerous casualties, with the former Guild Master’s side ultimately winning. That was all that could be discerned from the outside. While I didn’t know if Sheila was among them, she would definitely be involved. Therefore, I had no intention of overlooking it.

“Randolph is mine,”

“Understood. I’ll provide support.”

Sheila said. I looked into her eyes and nodded.

If she had the strength to do it with her own hands, I understood that feeling and wanted to grant it. Standing shoulder to shoulder with Sheila, I poured magical power into Ouroboros and spun it like a windmill. The hum and glow of filling magical power, Ouroboros’s joyful voice echoed through the darkness.

Circulation. Refining magical power. Ouroboros’s radiance intensified further.

Sheila and I charged in almost simultaneously. Taking that as their cue, our companions also moved.

A Magic Stone was embedded in the hilt of Randolph’s longsword. As soon as the Magic Circle’s glow appeared, magical light floated up to illuminate the surroundings.

“He uses magic too!”

Sheila and I split left and right, leaping sideways. A moment later, a Fireball released from Randolph’s sword exploded where we had been standing. Between the magical light and the Fireball… so he wanted to secure his allies’ vision first. How cunning. He wasn’t just a Thieves Guild executive for nothing.

“You brat!”

A giant man wielding a battle axe charged at me.

“Move!”

I used Ouroboros to parry the descending axe, then reversed my staff to deliver a strike aimed at his upper arm. The feeling of breaking bone. But the giant man showed no concern, forcefully swinging his battle axe upward from below. I shifted my body half a step sideways to avoid it.

“It’s not working!”

The man laughed while swinging his battle axe with one hand. —Drugs. Either from Slugthrow or some other substance. He felt no pain and displayed brute strength. But so what.

“Tramplethorn.”

“Wh-what!?”

Entangled by the Wood Magic Tramplethorn, he was enveloped in a sphere of thorns with only his head remaining.

This wasn’t magic that could be overcome with mere strength. I cast Levitation on him and sent him flying, then slammed the thorn mass into the group rushing toward me.

“Some of them don’t feel pain. Treat them like monsters from now on.”

“Yes!”

Responses came from Grace and the others. As action guidelines, it was simple and clear. Without factoring in flinching from pain perception, we would unleash attacks aimed at incapacitation.

Sleep Cloud billowed from Ashley’s hands, enveloping the enemy group. Then, as if strings had been cut, they collapsed in heaps. Ice spread from Lavigne’s feet, freezing the sleeping people along with their surroundings and sticking them to the ground.

Irmhild’s arrows, having taken the high ground, were sucked downward, piercing through the enemies’ insteps and pinning them to the ground, while Marlene’s Saucer flew in and delivered a powerful blow to their heads, harvesting their consciousness.

As for Grace—she didn’t lose in strength contests, so she leisurely pulled them to the ground and crushed their leg bones.

“—Fall.”

The figures of those who stepped into the Magic Array deployed around Claudia were erased.

Men who had been teleported into the air were screaming as they fell. …I see. So the air above the city is also part of the Labyrinth.

Miriam was fine too. Against opponents who showed no fear of her whip, she entangled their legs to pull them down and struck the backs of their hands to deprive them of combat ability. There were marksmen too—but the arrows flying toward them were all shattered by Seraphina’s horn.

“Annoying.”

Though they were Guild members who had gone after Sheila, in the flash of the Pearl Sword’s gleam, their tendons were severed and they tumbled across the ground.

“Magnetic Wave.”

“Whaaaugh!?”

I released magnetism toward the battle axe of the man caught in Tramplethorn, then swung him around. Might as well make full use of this man too. I charged toward Randolph’s guards.

When I swung him around like mowing down with a thorn mass, many of them probably weren’t using drugs, as screams rose from the bloodied men.

“Tch! You monster!”

Randolph clicked his tongue and cursed.

“Your opponent is me!”

Sheila charged at Randolph. As he blocked her straight sword slash, Randolph’s kick came upward. Sheila leaned her upper body away and flew back while spinning. A blade extended from Randolph’s toe. Magic, hidden weapons—he had quite the arsenal.

As expected, Randolph kept up with Sheila’s movements as she flew through the air. Was he controlling the Shield deployed at his feet himself? If he could use both sword and magic, there was no reason he wouldn’t have learned it.

“Kuku, good instincts!”

Sheila bounced off the air as if using it as footing and charged. Randolph blocked Sheila’s sword mid-air. Using his superior weight, he forcefully threw her off while simultaneously releasing a blade of Fighting Spirit, then fired a Fireball with deviation shooting to cover her evasion routes.

Sheila blocked the Fighting Spirit blade with her magic tool Shield and advanced through the shortest distance. If she dodged and took the Fireball, the blast would obstruct her vision.

“Impressive! Did you inherit that from your parents!?”

“You…!”

Sheila showed her anger at Randolph’s mocking smile.

“Nah, it was tough work. Your parents had abnormally sharp instincts too! After all, if I failed, the stench would give me away! After thinking about how to kill them, I had a Golem planted under the carriage! Like this!”

A small Golem was created and charged toward Sheila. The Pearl Sword wrapped in Fighting Spirit sliced the Golem in half. Hiding behind it, Randolph threw a dagger. As Sheila avoided it by tilting her head, Randolph brought his sword down from a high overhead stance.

The high-pitched sound of clashing swords rang out. Perhaps judging she couldn’t block it with one hand, Sheila discarded her single sword stance and received it with both hands. This wasn’t Sheila’s usual movement. Parrying or evading was her norm.

This was Randolph’s gambit. Listening would only poison her ears.

“Seraphina.”

“Mm-hmm!”

Seraphina, understanding my intent, stole Randolph’s voice. Randolph tried to say something else while still smiling, but no sound came out.

Seraphina was collecting Randolph’s words. Useless to look at me with hatred.

“If it’s worth hearing, I’ll convey it to her myself.”

Randolph’s attention was diverted for just a moment. But by then, Sheila was already moving. She flowed along Randolph’s sword blade as he tried to push through, then cartwheeled away like flowing water. Her cloak activated, causing her figure to vanish.

The Pearl Sword flew out from under Sheila’s cloak, gleaming. The Pearl Sword thrown aiming at his feet. Though Randolph showed a shocked expression, he reacted to even that, trying to leap back to avoid it. But—.

“I won’t let you escape.”

Sticky Thread connected to the Pearl Sword’s pommel. The blade swung like a whip drew a large arc, slicing through Randolph’s thigh.

If he lost his mobility against Sheila, it was as good as settled.

“That’s far enough!”

What stopped Sheila from closing the distance in one go was—a guard holding one of the mansion’s servants in a full nelson with a dagger pressed to her throat.

“You bastards! If you make any strange moves, I’ll kill this woman!”

To prevent captured people from being used like this… I had Caduceus causing havoc underground simultaneously with Randolph’s capture.

Still, to use his own servants without hesitation, huh? Regardless of how effective the hostage was, he must be quite cornered.

But in reality, Sheila looked at me for just a moment and stopped moving. She couldn’t use Magic Circle. Even chantless would be unfavorable as a gamble. There wasn’t much time to think.

Randolph bared his teeth in a grin and tried to approach Sheila with his sword in one hand. With his free hand, he was even using Healing Magic. Since it was low-rank magic, it would take time to heal—.

“Hey! Drop your weapons!”

At the hostage-taker’s words, Sheila’s expression darkened silently as she released the Pearl Sword.

There was a way. For a moment, I glanced at Irmhild. I had refined sufficient magical power within my body to handle most situations. Deploying a Spell Formula based on that. The Internal Formula using my own body as a catalyst, like I did with Gardinis too.

I handled two Spell Formulas. Leaving Mirage Body in place, I used Teleportation Magic to get behind him. Using my own body as a catalyst. Forgetting the recoil pain. Simultaneous with teleportation, I delivered an impact strike from behind. In one motion, I knocked down Ouroboros and broke his collarbone, then kicked him squarely in the groin.

“Gwaaaugh!”

The man’s body showed a momentary bouncing motion in all directions before collapsing, releasing the servant from his grasp. The servant screamed as she ran away.

Randolph, who had been raising his sword toward Sheila, froze as he looked at me. His mouth hung open like a hooked fish, but his voice was still sealed. Well, I could imagine what he was trying to say.

“—I might listen to the loser’s excuses.”

In that moment of delay, Irmhild’s arrow pierced through Randolph’s raised hand.

Randolph’s eyes widened in agony as he tried to use Levitation for high-speed escape. Sheila wasn’t one to let such sloppy movements slip by either. Chasing after him with wind-like speed, she sliced Randolph to pieces with the Sword Boar’s Dagger held in both hands as they passed each other.

“Guh!?”

Randolph’s voice returned. What came bursting from his mouth was a scream. Blood mist sprayed. While she severed the tendons in his limbs to kill his combat ability, she hadn’t given him any fatal wounds.

“Theodore!”

A signal from Sheila. If he uses magic—to capture him alive, we need to harvest his consciousness first.

“Sleep.”

Using Magnetic Wave to pull the thorn mass toward me, I jumped with the combined strength of Nemea and Capella. Jumping—catching up. Directly above Randolph. Positioning the thorn mass to cover him. Deploying a Shield directly above. Kicking it down for high-speed descent. Naturally, the Thorn Ball was pulled downward vigorously by the magnetic lines. Meaning, from directly above Randolph toward the ground—.

“Wai—ghebh!”

Randolph caught the Thorn Ball pressing down on his entire body and let out a strange scream before being slammed into the ground together with it.

+++

# **192 – Return Home at Dusk**

As we were tying up the remaining members one after another and leaving them scattered in the courtyard, Randolph seemed to regain consciousness.

After glaring at me with hostile eyes, he made a subtle expression. He must have realized his magic had been sealed.

“You… bastard…”

Randolph glared at me as if he wanted to curse me to death.

“I just want to confirm one thing. About Sheila’s parents. What you said earlier wasn’t a lie, was it? Were there any other perpetrators?”

“So that’s why you kept me alive? What a softhearted fool.”

Randolph smirked. Since we had captured his subordinates alive as well, we could uncover everything about the slave trading and drug-related matters. But regarding the Thieves Guild connections, especially concerning the former Guild Master, we had no choice but to hear it from him.

Interrogation through Magical Inquisition would be difficult considering Sheila’s position within the Thieves Guild.

“Yeah, there were others involved back then. If you want to find out who they are, you can’t just hand me over, right?”

Randolph seemed to be calculating this—but I had anticipated he would try to prolong his life with such smooth talk. Did he really think I would let him get away with such a dirty survival strategy?

“Fortok. What do you think?”

“…He’s not lying.”

Fortok the Carbuncle, who had been hiding in my pocket, squirmed before answering in a small voice like that. When we set out, he had offered to cooperate.

“That’s what he says. I have nothing more to ask you.”

“Huh?”

Randolph made a foolish expression—but the next moment, Sheila struck his neck with the hilt of her Pearl Sword, knocking him unconscious again.

“…Well, since he can’t resist anymore. From here on out, whoever we leave it to will probably be the same… but considering Theodore’s position, I’ll leave it to him.”

When our eyes met, Sheila said that.

Whoever we leave it to. If we hand him over to the country, he’ll be judged, and if we hand him over to the Thieves Guild, they’ll settle the score.

“…Understood. Let’s hurry with the rest of the cleanup.”

“Mm.”

Although the underground had been secured, we still needed to dispose of the Slugthrow tails.

The people who had been imprisoned underground were waiting quietly in the courtyard, knowing they could escape. Though they looked somewhat uneasy since they were surrounded by stone walls—many were holding hands with relieved expressions. Elves, Dwarves. And there were even some with the appearance of Monsters.

“Is that—the drug?”

Grace asked.

“Seems like it. Just from looking at it, I can’t tell what it is.”

In my hand was a mass of sap, translucent green.

It had a texture like amber turned into a vivid green. From what I saw of the underground experimental facilities, they seemed to process it here, turning it into powder before use.

But… in this state, it at least doesn’t look like a drug’s raw material. It would probably slip past surveillance easily. If they brought it to the location in this state and powdered it at the selling place, it would be difficult to identify as the same thing, wouldn’t it?

We kept just one Slugthrow plant from underground as evidence to submit.

“What about the rest?”

“Petrify all of them.”

I went around casting Petrification magic on the Slugthrow tails. We needed to make sure they couldn’t be used. Burning them would work too, but I’m worried the smoke might be dangerous.

“What will you do after this?”

“Since we’ve done something this large-scale. The soldiers are supposed to come rushing in.”

That way, the imprisoned people would be found and those guys would be captured. As for the disposal of the Slugthrow tails—I guess we’ll pass the baton to King Melvin.

Dexter… didn’t seem to be here, but that guy will probably be pursued by both the authorities and the Thieves Guild from now on.

After removing the stone walls and waiting for the soldiers to storm in, we withdrew… but my reunion with Dexter came surprisingly soon.

I went to take Miriam back to her shop, but Sheila said she heard voices in the alley behind the store, so when I peeked around back… there were Dexter and his group, and Isabella and her group.

Well, um. It looked like people who appeared to be Isabella’s companions were restraining Dexter and his group…

“…Who’s there? Come on out.”

Isabella seemed to have noticed our presence and called out like that. When I showed myself, she made a somewhat puzzled expression.

“M-Miriam! A-And even the Ambassador!? P-Please tell them it’s a misunderstanding! These guys have got the wrong idea! I just… yeah. I just came to make amends…!”

When Dexter recognized us, he said that. Miriam and I exchanged looks. What in the world is going on?

“…What’s the situation here?”

“Well, you see. We didn’t expect to meet you guys here either…”

Isabella shrugged her shoulders. Perhaps understanding that I was acquainted with Isabella, Dexter’s expression turned to despair.

Isabella wasn’t wearing the dress she had on when we met in the west district, but rather leather equipment that looked easy to move in. This might be Isabella’s Thieves Guild-style equipment.

“After our conversation, some things didn’t add up, so I did some investigating, and it seemed Dexter was gathering his old comrades and making moves. Since he was trying to break into this house with weapons prepared… I figured I might as well drag him out and ask him about various things.”

…So he was trying to ambush Miriam at her shop. And from the content of the questions I asked her, Isabella must have suspected something and was trying to find Dexter to question him.

Certainly… for intimidating someone to get information, this might be a convenient situation for Isabella, but Dexter himself must have missed my raid by a narrow margin…

“Sis. This guy had this on him.”

“Ah! That’s!”

“Hmm?”

When Isabella checked the contents of the bag, she frowned.

“You probably know what that is, don’t you?”
