A leather bag was tossed over to me. When I opened it, inside were plant seeds.

…They’re Slugthrow tail seeds. So this guy took them out.

“This is evidence. May we take custody of this?”

“Well, sure, I guess.”

Overhearing our exchange, Dexter shouted.

“Y-You bastards! Don’t think you can get away with doing this to me! Just wait until Randolph hears about this…!”

“Ah, we already took care of that guy earlier.”

“—Huh?”

Dexter made a foolish expression. Since he was busy here, he probably didn’t know about the commotion in the west district. Even when told, he didn’t seem to comprehend.

Still, what was he planning to do with those seeds he took out?

Randolph seemed to have been quite careful about concealment… he shouldn’t have allowed such careless removal. If he was waiting to ambush Miriam with the seeds, and he knew my identity too…

“…You weren’t planning to kidnap Miriam-san and flee Termwills, were you? And you dare bring up Randolph’s name?”

When I said this to Dexter, the color visibly drained from his face. Both Isabella and Miriam looked exasperated.

I’ll confirm it properly later, but I probably don’t even need to ask Fortok about the truth.

If you investigate Miriam’s movements, you could probably trace my identity and the shop purchase. That means you could deduce that the Otherworld Ambassador was trying to open a shop.

If I become the backer, even if the Thieves Guild is behind it, they won’t be able to make a move from now on. So even if he caused trouble, if he fled abroad, my identity wouldn’t matter.

Still, he’s beyond redemption, or what should I say. He betrayed Randolph, who had taken him under his wing, and planned to take just the money and seeds to start over in a new land. The reason he’s so well-prepared might be because he already had a plan to escape abroad and become independent.

Well. The problem is… what to do with this guy…

“…About you taking down Randolph”

Isabella asked.

“It’s true. It’s caused quite a commotion in the west district.”

“Is that so… Then I’ll hand Dexter over to you.”

“Is that alright?”

There should be some kind of score-settling, right? Well, if we’re talking about that, Randolph too.

“Though I’ve already incurred a big debt from you. I need to return at least some of what I owe. We’re just good citizens who caught some petty thieves and handed them over.”

Isabella shook her head while running her hand through her hair.

“Honestly, if Randolph’s been taken down, we have too much to do to bother with small fry.”

“Understood. We’ll take custody of these guys.”

Even if he’s not Sheila’s direct enemy, he was an indirect cause. I glanced at Sheila, but she shrugged and shook her head.

I see. Then let’s finish this quickly. I contacted Mercedes with the communication device. There shouldn’t be any problem treating this guy as one of Randolph’s accomplices.

“…You said I should take advantage of the situation, but a debt is still a debt. I might come by again sometime to properly express my gratitude.”

“Understood.”

Isabella probably doesn’t know that Randolph was the enemy of the former Guild Master… but the information might reach her eventually. Due to my position, I need to draw a line, but if it’s separate from Guild matters, I don’t mind. Besides, that conversation concerns Sheila too.

Isabella and her group quickly tied up Dexter and the others with rope before leaving.

“Well then, shall we head back after handing these guys over?”

Sheila nodded.

“…My, my. It’s been quite eventful, but I’ll work hard to open my shop soon too.”

“That’s right. Let’s make it a good shop.”

I made a promise to meet Miriam again.

After handing Dexter and his group over to the Knight Order that had rushed to the scene, we finally began our journey home.

It was already twilight. The sky was red.

“…I’m tired. I want to soak in the bath.”

Sheila looked up at the sunset and narrowed her eyes. Maybe she wanted some time alone.

Yeah. After she uses that time to sort out her feelings, let’s all spend some time together, slowly and peacefully.

Irmhild took Sheila’s hand.

“Let’s go home, Sheila-chan.”

“…Mm. Irmhild. I want to hear you play the lute again.”

“Okay. Anytime.”

Like that, the two of them exchanged smiles.

“Everyone… thank you for helping me.”

Then Sheila bowed her head to us. Both I and everyone else quietly smiled and nodded.

+++

# **193 – The Royal Family’s Circumstances**

It seems Miriam is energetically handling the store opening preparations by purchasing and bringing in necessary items, so it should be ready soon.

I was proceeding with my usual training, but I wanted to give Sheila some settled time too.

So today’s training is canceled. I decided to head to the Royal Castle to hear various updates from King Melvin and Rosemary.

First, when I went to request an audience with King Melvin, I was told he was receiving guests and wouldn’t have time for a while.

In that case, I should probably hear from Rosemary first.

I told them I’d come back later to request another audience, and was seen off by a bowing maid before heading to the North Tower. Riding the Floating Stone up the tower, I appeared at Rosemary’s room.

“Has the problem been resolved?”

Those were the first words out of Rosemary’s mouth when she saw me.

“For now. Though the city might experience some disturbances.”

“Those handling that kind of drug… must be connected to the underworld merchant circles. With their leader gone, there might be some confusion.”

“Seems there are other organizers, so the confusion probably won’t last long.”

“Is that so? Well, that’s good then. Now, let’s proceed with our discussion.”

As usual, we sat across from each other at the table.

“Last time, I believe we discussed analyzing ancient documents related to demons.”

“Yes. Not just codes, but even the characters used and phrasing conventions change with each era, giving me a headache… But I’ve been tracing literature regarding the connection between demons and seals. According to legends, long after demons appeared… several large-scale battles occurred between them and humans.”

It’s said that several countries were destroyed, and those taken away experienced hellish suffering as the demons’ livestock. Demons are said to respect the strong, but conversely show no mercy toward the weak.

Since their dietary preference is others’ negative emotions, the relationship inevitably becomes one of predator and prey. There are countless anecdotes, like when a delegation was sent seeking friendship only to be torn to pieces.

So the battles against demons were apparently extremely fierce. Many documents were lost during the demon wars, leaving few remaining records.

In that sense, Termwills has never been conquered, thanks to Claudia’s protection. Given the labyrinth system, both supply replenishment and combat enhancement can be handled within the city.

Furthermore, the Moon Goddess’s Blessing is effective against negative magical power like miasma and curses like the Amulet of Evil Repulsion. This must make things difficult for the demons.

Regarding these wars between demons and humans—chronologically, they occurred long after the magical storm Claudia mentioned. At least after the magical storm subsided… human nations were established and organized enough to fight demons.

“So the turning point in the disadvantageous situation came when countermeasures against demons and barrier magic were developed.”

Currently, barriers are deployed in urban areas and major strongholds of various countries. This serves as countermeasure against demon intrusion, enabling stronghold defense.

Simultaneously, making strongholds harder to attack means cutting off the demons’ food supply.

“That’s right. And that’s what we’ve discovered. Please keep in mind this is a hypothesis pieced together from various documents and current circumstances.”

After this preface, Rosemary continued.

“Countermeasures against demons—like widely spreading the Moon Goddess’s Blessing, or using barrier and sealing techniques by harnessing environmental magical power… It seems a group of magicians appeared who brought such advanced magical technology.”

“A group of magicians…”

“What you’re using is… probably magical power circulation, right? Among them, some apparently mastered it as a countermeasure against demons. Those capable of circulation due to their magical aptitude were quite limited. Plus, being magicians who fought on the frontlines, the technique declined after demon activity waned… but magical power circulation itself is recorded in ancient documents as one of the advanced techniques.”

That makes sense. Rosetta had researched and knew about circulation’s existence too. Probably an ideal technique for Rosetta’s fighting style, I’d imagine.

“Returning to our topic. With established countermeasures and stronghold defense, the balance tilted somewhat toward the human side. After large-scale battles with demons—they managed to repel but couldn’t destroy the demons’ overlord… so they decided to seal it. The kings of various countries discussed it—and the method employed was to split the demon overlord into soul and vessel, sealing them in separate locations.”

Overlord… Probably referring to the first one Gardinis mentioned.

“So one seal is in Termwills?”

“We haven’t found any descriptions of where or how it was sealed. So we don’t have documents connecting that part yet, but probably so. Soul and vessel. We don’t know which is sealed in the labyrinth…”

In that case… the Miasma Orb must have been brought from wherever the other half is sealed.

“The other location must be somewhere.”

“—Silvatoria, perhaps? Chronologically, maybe its predecessor Beriondora.”

Considering monsters emerge from the north… I think it might be around there.

“I see… Indeed, that country’s magical technology is head and shoulders above others… and considering the magician group as being from Beriondora makes sense. The unknown sealing location also fits if we assume the magicians settled there and established a country…”

“That’s true…”

That would explain why Beriondora was attacked by demons until the very end.

“…Should I visit that country?”

“Investigation in Silvatoria might be necessary… but you should probably avoid Beriondora itself. Since demons broke the seal and brought out the Miasma Orb, we should assume Beriondora might contain the enemy’s main base?”

“If they can only send elite forces here in small numbers, then repelling them and continuously whittling down their strength is the correct approach?”

“That’s what I think. Starting with the female demon from Cardiff that you defeated, then Blazing Heat, Dancing Sword, Black Bones. The notoriety of the latter three is quite significant. Though we don’t know how many demons of similar caliber remain…”

…Indeed. No reason to abandon the advantage of being able to defeat them individually. With Claudia here too, the labyrinth is definitely our home ground.

“Warning Silvatoria through diplomatic channels might be possible, but superficially things are calm now. It’s possible that sending investigators from Silvatoria could become the cause… of something.”

“…Quite difficult. I’ve heard that country has political instability too.”

“Ah. The Crown Prince matter.”

Rosemary smiled meaningfully.

“I’ve never met him myself. But since the amiable Stephania dislikes him, he must be quite something.”

First Princess Stephania, huh. Well, that’s information I can trust.

“Though Verdgar isn’t in a position to laugh about that either.”

“You’re one to talk.”

At my words, Rosemary happily covered her mouth with her feather fan, shoulders shaking.

“Though I was one who got disposed of too, since you took care of Roy, our political instability is limited to the discord between the Grand Duke’s and Duke’s families.”

“…Is that so?”

“You haven’t heard from Father, then? Father was born between the Duke’s family daughter and the royal family.”

“I’ve heard about the tug-of-war between the royal, grand ducal, and ducal families.”

But this is the first I’ve heard about discord between those two families.

“The Verdgar royal family, due to the Nation Protecting Ceremony relationship, also has talent maintenance issues, right? The originally related grand ducal and ducal families produce strong candidates to marry into the royal family. Royal authority is strong, but precisely because of that, there’s tug-of-war among the three families. Indeed, the First Queen is the grand ducal family’s daughter. Because of this, the grand ducal and ducal families try to interfere with the royal family, and Father pretends to listen while neutralizing their influence, or sometimes mediates between them—he’s caught in various dilemmas.”

…That sounds like quite difficult navigation just hearing about it.

“Roy aside… Josiah and Stephania are following Father’s example, trying to remain as moderate as possible. In that sense, those two are honor students. The First Queen doesn’t give special treatment to the grand ducal family either.”

Said the delinquent Rosemary. Well, in terms of royal independence, Rosemary’s thinking does align with moderation. She advocates meritocracy over family background or hierarchy.

“What about Rosemary?”

“My mother was from the neighboring country Glowfonica’s Marquis family.”

“Ah. So that’s why Prince Helfried’s study abroad destination is—”

“Yes. Glowfonica. I was following Josiah’s example and keeping my distance from Glowfonica.”

Rosemary was basically operating on the premise of becoming king, after all.

“Anyway, with you here, Father might find it easier to make various moves.”

Rosemary’s expression as she said this was hidden behind her feather fan.

+++

# **194 – Grand Duke Devonis**

…I imagine Rosemary’s ideal is likely the strengthening of royal authority and centralization.

The fact that she left goodwill with Growfonica to her younger brother while forming her own faction suggests she doesn’t want the maternal relatives to gain power. Following Prince Josiah and Princess Stephania’s methods clearly indicates she wants to diminish the influence of the Grand Duke and Duke families on the royal house.

This also appears in her meritocratic aspects—according to Rosemary’s thinking, she would prioritize marriages with excellent magicians, clerics, and shrine maidens “for the future of the Labyrinth and the royal house” over those two families. With the actual examples of Albert and Marlene already existing, Rosemary recognizes those two’s abilities.

King Melvin and the First Queen seem to be steering things in a direction where they don’t take sides with either family to prevent conflict between them. After saving face for the Grand Duke family through marriage with the First Queen, both the Second and Third Queens appear to have been chosen to have no connection with either family.

Keeping such background in mind while looking at the current situation from above…

“…Were they unable to investigate Marlene’s attempted assassination deeply because they were wary of maternal relatives?”

“Rather than wariness, I’d say it’s about maintaining relationships. It would be quite problematic if poking the bush too much made a snake appear. After the demon attack, reconstruction was the top priority, and we needed cooperation from both the Grand Duke and Duke families for that. If we had pursued a thorough investigation and found connections to either family, worsening relations would have been unavoidable.”

As a result, placing a person from the Grand Duke family in Roy’s vacant position suggests Roy had no connection with the Grand Duke family and it was his solo act… but Roy probably understood the circumstances and acted accordingly.

That said, it’s been bothering King Melvin too… The reason he recently supported my investigation is probably because the situation is different from back then.

This is what Rosemary meant when she said King Melvin can move more easily now.

The scars from the King of Deathly Slumber’s attack have been largely restored, the Knight Order has been rebuilt with personnel and equipment being refreshed, and the royal house can take a much stronger stance against both families.

I myself have no ties with either family either.

“Grand Duke Debonnis should be coming to the Royal Castle today… Well, I thought it would be better to let you know. Grand Duke Debonnis is no fool, so I don’t think there will be any problems though.”

I see. So King Melvin’s visitor was Grand Duke Debonnis.

Since the Grand Duke’s second son is King Melvin’s cousin—that would mean the Grand Duke’s aunt married King Melvin? The family tree must be quite complicated.

After finishing my conversation with Rosemary, I headed toward the King’s Tower to request another audience with King Melvin when I saw an elderly man approaching from the opposite direction with his attendants.

Noticing me, he quietly spoke.

“Hmm. That hair and eye color. You must be the rumored Otherworld Ambassador. I am Debonnis Bartwhistle.”

“You must be Grand Duke Debonnis. As you wisely observed, I am indeed Theodore Gartner, the Otherworld Ambassador.”

“…Yes. I’ve heard of your achievements. Keep working hard.”

Debonnis continued on his way without stopping.

…Somehow, I had braced myself expecting something more. I also got the impression he was being careful not to get too involved with me. And that expression where he narrowed his eyes slightly and smiled at the end… it looked like that of a tired person, somewhat lonely even.

“—Theodore-kun?”

While I was watching the hallway where Grand Duke Debonnis had disappeared, Crown Prince Josiah called out to me from behind.

“Your Highness Josiah.”

“You didn’t happen to see Grand Duke Debonnis around here, did you? Did he say anything to you?”

“We exchanged a few words of greeting, but…”

I wondered if I should mention my impression, but Prince Josiah looked at me as if urging me to continue.

“He seemed somewhat tired.”

“I see…”

Prince Josiah also made a bitter face at my response.

“I asked for some time after my conversation with Father. We talked about the conflict with the Duke family and the matter with Roy… I got a bit emotional, you see.”

Did he say something excessive?

It’s probably true that the conflict between the Grand Duke and Duke families was in the background of Marlene’s attempted assassination. It’s also true that Roy took advantage of that.

From Grand Duke Debonnis’s perspective, he probably had complaints about King Melvin, the First Queen, Prince Josiah, and Princess Stephania for not providing much favor.

But Roy was different. The fact that a person from the Grand Duke family was placed in Roy’s vacant position also means Roy had somewhat closed the distance with the Grand Duke.

So the idea that Grand Duke Debonnis’s words and actions influenced Roy’s way of thinking… isn’t entirely unthinkable.

And Prince Josiah probably criticized him for that. From Prince Josiah’s perspective, Roy was originally his close younger brother… so he would want to voice at least one complaint to Grand Duke Debonnis.

Though someone of the Grand Duke’s stature probably doesn’t have such naive thinking… judging by how he kept his distance from me, Prince Josiah’s words might have actually hit quite hard.

“…If you regret it, wouldn’t it be good to say a word to him?”

“—You’re right. I’ll do that.”

Prince Josiah gave a wry smile at my words and quickly walked down the hallway.

“Ah. Sorry to keep you waiting, Theodore.”

As I waited in the salon, King Melvin appeared.

“Yes.”

Tea was promptly served.

“I visited the North Tower earlier.”

The matters with Grand Duke Debonnis and Prince Josiah didn’t seem like something I should meddle in.

I proceeded with my own story. First, I told King Melvin what I had discussed with Rosemary. Since it involved Silvatoria, it would likely be relevant to our discussion from here on.

“I see… The founders of Barrier Magic—those who built the Spirit Hall and Moonlight Temple having connections with Silvatoria… That’s not an impossible story.”

“Has anything been discovered about those magicians from the other day?”

“Apparently those individuals are retainers of Marquis Zilbolt of Silvatoria. They insist they’re former retainers, but we believe it’s something arranged formally as a countermeasure against Magical Inquisition.”

Actually, if it’s formally arranged, it wouldn’t be a lie, and they could make excuses. Considering they’ve set up preventive measures, it’s highly likely they would feign ignorance even if we protested.

But Marquis Zilbolt, huh. I’m not very familiar with Silvatoria’s nobility, so I don’t know what kind of person he is…

“He belongs to that Crown Prince’s faction… but I haven’t heard good rumors about him. Precisely because of that, I can’t say it connects all the way to the Crown Prince.”

So the question is whether it’s Marquis Zilbolt’s independent decision or the Crown Prince’s intention. They probably couldn’t determine that even by interrogating those two.

Hearing the individuals’ opinions probably wouldn’t be meaningful anyway. More fundamentally, we still don’t clearly see the reason for sending operatives to our side.

“Regarding confirmation of the magicians’ identities and our protest. We should definitely proceed with this. I’ll prepare a personal letter so it doesn’t reach the Crown Prince’s ears. We also need warnings about the Beriondora incident.”

“Indeed… There’s a possibility the Crown Prince might interfere if we use ordinary envoys.”

“Yes. Next, regarding Randolph and Slugthrow’s tail.”

“Yes.”

“We’ll confiscate the wealth Randolph accumulated through improper means. This will be used to compensate the victims. After some verification experiments, Slugthrow’s tail will also be disposed of. That should cover it.”

Well… that seems reasonable. I don’t know how much Randolph had accumulated though.

“…So, let’s end the stressful talk here. I’m also a bit tired today. There’s still various confusion regarding southern governance.”

So that was Grand Duke Debonnis’s business. Although the Duoveris Cult’s power has diminished, the south still seems to have its share of troubles.

“Shall we change the topic then?”

“That would be good. I heard from Albert that you all are doing some quite interesting things.”

“Are you referring to opening a shop in the Eastern District?”

“Yes, that’s it. I was thinking of ordering some of the things you’ll be selling there for the castle as well.”

Billiards and darts. And cards too probably? The shaved ice machine and carbonated drinks as well?

He might have heard about the entertainment room matters from Albert. Indeed, placing them in the castle would make for good advertising.

“The King’s Tower and Knight’s Tower. And also the Guesthouse. Do you think it’s possible?”

“Understood. I’ll arrange to deliver them as soon as possible.”

“Yes. I’m counting on you.”

With that, King Melvin showed a smile that reminded me of Albert’s.

+++

# **195 – Craftsmen and Banquets**

“…And so, our first order will be for delivery to the royal family and the Royal Castle.”

Since King Melvin’s order was for the shop, we decided that instead of me making the items myself, we would deliver products made by the craftsmen.

I explained the current situation to the craftsmen Miriam had gathered from the masters of the Commerce Guild. As expected, there were quite a few Dwarves among them. The location was the Eastern District. We had gathered in one of the shops Miriam had found for this explanation. Since the back of the shop had a garden, we planned to use that area as our workshop.

“The royal family right from the start…”

“That’s quite the promising business.”

The craftsmen were visibly excited.

Yeah. I’m hoping this will serve as good motivation for them. You couldn’t ask for a better first job.

“With that said, here are the product samples.”

I removed the cloth and showed the craftsmen the product samples. I presented them both as finished products and disassembled into their individual materials and components so they could be put together.

Since many of these items didn’t exist elsewhere, I wanted them to first understand what they were. The best way to help them understand the products was to actually handle and play with them. There was also the aim of helping them bond with each other.

“Hmm? This thing… was it made using Magic for shaping and polishing…?”

“We do use Magic for minor processing sometimes too… but this is on a whole other level…”

Given their profession, they seemed to focus on different aspects. They held the billiard balls up to the light to examine their spherical surfaces, lined up the patterns on the backs of the cards, all with serious expressions.

“We’d like you to make these. I imagine I’ll bring other prototypes in the future as well. And also—please incorporate this design by firing or engraving it onto the products.”

I placed a stone medal on the table. Seeing the design, the craftsmen nodded in understanding.

“Looks interesting. If they can show us something this good made with Magic, we professionals can’t afford to lose.”

“Yeah. Seems like worthwhile work.”

“Please try playing with them and testing them out. I think it will help you see what areas need attention to make them better quality.”

When I said that, the craftsmen grinned and began enjoying themselves in their own ways—reading the rules and throwing darts, starting card games, turning the shaved ice machine.

One Dwarf craftsman chugged a carbonated drink and rolled his eyes. His beard made eating cotton candy difficult, and his fellow craftsmen were pointing and laughing at him… Well, it’s good that they seem to be enjoying themselves.

“How does it seem?”

Miriam asked me as I finished my explanation.

“We’ll have to see their skills from here on out… but they seem reliable.”

“That’s good to hear.”

Miriam smiled.

The fact that they could tell things were made with Magic suggested they had considerable experience. If their observational skills are sharp, they should produce good quality work, and they seemed highly motivated too.

“So, does this mean we’re mostly ready for the shop opening?”

Alfred smiled.

“Yes. The sign is finished too.”

It was a hanging sign with the logo. Made from copper plate with an impressive finish… Viola had processed this for us.

The shop’s name was Brightwelt Labyrinth Trading Company.

It was a derivative of Brightwelt Workshop, since we would be distributing products made at the workshop. Alfred had said he wanted the “Labyrinth” part to pair with Boundary Theater, so I incorporated it.

I was also thinking that, going forward, we could provide some employment for the Labyrinth Village residents and the Orphanage children. I also thought that if having the Trading Company’s products in the Royal Castle generated buzz, we might get more orders, but we’ll see how that goes.

“So, while it’s not exactly for the opening celebration… I’d like to invite Alfred, everyone, and Miriam-san to my home. What do you think?”

It felt like keeping a promise. When I said that, Miriam’s eyes sparkled.

“Thank you for having us today.”

Heather, the Adventurer Guild receptionist, bowed politely. Three people had come from the Adventurer Guild: Auria, Oswald, and Heather. Forestbird, Justia, and Dominique were with them too.

Heather had originally had quite a bit of contact with me, and recently she’d been doing work related to the theater as well.

“Please, this way.”

“Oh my.”

When Cecilia came to guide them, Auria’s eyes widened slightly.

“I am Auria. Pleased to meet you, friend of the forest.”

Cecilia had looked somewhat nervous, but Auria was the one to smile and extend her hand.

“The pleasure is mine. Lady Auria.”

Cecilia also smiled and took her hand.

“Though, I should say I haven’t returned to the forest in quite some time. It’s presumptuous for one like me to call myself a friend of the forest.”

“I’m in a similar situation.”

“I see. Then we are both living in the same land now. If you ever have any troubles, feel free to consult me anytime.”

“Thank you.”

Auria was easygoing, so they seemed to have broken the ice successfully. Elves who have left the forest and grown accustomed to human settlements don’t tend to stick strictly to racial customs. They’re aware of them, of course, but among them, Auria is special—she has a particularly deep understanding.

The invited guests continued to arrive. The breakdown of the banquet guests was as follows: from the workshop, Alfred, Viola, Talcott, and Miriam. Then the Dwarf master craftsman. Plus Ophelia and Cindy. From the Moon Temple, Head Shrine Maiden Penelope, and from the Orphanage, Director Sandra. From the Knight Order, Mildred, Chester, and Mercedes. The fact that there were also Labyrinth Village residents… made it quite a large, lively gathering.

…Well, I hadn’t initially planned for it to be this grand. But after inviting just a few people, it quickly snowballed.

Well, only a portion of the workshop members would be staying overnight.

The recreation room and the central courtyard were prepared with food made by Grace, Cecilia, Mihaela, and the Labyrinth Village residents. They had been preparing since morning, so it was quite lavish. There was roasted bird stuffed with herbs, among other creatively prepared dishes.

“To commemorate our opening, I’m truly happy to have you all gathered here today. It may be a modest affair, but I hope you will enjoy yourselves.”

After that greeting and a bow, applause rose from the attendees.

“I think you’d find listening to their performance more enjoyable than my boring speech, so I’ll hand it over to them.”

Saying that, I bowed once more and stepped down from the edge of the fountain.

As my greeting ended, Irmhild and the others began their performance. It was a bright, cheerful melody fitting for a banquet. Just listening to it made one feel merry—they were truly impressive.

“That’s quite rare! Well, everything in this mansion is rare, but… Getting to hear their performance before the next full moon is a real privilege.”

Miriam’s eyes were sparkling. Her gaze was fixed on the drum set Sheila was playing. Exchanging smiles with Irmhild, Sheila looked like she was having a great time playing.

“It’s several types of percussion instruments combined into one. With a certain level of skill, one person can handle the percussion section like that. In Sheila’s case, it’s less about skill and more about her innate Dexterity.”

“I see…”

While using ear muffs incorporating Wind Magic to protect their hearing from the drum volume, Sheila’s rhythm remained precise. Her drumstick handling was also splendid. It was possible precisely because of her excellent Dexterity and reflexes.

“Are you planning to sell that as a product too? Though it might be better to wait until the shop is established and we have some breathing room.”

“Yes. I think it’s groundbreaking. I have some musician acquaintances, so I thought I’d ask for their opinions sometime.”

Even as she said that, Miriam seemed to have some conviction about it.

+++

# **196 – The Head Shrine Maiden and the Goddess**

“I see… So the key lies in how you apply the spin.”

Talcott furrowed his brows while muttering about the movement of the cue ball I had struck. Quite the keen observation.

“You hit it slightly above just now, didn’t you? By moving it skillfully like that, you can either secure an advantageous position for your next shot or adjust the trajectory after the carom.”

“When it hits the rail, the rebound angle changes depending on the strength of the impact.”

“This runs deeper than I thought…”

Alfred, Talcott, Chester, and Miriam—all four of them—were engaged in a serious discussion about billiards.

They wanted to see my skills, so I joined the game, and it seemed to be providing good stimulation. Attempting techniques that lead to comebacks or digging your own grave adds depth to the game.

As expected, Chester, originally skilled with a spear, showed considerable finesse with the cue as well.

Next, I applied backspin to the cue ball, caroming it off the 8 and 9 balls into the pocket. Cheers and applause erupted.

“There are methods like making the ball jump or curve… but if you’re not used to it, you might tear the cloth, so I’d appreciate it if you stuck to regular play for a while.”

“Understood. In that case, let me try the technique you just showed us.”

It was good to see everyone enjoying themselves, not just with billiards. I wondered how the others were doing.

Seraphina seemed to have taken a liking to the custom darts. She appeared to be having fun playing darts with Ashley.

Forestbird, Oswald, and Auria seemed to be playing cards.

“Come on, Oswald. Hand over your cards.”

“Damn you…”

It seemed Auria was currently dominating. Oswald was being forced to surrender his powerful cards to her.

“…Um, excuse me. I’ve been wondering since we met at the theater the other day… Have we met somewhere before? It’s as if I’ve known you since long ago, I suppose. I feel something… peculiar.”

As I scanned the recreation room, I saw Penelope speaking to Claudia with a somewhat puzzled expression. Nearby, Marlene was smiling happily.

Penelope was the Head Shrine Maiden. Perhaps she sensed something about Claudia’s presence.

“Perhaps—we have.”

Claudia glanced in my direction. She seemed to be asking whether she should reveal it.

I nodded and headed over to them. Penelope was trustworthy, especially considering her relationship with Marlene. Claudia didn’t seem to enjoy being treated with special regard… but if I explained the circumstances, Penelope would understand.

Claudia likely had some understanding of Penelope’s character and wanted to reveal the truth to her, which was why she sought my opinion. In that case, I wanted to honor Claudia’s wishes.

“Could you come with me?”

The three of us stepped out into the courtyard and moved to a bench a short distance away.

“I imagine this will come as a shock—”

With that preface, Claudia revealed that she was Shuath.

“That… I, well… I am indeed shocked…”

Penelope seemed stunned at first, but soon she nodded with a serious expression, narrowing her eyes as if beholding something divine.

“But indeed… now that you mention it, it makes sense. I sense the same presence from Claudia-sama as during the Oracle.”

Marlene nodded repeatedly, and Penelope smiled as she patted Marlene’s head.

“I’m sorry I don’t look like the figure described in the Temple. If you require proof, I can send a revelation to you, Penelope.”

Ah, that’s right. Claudia was somewhat self-conscious about her childlike appearance.

“That won’t be necessary. I’ve heard legends that the Messenger takes the form of a beautiful maiden. Reflecting on it now, that must have been Claudia-sama.”

“If you’re referring to the tales from the Labyrinth… perhaps so.”

Claudia gave a wry smile.

“If it is Claudia-sama’s wish, I shall keep this conversation to myself. I am honored to serve Claudia-sama, who has watched over and guided us all this time.”

Penelope placed a hand over her heart, closed her eyes, and bowed. Knowing that Claudia disliked being treated as a goddess, she seemed to avoid excessive ceremony while still showing the utmost respect.

“I am grateful to the children of the Temple as well. Without you, the people here might not have been accepted so easily.”

Claudia tilted her head slightly and smiled gently. She was probably right about the foundation for the Labyrinth Village residents’ acceptance.

“…Speaking of which, what about the other gods besides Claudia?”

The question occurred to me suddenly.

Claudia—Shuath—wasn’t the only one worshipped as a deity. In various sects, there were undoubtedly beings who answered the prayers of shrine maidens and supplied power as blessings.

So—perhaps the other so-called gods were members of the Moon King’s lineage?

“Those are most likely Spirit Kings who have existed for ages.”

“Spirit Kings… I see. Since spirits are influenced by human thoughts…”

It was similar to how Seraphina gained strange traits during the spirit incident.

“Exactly. Powerful spirits, through being revered, eventually had their aspects fixed and attained divinity. I have similarities, but unlike spirits, my essence isn’t swayed.”

That explained why the Moon Goddess’s commandments were comparatively lenient. Spirits with fixed aspects would likely be less flexible than Claudia in many ways.

Still, since they originated as spirits, many tended toward nature worship, leading to mutual relationships rather than conflicts between deities, which minimized religious strife.

Well, with threats like Magical Storms, monsters, and demons abound, perhaps it also fostered unity among humans.

“Ah, that was a wonderful bath.”

“I’m glad to hear it.”

The banquet had ended, and Miriam returned from the large bath in high spirits.

“This will be your room.”

“Oh my… This is quite an interesting design.”

Miriam, guided to the guest room by Cecilia, let out an admiring voice. As expected, the loft seemed to catch her interest.

Lofts had the drawback of trapping heat in summer, but by engraving simple Wind Magic and Water Magic into Magic Stones, we could cool and circulate the air, paying some attention to climate control.

“If the room gets too warm, please insert a Magic Stone into this recess to adjust it.”

“You’ve thought of everything…”

We skipped it this time since it required somewhat elaborate Magic Tools—but by winter, I hoped to use Magic Construction to install central heating with warm water pipes in every room.

A knock sounded at the door.

“Come in.”

As Miriam answered, the door opened to reveal Grace, who bowed.

“Is something the matter?”

“Ophelia-sama, Talcott-sama, and Cindy-sama have also expressed a wish to stay the night.”

“Hmm. We have spare rooms, so I don’t see why not.”

“After their baths, they mentioned wanting to gather in Alfred-sama’s room for a card tournament… What would you like to do?”

“I’ll join. What about you, Miriam-san?”

“I’d be delighted to, if I may.”

Miriam smiled.

“Cecilia, why don’t you join us too? It’s nighttime, so your workload should be lighter.”

“Is that alright?”

“You worked hard during the banquet as well. Please invite Mihaela-san too. The other servants are probably taking breaks in shifts.”

“Thank you. I believe Mihaela-sama would be pleased.”

Cecilia nodded happily.

“Then—I’ll finish up the remaining tasks so I can join you all as soon as possible.”

With those words and a bow, she left the room.

Grace watched Cecilia depart with a smile.

“In that case, I’ll prepare some tea.”

Right. It looked like we’d be up quite late tonight. Let’s all enjoy a relaxing game of cards together.

+++

# **197 – Interlude: Battle of the Abandoned Capital**

“…The Chamber of Keys has been occupied?”

“Yes. It seems they grew impatient waiting for Gardinis to return…”

“Fools.”

Valros spat out the words upon hearing Zaradi’s report.

Gardinis’s trusted followers had likely intended to act only after Gardinis returned with results. But no matter how long they waited, Gardinis himself never appeared. Meanwhile, they and their faction were under surveillance by Valros and Zaradi.

So was this reckless move an expression of loyalty to Gardinis, or fear of their master? They could no longer sit idle and wait… but this was exactly what Valros had feared.

He had suspected they might attack the last Sacred Tree Garden under Mustra’s management and take the Seal hostage. An assault on the Sacred Trees would be considered a breach of contract, and Valros wanted to avoid rendering all the time spent on the seal’s liberation meaningless.

Thus, he had gathered allies with aligned interests and some degree of trust to guard the Sacred Tree Garden… but now this.

“So, the Chamber of Keys.”

It was a good place for a siege. They probably calculated that even if fighting broke out, Valros wouldn’t be able to unleash his full power for fear of destroying the chamber.

“Clever little rats.”

As Valros stood, Zaradi followed.

“What shall we do?”

“What else but crush them?”

“Ha.”

Zaradi grinned at Valros’s words.

Leaving the chamber, they headed for the Chamber of Keys. Walking through Beriondora’s corridor, they found Mustra leaning against the wall with a smile.

“I heard. The Chamber of Keys has been occupied, it seems.”

She must have come out from the Sacred Tree Garden after hearing the news. The side passage led to the corridor heading to Mustra’s assigned garden.

“Indeed. I’m going to crush them now.”

“Oh my. How dreadful.”

Mustra’s expression broke into a wider smile at Valros’s menacing words.

“How goes your progress?”

“A bit more, I’d say. But in your plans, won’t you need the Chamber of Keys as well?”

“That depends. At worst, I don’t mind if it’s destroyed.”

“I see. Lord Zaradi, then?”

“Precisely. I’ve made other arrangements too.”

As Valros tried to pass by, Mustra spoke up.

“Shall I assist? Lord Zaradi excels at defense. If there’s something more important than the Chamber of Keys, it would be more fitting for him to guard near the Sacred Tree Garden.”

After saying this, Mustra laughed. Valros frowned suspiciously but shrugged and replied.

“…Fine. Zaradi, you heard?”

“Yes… May fortune favor you.”

Zaradi bowed and walked toward the passage connecting to the Sacred Tree Garden.

Valros and Mustra proceeded to the Chamber of Keys without further words.

Passing through the corridor lined with stone pillars, they soon arrived before a massive black stone gate.

Before the stone gate, a group of Demons awaited Valros and his companion. They seemed to have formed multiple defensive layers—these were the ones who had been waiting for a chance to strike Valros down.

“Valros is here! Mustra is with him!”

As one Demon called out, Gardinis’s trusted follower Azurabelg emerged from deep within the Chamber of Keys and shouted.

“Halt right there!”

Valros narrowed his eyes and bared his fangs in a grin.

“Gardinis’s schemes are worthless if the master himself doesn’t return.”

“Silence! How could our lord lose to mere humans! Do you even understand the situation!? We have this many supporters! With the Chamber of Keys at our backs, the terrain favors us! Hand over the keys quietly and surrender your authority—”

Azurabelg’s words were cut short. A black flash, casually released from Valros’s hand, carved a crack into the stone gate.

Azurabelg stared at Valros in stunned disbelief.

“Why… Do you know why we kept you under surveillance while letting you move freely?”

Saying this, Valros widened his eyes and bared his fangs. It was a grin like that of a beast in human form. Though called a Demon unlike other Demons, his smile embodied the savagery of their kind, sending a shudder through the Demon ranks.

“It was to let those who resent me but don’t belong to Gardinis’s faction gather together. I thought it’d be better to squeeze out the pus all at once. I assumed even if you feigned loyalty, as Demons you’d eventually bare your fangs. But now that you have, don’t think I’ll go easy on you?”

Azurabelg was well aware they were being watched.

It was precisely because their master was absent and they were under surveillance that they feared both purges and rebellion. Even among their own ranks were Demons skilled in combat but unrelated to those Valros had gathered… They followed Gardinis, but whether Azurabelg could control them in the long run was doubtful. In other words—in Gardinis’s continued absence, Azurabelg’s tension had snapped first.

That’s why he had executed the plan meant to be activated only upon Gardinis’s return.

“So it ends as a purge for demonstration and unity. A pity.”

As Valros crouched, he charged forward with speed that left no trace.

The first to be touched was a Demon in the front line.

“Val—”

A Palm Strike that slammed upward into the abdomen. The struck Demon was sent flying through the corridor’s ceiling like a twig caught in a storm, tumbling through the air. In its abdomen swirled a coiling Miasma. By some power, when Valros clenched the fist he raised overhead, a huge hole was torn through the Demon’s stomach in response.

“Guhah!?”

“Eek!”

A hand chop. What appeared to be a casually released strike sliced a Demon in half clean through the torso, ignoring its Miasma Barrier. Grabbing a nearby stunned Demon, he literally crushed it.

“Impossible!?”

Azurabelg stared wide-eyed.

That Demon had claimed to excel at deploying barriers. He’d positioned it at the front precisely because it was suited for sieges and buying time. Yet it was slaughtered in a single blow—.

No matter how you looked at it, this attack power was abnormal. If Valros had formed a Miasma Blade, cutting through the barrier would be understandable. But Valros merely had a thin mist-like Miasma wrapped around one hand. The scene surpassed Azurabelg’s common sense, and he couldn’t comprehend it.

Or perhaps this was Valros’s ability—the power of a Transcendent, granted only to high-ranking Demons like Gardinis, Luceriage, and Zevion.

In battles between Demons, there were no Blessings or cycles to reduce Miasma attributes. It became a contest of raw strength. He understood that, but even so, this—.

“You bastard!”

Demons who had formed Miasma Blades rushed at Valros. Valros’s body swayed lightly. His movements clearly suggested rigorous training.

The three Demons who had swung their blades were stunned as Valros slipped through without their swords even meeting. And by then, it was all over.

Face, over the heart, and the medulla oblongata. Coiling there was darkness—the Miasma Valros left behind upon contact as he slipped through.

Valros silently clenched his hand. Centered on the darkness he left, the Demons’ respective body parts were gouged out as if scooped away. Belatedly, the bodies of the slain Demons turned to dust.

“Eek! Eeeek!”

Whether fear had overcome them at the sight, some Demons tried to flee past Valros. Valros glanced at them as if looking at something boring but silently let them go. He knew they couldn’t escape even without him lifting a hand.

“My, my. Where do you think you’re going?”

Waiting for them was a laughing Demon—Mustra.

Her movements, different from Valros’s, were languid. From her body rose an unfathomable Miasma.

“Move!”

A panicked Demon fired a Miasma Bullet at Mustra. Mustra also fired a Miasma Bullet in response, crossing her arms to defend. As the Miasma Bullet struck, another Demon leaped out from behind the first and thrust a Miasma Blade toward Mustra’s heart. Mustra—didn’t even try to avoid it.

The Miasma Blade sank deep. Feeling the impact, the Demon grinned, sensing a Critical hit.

A scream came from the Demon behind who had blocked the Miasma Bullet. Turning to see what happened, he witnessed something unbelievable.

“Uwaaah!? My arm, my arm!?”

As if melting candy craft. The Demon’s right and left arms had fused together in their crossed position.

“Haha, too bad. Not bad for an impromptu effort.”

This can’t be, thought the Demon who had thrust the blade, realizing his grin had twisted. Returning his gaze, he saw Mustra still smiling, the blade piercing her heart. Happily. Delightedly.

Yes, she was pleased. Her eyes, distorted with joy, were scrutinizing how to play with him, licking her lips in anticipation.

Miasma attributes. Distance. Mortal peril. A mad grin. Releasing the Miasma Blade, he tried to retreat. But he couldn’t escape. Where had the attack come from? He was impaled from all directions by something like black spears.

“Once in a while, the Fear of one’s own kind isn’t so bad, is it?”

Saying this, she shrugged and laughed. The remaining Demons were speechless.

Abilities that made even other Demons find them utterly horrifying. The one that melted arms and the one that unleashed a spear formation from all sides. Even though they had witnessed everything, they couldn’t grasp the true nature of her Miasma attributes.

If Valros was a Demon embodying storm-like brutality, then Mustra was a Demon who seemed to personify another aspect of Demonkind. Whether they stayed or advanced, it was hell.

“F-fire!”

The Demons unleashed a volley of Miasma Bullets at Valros. But the moment they touched Valros’s Miasma, they were deflected in random directions, streaming away behind him.

Around Valros, dark Miasma floated as a sphere, spinning rapidly around him. A black flash from his raised hand. Simultaneously, from the sphere, a dark Lightning Strike pierced the spot illuminated by the flash.

“Are you insane!? Do you know what’s behind us…!?”

“A bit regrettable, but I don’t mind if it’s lost. It’s not even worth comparing to the Sacred Tree Garden.”

Valros spoke as if it were nothing.

Sweeping. Mowing down. The formed ranks. The Demons. Shattered and blown away.

“You bastard…! You bastard, bastard, baaaaastard!!”

Enraged, Azurabelg charged at Valros while transforming his body’s shape. His form became that of a streamlined quadruped beast. His speed was on par with Valros’s earlier charge. A silver shadow flashed.

“Oh?”

Valros tilted his head slightly, letting out what sounded like his first impressed murmur. A small cut on his cheek. Azurabelg, having turned Miasma into a thin blade and reached top speed from the initial burst, had slashed at him as they passed. His form was like a meteor. Using the lined stone pillars as footholds, he bounced at high speed and charged from Valros’s diagonal rear.

“Die—!”

“Too naive.”

Along with a sense of incongruity, Azurabelg this time lost his words completely.

Valros had stopped the Miasma Blade thrust from his diagonal rear with just two fingers.

“That’s—”

Faster than he could say “impossible,” Azurabelg felt his body being pulled and then slammed back-first into the ground.

The sheer force of it. The floor cratered, cracks radiating out from the impact.

“Guhah!”

“Farewell.”

Writhing from the shock and intense pain, Azurabelg looked up. Above Valros’s raised palm was a pitch-black sphere emitting black sparks—.

“—My, my. How anticlimactic.”

Mustra delivered the Finishing Blow to the last one begging for mercy, then shook her shoulders laughing.

The corridor to the Chamber of Keys. And inside the Chamber itself, none of the insurgents survived. They had been massacred by just two Demons—only the wounded guards remained, staring blankly at Valros and Mustra.

Though extraordinary traces of destruction remained in the corridor, because it was a battle between Demons, not even corpses were left behind.

“You seem to be enjoying yourself.”

“Yes. Without things like this, I just can’t get into proper form. Is the Chamber of Keys intact?”

Valros looked around at the Altar and its surroundings within the Chamber before answering.

“Some damage. It’ll take a little time to repair, but… it should be manageable.”

“That’s a relief. If acquiring the keys had been for nothing, she would be angry too, wouldn’t she?”

At Mustra’s words, Valros gave a small wry smile.

“Probably. He’s free now too. Regarding the Miasma Orb I used to break the seal, I hear he’ll deliver it to Termwills.”

“I see. Then, as planned.”

“I told him to avoid combat. I wonder how that will go.”

“…Hmm. So the old man Gardinis actually lost, did he?”

“That’s how it looks. If he’s been defeated after Zevion and Luceriage… there’s no room for doubt anymore.”

“Doubt about what?”

In response to Mustra’s query, Valros narrowed his eyes and answered.

“What’s in Termwills is a kind of monster.”

+++

# **198 – Fiery Heat Fortress**

Between dealing with matters involving the Thieves Guild and Sheila’s past, preparing the shop, the opening celebration banquet with everyone staying over, the card tournament, and various other events… I couldn’t spend all my time on town activities.

Especially when it came to the Labyrinth’s Last Guardian and matters involving Demons, we needed to further strengthen our combat capabilities. For example, through training and Labyrinth Exploration—or deciphering the code in Mother’s notes.

“Absorbing magical power from the environment… Hmm.”

“Is that Lady Lisa’s notes?”

Grace, who had brought me tea, asked about the murmur I’d let slip while researching with Mother’s notes at the desk in the master bedroom.

“Yes. It also contained information about Mother’s constitution.”

Regarding Mother’s constitution—it seemed her magical aptitude was closer to the original essence of magical power itself rather than that of a healing sorcerer.

If healing sorcerers suffer from their life force dissolving into magical power and weakening, Mother’s case suggested her magical power might be dissipating into the natural environment.

If that were true, she should have experienced weakening due to magical power depletion, but Mother’s symptoms weren’t that severe. The reason she didn’t deteriorate further seemed to be that her unique magical aptitude actually allowed her to manipulate magical power to absorb it from the natural environment.

However, after absorbing environmental magical power into her body, she needed to neutralize the excess. Monsters handle this role with the magic stones inside their bodies. Since she lacked that, the notes hypothesized this might have been why she frequently fell ill.

“Is that so… Lady Lisa…”

At my explanation, Grace touched her ring and showed a slightly lonely expression.

“I keep thinking if only I could have used Circulating Ki back then.”

“Please don’t blame yourself. I… no, everyone else has also received so much from Theo and been supported by him.”

“Hmm…”

I’m being supported too. I nodded at Grace and returned her smile.

Mother… seemed to have suppressed her own constitution with a Cursed Tool that sealed her characteristics… but it didn’t change the fundamental nature of her magical power, and while the dissipation slowed, it never completely stopped. Grace is the same. The backlash of her bloodsucking impulse doesn’t disappear either, requiring her to balance it out somewhere. The ring is by no means a perfect solution.

In Grace’s case, being with me can solve the problem, but Mother needed to occasionally remove the ring and perform the essential task of absorbing magical power—in other words, she needed to come up for air. That’s why she could never completely escape poor health.

Based on the hypothesis—methods for improving her own constitution were also recorded.

This was still a work in progress, with the theory left unfinished… Essentially, it was about whether she could create a spell formula to freely absorb and handle magical power from the surroundings by neutralizing it through the spell formula. In other words, she was probably thinking about reinforcing her own constitution with a spell formula. Rosetta’s theory that Circulating Ki could compensate for it was also correct, but unfortunately, it had been lost in our current generation.

“…Let’s stop here for today.”

“Yes. Tomorrow is the Blazing Fortress, correct?”

“Right. Let’s rest well and prepare for tomorrow.”

After continuing the decryption for a while—I emptied my teacup and stretched deeply.

Then I thought:

…Couldn’t I aim to complete this spell formula with my own hands?

It would be like inheriting Mother’s research. Completing unfinished work. It should definitely be something worth learning for me too.

The next day—. When we transferred with Claudia’s assistance from the Labyrinth entrance’s stone monument, we found ourselves in a scorching world.

The entire ceiling of the massive cavern was covered with red-hot crystal-like ore protruding downward. Not just the ceiling either. It jutted out from various places in the stone pavement, scattering intense heat around.

“So this is the Blazing Fortress—”

Ashley looked up at the massive structure towering in the distance and murmured.

Yes. It was a castle. A fortress with high stone walls glowing red and numerous spires. A location situated quite deep within the Labyrinth. The enemies are strong, the terrain is highly dangerous, making it a considerably high-difficulty area. While taking as much safety margin as possible, we aimed to gain combat experience here and further strengthen our fighting capabilities. Considering the example of the Great Corruption Lake, this area might become the main battlefield during a Demon battle. Gaining experience to handle that wouldn’t be wasted.

“Are you okay, Lavigne? What about everyone?”

Defense against the blazing heat through fire rat pelts. Blocking the heat and cooling with Wind Magic and Water Magic. We’d taken all conceivable countermeasures, but how effective were they?

“Lavigne… seems to be fine.”

“I’m okay too.”

“Same here.”

Everyone nodded. When my eyes met Marlene’s, she nodded with a serious expression.

“Good… Well then, I guess we start by breaking through that castle gate.”

The long stone-paved slope continued endlessly. Beyond it, we could see the massive castle gate—but annoyingly, we couldn’t infiltrate the fortress interior without first conquering those castle walls.

“Can’t we fly over those walls from above?”

Sheila asked.

Yeah. Someone in BFO thought of that too. As for how that turned out… well, it was pretty disastrous.

“The crystals on the ceiling emit considerable heat, and there’s a barrier covering the entire upper airspace. We can manage to some extent, but it’s better not to gain too much altitude. If we get pinned down, we’ll be sniped with bows. Even if we enter the castle interior, the spires don’t have anything resembling windows, so we’d eventually need to proceed through the inside anyway.”

“I see…”

Just having Aerial Combat Gear is quite useful even if we can’t take the high-altitude approach. Not having to worry about falling from heights is particularly convenient.

That said, regarding the castle gate, we have no choice but to charge straight at it.

“There’s a stone monument past the castle gate. Today is just reconnaissance, but let’s at least reach that point.”

“Understood.”

“Coming.”

The road leading to the castle gate is a single path. The visibility is good, with abysses on both sides of the slope. No detours either. Having spotted us, the Living Armors formed ranks and attacked. There were guard posts at various points along the slope, and they were attacking from there.

The castle gate of the Blazing Fortress. The Living Armors’ military-like movements made it tough, and when I first came here, I had to form a Raid Party to break through—.

“Advance.”

I had the Golems form ranks and spear formations to advance forward. However, simply thrusting spears at hollow Living Armors would be meaningless. That’s why the Golems’ ranks were equipped with sasumata—tools for restraining. And the Golems’ material was earth, making the enemy’s weapons ineffective against them too.

Therefore, the tactic was to advance regardless while engaging. Restraining the Living Armors with sasumata, or having the earth bodies absorb their armor to immobilize them. And then—.

“There we go.”

An axe thrown by Grace, who had jumped, flew at tremendous speed. The super-heavyweight axe penetrated the Living Armor’s torso like paper.

Irmhild’s bow and arrows were also effective. Seraphina, perched on Irmhild’s shoulder, amplified and fired Light Arrows imbued with Cursed Melody. This seemed to have quite a fatal effect on Living Armors, as those hit would jerk violently and cease functioning.

When Sheila, who had circled around, kicked off a Living Armor’s helmet from the air, the headless Living Armor panicked, dropped its weapon, and reached for its head. That’s when the Golems restrained it. The adhesive nets also seemed to be functioning very effectively.

Against the archers from high positions, Ashley and Lavigne created Ice Walls, and Marlene deployed Saucers to completely handle the situation. We climbed the slope as if expanding our territory.

“Rocks!”

Sheila’s warning.

The Living Armors were rolling blazing rock spheres down from above the slope. They must have changed tactics upon seeing the vanguard at a disadvantage. Normally, the standard approach would be to retreat to the Living Armor guard posts we had suppressed—.

“No need to avoid them. Continue advancing forward.”

I leaped over the Golems, charged Ouroboros with magical power, and swung it around. I smashed the Living Armors we were engaged with down into the abyss beside the slope, moving ahead of the front line.

Ouroboros’s roar of delight. The swelling surge of circulating magical power. Along with scattering sparks, I thrust the Dragon Staff into the rolling boulder. Transmitting impact from a single point to crush the rock while simultaneously using Levitation and Fire Magic together. I rebounded the blast back toward the reinforcing Living Armors trying to attack along with the rocks. The Living Armor ranks hit by the scatter shot were thrown into disarray.

“Charge in!”

At my command, Grace and the others kicked off their Shields and moved forward. Marlene also ran up at high speed alongside Dullahan. They scattered the Living Armors, raced up the slope—and advanced to the open area before the castle gate.

“Seal it!”

“Yes!”

Once all our comrades had rushed in, Ashley and Lavigne created Ice Walls on the path connecting the slope to the plaza. This was to prevent Living Armor reinforcements from coming from the various guard posts in the rear. These guys here would calmly attempt first-time-killer tactics like leaving surplus combat forces to pincer attack us in the plaza.

It’s a challenging area indeed. Ashley constructed a Defense Field from her Magic Tool, forming a defensive formation.

From the guard post beside the plaza emerged a group of Living Armor upper species, Heavy Armors. The front gate opened, and from beyond it appeared a Giant wielding a spiked iron ball and a Flame Demon clad in armor.

They’re the ones called Sub-Guardian level—monsters stationed in specific locations. Was the Blazing Fortress also created with the purpose of being conquered? By defeating these guys, we can open the castle gate.

“I’ll handle the burning one.”

“Then I’ll take the Giant.”

I stepped forward alongside Grace. Quite an enthusiastic welcome.

“Signal if anything happens.”

“Hmm.”

Claudia is always ready to respond for retreat, so our escape route is secured… but if we can’t break through here, it’s pointless. Well then, let the battle begin.

+++

# **199 – Demons and Giants**

Though they’re called Sub-Guardian class… given how they’re positioned like bosses in the lower levels, the Flame Demon would likely be a higher-level opponent than the true Guardians like the Sword Boar or Captain Nautilus. It’s a classic type that handles both close and long range with no openings. Defeating it truly tests one’s raw ability.

But there’s no need to observe. I charge straight toward the Flame Demon.

To intercept me, a flaming greatsword swings upward from below. I deploy my Shield. While defending, I leap as if riding the momentum of the greatsword. Soaring over the Flame Demon’s head, I kick off the air faster than it can turn around, tracing a straight trajectory.

Ouroboros’s strike leaves a pale blue glow in the air. The Flame Demon barely avoids it by bending its body. As the demon swings its left hand upward, a massive pillar of fire rises, attempting to burn me.

Even wearing the Fire Rat cloak, there are gaps. If engulfed by the flames as is, taking damage would be unavoidable.

So, just like with Zevion—I create a layer of air to block the heat. Breaking through the fire pillar, I charge at the Flame Demon, which blocks my strike with its greatsword. The Dragon Staff and greatsword clash, scattering sparks.

A roar and scorching wind. Wings of raging flames spread from its back. We ascend while locked in a stalemate.

Something log-like approaches from the side. The Flame Demon’s tail. Nemea’s arm shoots out from a gap in the cloak to intercept.

We’re both knocked back. Instantly reversing, we cross paths countless times in the air, leaving trails of fire and magical light. Each time, shockwaves run through us, and Spark Light scatters.

An exchange of strikes and slash attacks. Tail and claws. Blast waves and impacts. I bend the spreading fiery Breath with Flame Absorb and strike down.

Its reaction speed is extraordinary. I don’t know its mental structure, but it shows no agitation. Even the irregular movements and increased attacks from using Capella and Nemea are accepted and countered as they are.

Activate Mirage Body. Slipping past the greatsword and tail, I drive a Dragon Staff strike into its flank, but it shows no reaction and immediately brings the greatsword down from a high stance. I deflect with the Dragon Staff while spinning sideways and ascending. I slam the Dragon Staff straight into its face, but it responds by swinging its head as if brandishing its horns to parry.

Both toughness and fighting spirit are more than sufficient. Combat skills and reaction speed are both excellent. Well now—isn’t this getting interesting?

The fact that they’ve created a formation with Defense Field and Ice Wall means the Heavy Armors will find it harder to surround or suppress. Stepping into the field would hinder movement.

Thus, it seems they’ve chosen to form ranks from one direction and crush us with the weight of their armor.

Holding them back and responding are Ashley riding Lavigne’s back, Marlene hovering Saucers around herself and Dullahan, and from the rearguard, Irmhild and Seraphina in the role of finishing them off with arrows.

The thrusting spears have their momentum killed by the Defense Field, their tips swallowed by ice trees sprouting from the ground, forcibly stopping their movement.

Sweeping through that gap is a blow from a Long Mace wreathed in ice. Using Levitation in tandem, it effortlessly blows away the Heavy Armor, slamming it into the back ranks. As the formation crumbles, Dullahan tramples through. Swinging its greatsword, it sends the Heavy Armors flying upward. Counterattacks don’t reach them because the rapidly spinning Saucers deflect spears, swords, and arrows alike.

The Heavy Armors flung high into the sky are pierced one after another by Light Arrows. Even fully armed and holding shields, being blown away by Dullahan renders them useless.

“Sheila!”

Sheila’s role is offense. As the front spear-wielders collapse, at Irmhild’s word, Sheila leaps. Releasing Sticky Thread onto the ground, using the adhered spot as a pivot, she draws a large arc, breaks through the encirclement with ease, and positions herself far behind the surrounding Heavy Armors.

Her target—the Heavy Armor with a feathered decoration on its helmet. The so-called commander. Its combat ability is higher than the others, and it commands the Living Armors and Heavy Armors in this area. Conversely—taking out the commander would disrupt their coordination and movements.

“Going in.”

After flying erratically in several directions, Sheila makes her move. The commander responds. Blocking the Pearl Sword wreathed in fighting spirit with its silver straight sword, it steps in, thrusting its left-hand shield forward.

I ride the momentum. Leaping without resisting the shield’s force. Showing movement devoid of weight, she reverses in mid-air and rebounds linearly.

Sword and shield. The high-pitched clashing sounds ring out.

Interference—none enters. The Ice Wall separates Sheila and Ashley’s battlefield.

Enhanced by the Circlet’s Water Magic, Ashley’s spatial control ability is now considerable. The ice itself has also become more robust.

Approaching the commander with three-dimensional movements, she freely wields her Twin Swords. Slash attacks dance wildly as if she were performing. Movements where evasion and attack merge into one. The commander frantically tries to impose its shield advantage, but against Sheila, it only creates more blind spots for itself.

They cross blades several times. Attacks with the Pearl Sword are somewhat less effective—but Sheila’s aim isn’t brute force.

The commander’s Shield Bash. But Sheila isn’t there. Taking advantage of the absence of nearby Blazing Heat attackers, she leaves the Fire Rat cloak behind like a shed skin, disappearing, then emerging from beneath it.

Stomping at the lack of expected resistance, the commander finds Sheila already turned around, having aimed from behind with the Arachnear Ring.

The incoming iron ball is met head-on.

The Giant’s iron ball and Grace’s axe. Both are wreathed in fighting spirit. They collide with a tremendous sound. In terms of range, the Giant has the advantage. As Grace advances while batting away the iron ball, the Giant shows a sweeping motion with the chain connected to the retrieved iron ball. Fighting spirit coils around the chain too.

Even if she flew away to escape, it would likely change and pursue—but Grace shows no sign of fear facing the Giant, advancing straight forward.

The whip-like strike’s power plummets if its impact point is missed. Incredibly, she grabs the chain and steps straight forward.

The Giant roars in irritation and launches a kick. The iron greaves, wrapped in fighting spirit, hint at destructive power.

Then—Grace stops. Deploys a Shield in front. An abrupt halt. The moment the kick passes with a gust of wind, she leaps sideways still holding the chain. Fixes herself in mid-air with the Shield. The Giant’s body, still holding the chain, is pulled, flailing. Its posture breaks.

“Take this.”

The fighting spirit axe, emitting a purple gleam, is thrown. Aiming for the neck. It leans back to dodge. Regardless of the Giant’s absurd muscle density, it gouges out part of its shoulder. A leap. Closing in with cannonball-like momentum.

Roaring in agony, the Giant meets it. As if to show it could overpower at close range with bare hands, not the iron ball. It coats its fist with fighting spirit and strikes. It wears gauntlets. More than sufficient as weapons.

Grace’s actions don’t change. Interception with her axe. However, she’s not just wrapping her axe but her entire body in fighting spirit. Grace’s axe and the Giant’s fist collide violently. The Giant advances. Grace, even if knocked back, instantly reverses. A charge.

She doesn’t retreat. Doesn’t retreat. Fist and axe clash. No, collide. With an explosive sound, fighting spirit vs. fighting spirit. A head-on contest of power vs. power. Grace’s arm strength shows no disadvantage despite the mass difference.

Grace, wrapping her entire body in fighting spirit to fly, and the Giant, using fighting spirit only for attack and defense. In terms of endurance, the Giant would likely win. A prolonged battle would favor the Giant.

That’s how it should have been.

That was the old Grace. Grace, supplied with the night’s power from her dress, even smiles faintly, then unleashes further honed fighting spirit, swinging her axe.

Then, what decides victory is equipment quality. Though using fighting spirit, the Giant’s equipment is mere iron. Unable to withstand the repeated intense impacts, the Giant’s gauntlet shatters, and the axe deeply cleaves its fist.

It cries out in anguish, pulling back its fist. Grace steps in to point-blank range. It tries to grab with its uninjured arm. She slams the axe into its palm, and Grace performs a Form Shift. The attack hidden by her body’s shadow was a complete blind spot for the Giant. Additionally, she activates a phantom axe to prevent reading her trajectory.

Right through the Giant’s iron helmet visor—its face—its eyes are sliced clean across. The projected slash attack from fighting spirit completely robs it of vision.

“Grace!”

Sheila calls. Sheila’s figure has captured the commander in a sticky web. Ashley’s controlled ice creates a path like a rail from the commander to the Giant. Grace discerns the intent, kicks off her Shield, and lands on the ground.

She slams her axe into the Giant’s wide-open heel as it writhes, holding its face. Like felling a giant tree, the Giant’s body sways. Ashley, running in with Lavigne, casts Levitation on the commander. Sheila swings the sticky web with centrifugal force, sliding the commander along the ice rail—.

“Haaah!”

Grace grabs the Giant’s leg with both hands—and with a sharp cry, using a shoulder throw motion, hurls it. Right onto the sliding commander.

The flame-wreathed greatsword. The radiating heat waves. But it’s different from with Zevion. Countermeasures against flames are fully in place. Therefore—exchanging blows at breath-taking distance, where our weapons reflect each other, works to my advantage. The range where it can fully utilize its weapon’s properties—inside that is my distance. Nemea, clad in ice armor from Water Magic, firmly grabs the Flame Demon’s tail with her claws, not allowing escape.

Even so, the Flame Demon persists. Clashing staff and greatsword repeatedly, baring fangs, thrusting sharp claws. The scorching wind grazing my cheek. Ringing high-pitched sounds as we dance through the air, crossing blades.

Reversing heaven and earth, switching offense and defense. We dance, incidentally mowing down the archers stationed atop the castle walls.

A rising strike with the pommel. Simultaneously, a Knee Strike to divert attention from the high stance. I intercept the high stance with my Shield, the low stance with Capella’s headbutt. Receiving the attack with my Shield while releasing an impact strike.

The Flame Demon pulls back its greatsword but opens its maw wide and unleashes a Breath. The fire Breath’s effect is weak. It knows this too, combining Breath with Earth Magic to shoot scattered pellets of scorched stone.

Still, the aim to obscure vision with flames remains unchanged.

Deploy Shield in all directions for detection. A sharp claw thrust from diagonally below, aiming for my flank. I twist my body to evade, and without even turning around, thrust backward with Ouroboros.

Even after taking an impact strike to the head, it swings its greatsword back. A slash attack from a broken posture. I deploy my Shield diagonally, deflecting it greatly.

Impressive fighting spirit, but that depends on time and place. I perform another Form Shift, place my hand on its abdomen, deliver an impact strike, and immediately follow with a slap from Ouroboros.

“Grooargh!”

The Flame Demon still doesn’t retreat. Ignoring damage, it flaps its wings, rapidly ascending as if to push me away. To prevent escape, it deliberately entangles its tail with Nemea, pressing me from both sides with its arms through my Shield, adopting a reckless stance abandoning defense.

Its aim—to smash me into the Barrier, perhaps—.

Magic Circle deployment. The Flame Demon’s eyes widen at its scale. Still, it doesn’t stop ascending. Thinking that at this distance, it could entrap me in its own magic depending on the spell type. If it’s Great Magic, indeed. That assessment is both correct and mistaken. Both it and I laugh.

“But that too is futile.”

My Spell Formula completes faster than I’m slammed into the Barrier. Simultaneously, impact comes. I defend my back with my Shield just before crashing into the castle wall, using Wind Magic to soften the collision impact.

Using teleportation, I moved along with the Flame Demon. Thrusting the Dragon Staff into the Flame Demon’s wide-open mouth before it can comprehend. Ouroboros growls as if laughing.

“Pierce!”

Water Magic 5th Tier Icicle Blade. A magic that creates a sharp ice greatsword.

The ice sword deployed from Ouroboros’s tip penetrates the Flame Demon’s head. Breaking free from the slackened Flame Demon’s grasp, I spin vertically while sweeping. The ice greatsword draws a silver arc, and the Flame Demon, its head vertically split in two behind me, plummets downward.

Thank you for reading my work.

Reports of typos or missing characters, impressions, bookmarks, ratings, PVs, etc., are always a great encouragement for my writing.

Thanks to you, I’ve reached chapter 200. I express my gratitude here.

I’ve posted a brief introduction article for characters from chapters 101 to 150 in the activity report.

As usual, to prevent spoilers, it contains minimal information, but I hope you find it useful.

Also, since there was a previous comment wanting to know the characters’ appearances,

though brief, I’ve posted starting with party members and some characters around the royal family.

# **200 – The Daughter of the Previous Generation**

“Is everyone injured?”

“We’re fine on our end.”

After dealing with the Flame Demon, the Giant, and the commander, then mopping up the rest, the situation had calmed down somewhat.

No one seemed particularly injured. Well, since monsters like Bomb Rocks appeared inside the castle, the Armors probably weren’t much of a threat anyway.

The deactivated Living Armors and Heavy Armors could either have their Magic Stones extracted or be collected as-is for armor or metal materials. Irmhild’s arrows had left the original forms of the Living Armors largely intact… They’d likely fetch a good price, which was quite fortunate.

The Giant and Flame Demon had their Magic Stones extracted. These turned out to be quite high-quality stones. I’d have to think about how to use them later.

…And so, after finishing collecting our spoils, we returned via the stone monument located just past the castle gate.

“…The Blazing Fortress? Does this mean you defeated the gatekeepers?”

Receptionist Heather’s eyes widened as she looked over the arranged trophies.

“Essentially, yes. But those guys eventually respawn even after being defeated, right?”

“That should be the case. The records are quite old, but they do mention revivals.”

In BFO, it was based on moon phases. In reality now, it seems they won’t revive for a while… but eventually they will. Having Flame Demons and Giants that respawn for practical combat training each time isn’t such a bad idea either.

“They say it’s the Blazing Fortress…”

“Heard they took down the gatekeepers. Should we give it a try?”

“Don’t be stupid. First of all, reaching the lower levels is practically impossible. And even getting to the castle gate is supposed to be pretty dangerous, from what I hear.”

“Yeah. That kid… isn’t that the one who built the theater recently?”

“Looks can be deceiving, as they say.”

“That’s it. She must be a magician who’s trained for hundreds of years.”

“I see…”

…Ah. Rumors are spreading on their own and they’re reaching strange conclusions, but I’ll pretend I didn’t hear that. Heather wore a wry smile at the surrounding gossip.

“Anyway, it’s been a very long time since we’ve had a party capable of exploring inside the fortress, so the Guild has high expectations for your spoils. But please be careful not to get injured.”

“I’ll be careful.”

“You’ve got a lot on your plate too, Theo-kun.”

“Absolutely.”

When I told Alfred, who had come to visit, about what happened at the Guild, he gave me a wry smile—as expected, or rather, just as I anticipated.

“So, this is that Magic Stone?”

“Yes. But… this stone already has an element attached from the start.”

The Flame Demon’s Magic Stone placed on the counter in the recreation room felt warm to the touch. Among high-quality Magic Stones, some like this with attached elements appear. They lack versatility but can be quite powerful in their specialized areas.

“Have you decided how to use it?”

“Not yet. I’m thinking about uses for both this and the Giant’s Magic Stone, but haven’t decided.”

While bringing this to the workshop would be fine, I’m unsure how to utilize it. With quality this good, it could be used for large-scale magic tools, or perhaps I should challenge myself to create something entirely new.
