While Alfred and I were discussing various potential uses, Cecilia appeared in the recreation room.

“Master. Lady Isabella is here to see you.”

“A guest? Don’t mind me, you should go.”

“…Understood. I’ll head to the reception room immediately. Could you call Sheila for me too?”

“Certainly.”

Cecilia bowed slightly and left.

“Hmm. Sorry about this.”

“Don’t worry about it. I’m just here to hang out anyway.”

Alfred smiled and glanced toward the billiards table. He’d really taken a liking to it.

“If you like it that much, should I put one in the workshop too?”

“I’d appreciate that, but having too many distractions could be problematic… Eventually, I’ll be able to play at the Royal Castle too, so I should keep it moderate.”

Saying this, Alfred began playing billiards with the Labyrinth Village residents who were on break.

When I headed to the reception room with Sheila, Isabella and another person were there.

Let’s see… I feel like I’ve seen her somewhere before… Ah, she was the receptionist at the brothel, right?

“Thank you for your generous treatment of people like us despite this sudden visit. This is Dorothy.”

“My apologies for not introducing myself the other day. I’m Dorothy.”

As soon as Isabella saw me, she bowed her head along with Dorothy, the receptionist beside her. Isabella’s appearance had changed again from when I last saw her. Unlike her workplace dress or the mobility-focused Thieves Guild outfit, both she and Dorothy wore chic, subdued formal clothing. Her speech was also much more formal now…

“Not at all. I should apologize for keeping you waiting. I’m Theodore Gartner. This is Sheila.”

Saying this, I sat down with Sheila. A servant immediately brought us tea.

“I came today regarding the matter from the other day.”

“Isabella-san. I’ll take it from here.”

Dorothy took over from Isabella, then bowed her head while kneeling on one knee.

“Thank you for avenging my father.”

So it’s about the Thieves Guild incident. Since Isabella came along too, she must be the previous leader’s daughter. Probably, while dealing with Randolph’s aftermath in connection with the Thieves Guild, information must have leaked from somewhere.

“Please raise your head. That was part of my job as well.”

“Even so. After my father passed away, Isabella-san took me in… I’ve been in her care but haven’t been able to repay her at all. But… no. Precisely because of that, I cannot forget the kindness I’ve received. I may not be capable of much, but if there’s anything I can do to repay you…”

At Dorothy’s words, Isabella smiled slightly with a somewhat troubled expression. Working as a receptionist at the brothel was probably… Dorothy’s own idea.

“I’ve certainly received your words.”

“Yes…”

“Well, as I said earlier, it was part of my job. From my position, I might occasionally ask for cooperation through acquaintances. That’s about all I can say. Besides, I don’t particularly like heavy debts.”

I vaguely implied that I might use her as an information source for the Thieves Guild in the future.

I paused there and glanced at Sheila. She nodded slightly and took over the conversation.

“Randolph was my enemy too.”

“Isabella-san told me.”

Dorothy smiled wryly with a somewhat lonely expression.

“My parents and Dorothy’s father… apparently knew each other through work, but we’re meeting for the first time. So…”

Sheila extended her right hand and said,

“I’d be happy if Dorothy would be my friend.”

“I-I’d be delighted if you’d have me…!”

Dorothy took Sheila’s hand and stood up.

Friends, huh… Well, I think that’s fine.

“Since we have the opportunity, why don’t you go play together in the recreation room for a while?”

“Mm. Dorothy, want to come with me?”

“Eh, um?”

“You should go.”

Seen off by me and Isabella, the two left.

Even though they have deep connections to the underworld… both Isabella and Dorothy are in positions of influence in the town. Since they operate with a sense of duty and human feelings, if the Thieves Guild is favorable toward the friendly monsters, that should be something I welcome.

“Is the Guild doing alright?”

“I’m managing to organize the remaining members. I heard from some of those captured by Randolph… Well, that’s how I learned what Randolph did to the previous leader.”

“…I see.”

So there were Thieves Guild members among those imprisoned in Randolph’s mansion.

“Like the young lady, I also consider this an unrepayable debt… but considering the Ambassador’s position, I thought it might be troublesome if people like us showed up in large numbers. Still, a debt is a debt. I had to convey my gratitude.”

“So you came as individuals rather than representing the Guild?”

“Yes. I also want to tell you that from now on, we will be on the Ambassador’s side. Given your position, you probably can’t announce it publicly, but if anything happens, we’ll come running anytime.”

“I’ll remember that.”

When I answered, Isabella nodded quietly.

“Well… that’s enough about that. Isabella-san, why don’t you stop by the recreation room too?”

At my words, Isabella blinked in surprise.

+++

# **201 – Evil Weed and Home Garden**

After inviting the two to the entertainment room, we conquered all the games there together with Sheila, Alfred, and the residents of Labyrinth Village.

Isabella and Dorothy quickly became friendly with the Labyrinth Village residents too. Their good interpersonal skills probably came from backgrounds involving plenty of people with complicated circumstances around the Thieves Guild and brothels.

“Are you performing at that theater?”

“Only on full moon nights.”

As for Dorothy, she was enthusiastically discussing songs and musical instruments with Sheila and Irmhild. She seemed to be having quite a good time. Isabella watched Dorothy and Sheila with an affectionate gaze before turning to me.

“Speaking of which… the Ambassador opened a shop in the Eastern District, didn’t you? Are you planning to sell these there?”

“Yes. That’s the plan.”

“In that case… I’d like to place an order too, if that’s alright? Well, it’s partly because I personally like them, but—”

According to Isabella… it seems that having casual games like cards and darts would be perfect for brothels.

“That would be very helpful. The shop has only just opened, after all.”

I suppose this counts as developing sales channels. There’s no reason for me to refuse.

Isabella herself had become quite absorbed in darts too. Sheila had good control, but Isabella seemed to quickly grasp the technique as well. Being an executive of the Thieves Guild, this was probably her area of expertise.

“I’m not familiar with this drink—but I suspect there might be copycats for these games. Should we keep an eye out for those dealing in shoddy imitations?”

Isabella murmured something like that. It sounded like she was talking about cracking down on pirated versions.

“No, that won’t be necessary. The artisans from the Commerce Guild seem to be thoroughly keeping the information confidential, and if someone were to make them, they’d have to learn by watching and imitate, right? Unless it’s particularly malicious, I think that’s fine.”

We have the know-how first, and we’re getting proper cooperation from artisans through the Commerce Guild. If the quality differs, that’s where the added value of our logo will come into play. I have no intention of lagging behind anyone.

“Then I’ll inform you if I think it’s malicious.”

“Understood.”

I smiled wryly. She’s really quite dutiful.

“How’s Harvesta doing?”

At night—I was conducting experiments and observations on Evil Weed’s Harvesta in the Japanese-style room’s low table, watching carefully with my hands on the edge of the table alongside Marlene and Seraphina, when Ashley asked.

“Yeah. It’s pretty interesting.”

“Harvesta is amazing!”

We were bringing various types of insects we’d caught in insect cages close to Harvesta to observe the reactions…

Creatures like earthworms that help with soil improvement were left alone, but insects that eat leaves were either actively tried to be eaten like carnivorous plants or shown gestures of being chased away with leaves.

What’s particularly interesting is that Harvesta seems to ignore insects like bees that help with pollination, or beneficial insects that prey on pests.

Well, that’s about it. I released the captured insects out the window, marking the end of the experiment for now.

“It doesn’t seem to just be picky about what it likes and dislikes.”

“Yeah. I think it properly judges whether insects are beneficial to it or not. For example, this insect eats other insects, so for Harvesta it’s neutral but not an enemy.”

“Harvesta seems quite clever.”

“How about the potted plants outside?”

When Grace asked following Claudia’s words, Ashley answered.

“Those too… when grown together with Evil Weed, the growth speed is completely different.”

Hmm… This definitely seems worth conducting field tests.

“It would be good to try growing them together with some crops.”

“I see. Theodore is thinking about whether it can be used in farming methods.”

I nodded at Claudia’s words.

“That’s further down the line. For now, we need to keep it on a smaller scale and verify safety.”

“Labyrinth Village has various crop seeds and seedlings.”

“Perfect timing. If we can get some, let’s make a garden next to the storage shed.”

“If it comes to larger scale, I think the Barony of Silun could cooperate too.”

“Yeah. That would be helpful.”

“If the territory’s harvest increases, that would be wonderful.”

Saying that, Ashley smiled.

Ashley’s territory is a grain-producing region. Considering that Ashley and I are engaged, if farming methods using Evil Weed are established, it would probably be among the first to adopt them.

The current test scale is like a home garden, but I’d like to conduct it on a somewhat larger scale in the future. For that purpose, we need to check the taste and properties of crops grown together with Evil Weed.

So the next day, we decided to create a garden next to the storage shed.

Even with crops, there are appropriate planting seasons, but when it comes to farming, the Labyrinth Village residents have more experience, so advice is readily available.

“For this season… um. How about planting pumpkins?”

“Yeah. We have some extra seedlings.”

Claire the Arachne and Cyrille the Centaur looked at each other and answered like that. So pumpkins it was. If we plant them now, we should be able to harvest in autumn.

Farming work—especially creating a garden from scratch—often gives the impression of being quite troublesome… but in my case, I can use Golems for tasks like removing stones from the garden area or tilling the soil. So I had the Golems divide the work and complete it quickly. Seraphina happily rode on the head of a working Golem.

We transplanted the flowers grown by Evil Weed inside a fence to create a proper flower bed.

Meanwhile, for the vegetable garden, we made rounded ridges and transplanted the Evil Weeds between them, then planted the seedlings to complete the basic setup. From my knowledge, I considered spreading lime, but since we want to see Evil Weed’s effects, it would be better to create both a garden without it and one with it for testing.

Since we had the seedlings, we decided to plant them by hand together. Though it’s a bit rich coming from me who’s using Golems to make things easier, there’s something quintessentially garden-like about it.

“I like this kind of work.”

Claudia happily planted the seedlings. She seemed somewhat skilled—perhaps she’s become accustomed to such tasks in Labyrinth Village.

“Claudia, in Labyrinth Village after all?”

“Yes. Though they don’t let me help much, saying I shouldn’t be doing manual labor.”

“We’d rather have our princess be more elegant.”

“Right?”

Claire and Cyrille nodded to each other with smiles, and Claudia gave a small wry smile.

Lavigne dug holes with her front legs, Marlene planted the seedlings, and Seraphina covered them with soil—the farming work progressed peacefully throughout. It was quite a heartwarming scene, and the women’s smiles seemed particularly bright.

“The seedlings have been watered thoroughly. After this, we’ll adjust things while observing their progress. When the pumpkins flower, they’ll need to be pollinated.”

Claire explained various things. It seemed processes like pruning and artificial pollination remained.

Hmm. Leaving pruning aside, would Evil Weed handle artificial pollination too?

While I thought I might be expecting too much, part of me wondered if it might. They are the ones who seem to be cultivating surrounding plants.

“Please take good care of them.”

The Evil Weeds were being petted on the head by Ashley. Those stationed between the ridges remained docile and accepting.

Hmm. Essentially, as long as we can confirm that scene… If we don’t miss the flowering timing, we should be able to observe Evil Weed’s reactions.

Well, I’m also somewhat concerned about the garden’s growth progress, so I’ll check on it frequently while observing.

+++

# **202 – The Book of Captives**

After the farm work had settled down for a while, Cecilia brought us some shaved ice. Since the weather was nice, I decided to eat it outside and take a break with everyone.

“Pumpkins, huh? I’m looking forward to the harvest.”

“There are some experimental aspects too, but I’m looking forward to those as well.”

“Yes. I’ve… always liked the pumpkin pies that Mihaela-sama makes.”

“Is that so? If we get a harvest that’s good enough to eat, it might be nice to have her bake us some pies.”

At those words, Mihaela straightened her posture and bowed her head.

“I don’t know if it will suit your taste, but if my baking is acceptable…”

“Please let us help you when the time comes,” said Grace and Cecilia.

Mihaela showed a gentle smile, nodded, and elegantly brought the shaved ice to her mouth.

“…Speaking of which, are there any unusual crops in the Labyrinth Village?”

Curious, I asked Claudia. It wouldn’t be bad to try cultivating something rare if they had it. Since there are seasonal considerations like sowing seeds and planting, it’s better to make plans early.

At my words, Claudia showed a thoughtful expression before answering.

“There aren’t particularly rare agricultural products… but there might be something that could be called a specialty product. I’m not very knowledgeable about worldly matters, so I’m not sure.”

“A specialty product, huh? It might be good to consider selling it. Like selling only what we receive.”

If we only sell what we receive, the burden on production would be light.

“That might be good. It’s the clothing that the village residents wear, but it’s made from fabric woven from thread spun by the Arachnes.”

“That’s… certainly unusual.”

“Would it be something we could sell?”

Claire, who was eating shaved ice, seemed unsure…

“Actually, in Termwills, clothes woven from water spider silk by Mermaids and Sirens are imported through trade and sold. It might be good to ask an expert. Of course, we’ll only proceed if we get positive opinions.”

“In that case, I’ll ask the other Arachnes.”

Hmm. If we could sell that fabric here, use the money earned to buy outside goods, and bring prosperity to the Labyrinth Village… it would essentially become a form of trade.

“The Arachnes seem enthusiastic. They had some fabric before tailoring, so I brought it with me… what do you think?”

That evening, I got a response from Claudia. She let me touch the fabric she was holding, and it had a very nice texture. Spider silk, huh? I’ve heard that as thread, it’s actually quite durable. If that’s the case, Arachne Thread should also have excellent durability.

“Then I’ll take that to town and ask around.”

The tailor who helped us with the Lunaworm coat before would be good. I’ll go with Miriam another day.

“They said they want to try whether it can be sold as a product,” Claudia said with a smile.

Yeah. It seems to be stimulating them in various ways, which is good.

While relaxing in the Japanese-style room and thinking about the fabric, I received a communication from Alfred on the Communication Device.

“Can you come to the North Tower now? There seems to be a problem.”

…A problem at the North Tower? It must involve Rosemary… but what could have happened?

Although it’s a communication from Alfred, I should probably consider it as coming from King Melvin.

“…I need to go to the Royal Castle for a bit. It seems there’s something to discuss about Rosemary. I might be late.”

“Understood.”

“I’ll leave Caduceus here. If anything happens, contact me via the Communication Device.”

…I’ll take Ouroboros with me. Who knows what might happen. Putting on my Chimera Coat, I replied that I would head over immediately, then went to where Lindwurm was playing with the Carbuncles in the courtyard.

“To the Royal Castle.”

Mounting Lindwurm’s back, I announced our destination, and he let out a cry. After waiting for the Carbuncles to move away, he took flight.

Rushing to the Royal Castle, I landed near the Dragon Stable and headed to the North Tower. The guards at the entrance seemed normal. Apparently, it’s not an escape situation.

Riding the Floating Stone, I ascended to the upper floors of the North Tower. Passing through the corridor, I showed my face at Rosemary’s room to find King Melvin was there. Several servants stationed at the North Tower were also present. Rosemary… seemed to be sitting still in her chair.

“You’ve come,” said King Melvin, his expression somewhat stiff.

“What happened?”

“Hmm. Rosemary’s condition is strange. It’s somewhat beyond my ability to handle.”

I looked at Rosemary. I had noticed it since entering the room… the abnormality was obvious.

Her expression was so lifeless that you’d believe it if told she was a Doll. Her eyes remained hazy, as if all emotion had been stripped away. Certainly, this could be called an abnormal situation.

Judging from the circumstances, a servant probably noticed the abnormality and reported it to King Melvin.

If I had to guess, it might be a Magic Potion. Or something else… If it’s a Magic Potion, it should be possible to remove it later with the Amulet of Evil Repulsion, but…

“Excuse me.”

I touched Rosemary’s hand and performed Circulating Ki.

The flow of Magical Power is strange. It’s very low… or rather, it seems to be leaking outside her body somehow…

Following her Magical Power slowly, as if tracing a thin thread. Where it leads to is—

“…Who discovered her first?”

“I-It was me,” a servant timidly raised her hand.

“Could you tell me in detail about the situation at that time?”

“Well… when I noticed, she was in this state. I had brought her dinner, but she didn’t respond when I called… I thought she was doing research at her desk as usual, but…”

I see…

There was a single book placed on the desk. Rosemary’s Magical Power seemed to be being absorbed into that book.

It must be a Spell Formula similar to Curse Magic. The book’s pages were left open, but since they were left like that and no one except Rosemary had experienced abnormalities, it seemed that merely looking at it wouldn’t cause anything to happen. The written characters appeared to be from quite an old era, and at a glance, it was impossible to tell what was written.

Ancient characters, huh… This is, well…

I used the Communication Device to make contact. After briefly explaining the situation, I received a reply after a short while.

“That’s a magical trap set by ancient Magicians. They embed it in books to capture the souls of those who understand the meaning of specific pages, drawing them into the world within the book.”

That was the content of Claudia’s response.

Capture, huh… It’s fortunate it wasn’t an immediately fatal trap… but she said it’s problematic because if left alone, it would be the same as Magical Power depletion.

“What’s the method for breaking the curse?”

“From the outside, it’s impossible except for the one who set the trap. From the inside, it’s possible… by defeating the guard, though it requires using force… I hear the book’s jailer is quite formidable.”

According to Claudia, the Spell Formula only works by leaving an escape route from the inside, thereby increasing the risk to enhance its effectiveness. So even if captured by the book, it doesn’t mean immediate doom. Inside the book, you can fight just like outside… but of course, that also means the jailer is strengthened accordingly.

It’s probably a trap to counter those who would disturb the study.

For a forbidden book archive, such traps would be prepared, I suppose. From the perspective of the one who set the trap, they can do whatever they want—boil, roast, prepare as they like—with the opponent who’s been captured and turned into a doll-like state.

Let me organize the situation. So Rosemary attempted to decipher the Ancient Document with the trap set in it, and got captured by the book.

Self-rescue would be impossible for Rosemary, who has her Magic sealed. To go in after her for a Rescue… I need to understand the meaning of the Ancient Document’s pages. Around the book were Rosemary’s notes. There was also a comparison table of the characters Rosemary had deciphered. With this…

“The situation has become clear.”

After explaining Claudia’s information and the countermeasures I’d considered to King Melvin, he furrowed his brows and closed his eyes.

“What will happen if she stays like this?”

“It would be the same as continuing in a state close to Magical Power depletion. If she can’t get out for a long time, she’ll weaken and waste away… eventually, that is.”

King Melvin made a pained expression. That said, my course of action was already decided.

“…I’m thinking of going into the book.”

“—You, huh? But considering what she did, it wouldn’t be right to make you cross such a dangerous bridge.”

“That may be so, but that’s that. Part of why she’s in this state is because she was assisting with my work… and above all, I can’t stand the part about her weakening.”

The situation of a family member just watching their relative weaken is sickening even from a bystander’s perspective.

Entrusting it to the Knight Order is impossible. Understanding the Grimoire’s content is necessary. The Mage Corps might be able to go after her, but… Claudia said the opponent is quite formidable. With half-baked skills, we might end up with a double disaster.

In any case, in this situation, I don’t have the option of leaving it to others. To avoid tasting such bitterness ever again, I want to become much, much stronger.

“May I take her and the book to the mansion? If I don’t return, please send reinforcements.”

Saying this with a smile, King Melvin agonized for quite a long time… but eventually told me.

“My apologies… I must say this not as a king, but as a single father. Please forgive my foolishness for always putting you on the front lines.”

“No. I choose my own battlefields. This is the result of that.”

Well then… The book’s gatekeeper, huh? I wonder what kind of opponent it is.

+++

# **203 – The Contents of the Book**

Rosemary and her journal. A book said to capture souls.

First, we decided to move these to my mansion. This was to secure backup from Claudia.

Rosemary was placed under restrictions through Subjugation Magic, prohibiting her from using magic or creating Magic Potions, and further banning her from leaking information obtained through Magic Potions.

The former is the current problem. If she could use magic, it would help her escape from the book, whether she did it on her own or cooperated with me. However, to remove the Subjugation Magic, her own awareness is absolutely necessary, meaning Rosemary herself needs to respond.

To remove it, either the person holding the reins of the Subjugation Magic, someone who has mastered the removal Spell Formula, or someone possessing the removal Magic Tool, which is a Treasure, must make direct contact with the person herself.

In short, this means the prerequisite for removal cannot be cleared without going into the book. Since King Melvin holds the reins of Rosemary’s Subjugation Magic, we can’t have him go into the book.

The same goes for someone who knows the Spell Formula. Even if they go in, if they’re a non-combatant, it’s meaningless.

So, I would charge into the book while carrying the Magic Tool… but the one possessing it is my physical body. It was uncertain whether it would apply once I was inside the book—in a state of just my soul.

“The written content… when you understand the description of the Spell Formula to some extent, a trap activates and you get pulled into the world inside. I’ve already told you the precautions regarding the guardian… do you have any other questions?”

“I’m fine. First, I’ll just copy the pages that were open without deciphering them, so please prepare a system to handle a double distress situation.”

I copied the ink-written characters on the paper as they were and handed them over to Claudia. This was so she could proceed with deciphering them in a way that didn’t involve the book directly, enabling a rapid deployment of personnel later if needed.

“Yes. I’ll leave matters after Theodore enters to me.”

Claudia received the papers and nodded with a serious expression.

“…Please be careful. If anything happens, I will come too.”

“Theodore-sama… please don’t get hurt.”

“Come… back.”

Grace, Ashley, and Marlene… all wore worried expressions.

“It’s fine.”

I smiled at them and hugged them for a while. Since it was a solo infiltration, the circumstances were different from usual, so they were probably concerned. Regarding the physical body’s weakening due to Magical Power depletion, it should be possible to delay it by supplying Magical Power with Magic Potions.

“Be careful, Theodore.”

“When Justia and Dominique arrive, we’ll support you with Cursed Melody.”

“I’ll help Ilum too.”

Sheila, Irmhild, Seraphina. I nodded to them.

“May fortune favor your arms.”

“Please take care.”

And then Cecilia and Mihaela. Fortok, Claire, and the other Labyrinth Village residents. Watched over by them, I faced the book.

“Mm. Well then, I’m off.”

There was one problem with heading inside. Normally, it’s impossible to bring Equipment in when your soul is being drawn in, apparently.

So, I took countermeasures by passing Magical Power circulated through Ouroboros and Chimera Coat to make them be mistakenly recognized as pseudo-parts of me. Both Ouroboros and Chimera Coat are Magical Creatures. Whether this works or not is about fifty-fifty, I’d say.

I left Caduceus behind. I confirmed that the Magical Power connection was maintained. We might be able to create a means of communication with the outside.

While increasing my Magical Power through circulation, I compared the dictionary with Rosemary’s journal and proceeded with deciphering. The characters used were from an older era… but I was used to deciphering work from having done various things.

Since it was originally a trap and Rosemary’s journal was also there, the Difficulty of deciphering itself wasn’t that high.

The description of the Spell Formula. As the meaning became clearer through deciphering, I felt a sensation as if scenes were appearing in my mind.

It was a town. The streets of some town. Writhing shadows and silver fish flying in the sky.

For a moment, my consciousness faded—I felt a dizzying sensation—and when I came to, I was in the middle of an unfamiliar town.

The surroundings were open, and various things were writhing, but there was no sign of them attacking. Ouroboros and Chimera Coat—they’re fine. They came along. Circulation… is possible. No problem. The band of Magical Power was connecting my physical body and the book.

I can feel the connection with Caduceus… but it seems I can’t link. I can’t see the situation outside, but well, since I can send minimal instructions, I should be able to let them know I’m safe.

I looked around. The townscape felt somewhat unnatural. There were no traces of people living there. There was no deterioration or patina that should appear over time. It gave the impression of being artificial, like a tasteless, dry replica of a town.

In the distance, a huge Castle. The people walking the streets were like hollow shadows. Occasionally, they let out something that sounded like pained moans.

Eyes and a mouth. Faces with just three round holes. Bodies like vague mist. They seemed to be wandering aimlessly.

Looking up at the sky, silver creatures flying around at bullet-like speeds. Those are… giant

Silverfish (Shimi), aren’t they? Were they called bookworms? The sky was dreary and cloudy, eerie… but indeed, this was inside a book.

The insect typically called a bookworm is the deathwatch beetle, but I don’t see any of those here. Since silverfish cause less damage, perhaps their presence is tolerated?

Anyway, neither the shadow residents nor the silverfish pay any attention to me. I don’t know what would happen if I provoked them.

Still… somehow, I feel a sense of nostalgia, of familiarity.

“Ah… this is—”

This discomfort is similar to being inside a space reproduced in VR.

Looking from that perspective, I notice that the townscape occasionally has noise running through it, and fragmentary, meaningless symbols flicker here and there.

Claudia said that the guardian is the ruler who constructs and maintains this world, but the captive is ultimately equal. That’s the nature of the contract’s Spell Formula, the Curse Magic, apparently.

She said the person’s actual abilities are accurately reflected, but the essence is closer to a mental world… I see.

A virtual space that draws in souls. Now that you mention it, it’s similar to VR.

But rather than pondering that, I have other things to do now. I’ll stop the analysis here; I need to find Rosemary.

The immediate problem is how to find someone whose location I don’t know.

The first idea that comes to mind is heading towards the conspicuous Castle in the distance… but Rosemary is more the type to thoroughly grasp the situation first before moving, rather than heading straight to such an obvious place.

In that case… the reasonable approach would be to create a commotion while sending a recognizable signal to her.

First, I walked through the town for a while—and came out into a square. This area should be good. I decided to send a signal to Rosemary, also to check the sensation of using Magic inside the book.

The method—creating a Golem. I broke up the cobblestones and began constructing a huge Golem.

The shadow residents slowly moved away, but the silverfish seemed to have noticed me and came flying towards me.

Silverfish, huh. I don’t really want to deal with them, but—.

“Don’t get in the way.”

I struck down the silverfish charging at high speed with Ouroboros. The moment they touched the Dragon Staff imbued with Magical Power, they shattered, leaving silver splashes. Their movements are quick, but they’re fragile. I probably don’t need to check their Attack Power.

I deployed a Shield. The moment a silverfish touched it, I used Magical Power manipulation to deliver a shock strike, and it burst like a silver firework. A moment later, ancient characters ran like noise and disappeared.

About a dozen or so, I guess. While enlarging the Golem and casually dealing with the silverfish, they seemed to realize it was no contest and moved away on their own.

They’re still flying around at a distance—but it seems the silverfish have given up attacking me for now. Since there’s no one else attacking, I focused on building the Golem.

Earth Magic 7th Tier: Create Huge Golem. It’s a Golem larger than the surrounding buildings, but its appearance is modeled directly after my own. I think Rosemary is more likely to notice and come to check. I myself can just float around head-level using Levitation.

Well… if this doesn’t get her attention, I might have to wreck some of the townscape a bit.

“I thought I had finally gone mad…”

As planned, or rather, a little while later, Rosemary appeared in the square.

It was just when I was thinking about smashing the town. Good thing it was in time.

“I’m glad you’re not hurt.”

Saying that, I landed on the ground. Perhaps she had been attacked by the silverfish; the hem of Rosemary’s dress was torn. She was holding a stick she must have picked up from somewhere—but she didn’t seem to be injured from the look of it.

“Why are you here?”

Rosemary seemed astonished as she said that.

“To rescue you. Outside the book, Rosemary’s body has become like an empty shell.”

When I gave that answer, Rosemary’s eyes widened.

“Outside… the book? So… that’s it. So you understood that I was captured, not that I ran away. My body is left outside? I see…”

Rosemary seemed to grasp her situation relatively accurately from my words.

“First… thank you, I’ll say that. But—”

She hesitated for a moment, then made a sour face.

“Considering the situation, your person is far more important, isn’t it? Is this my father’s decision?”

Does she think I charged in without prior information? Certainly… from Rosemary’s perspective, she doesn’t even know if there’s a way out.

For the current Kingdom of Verdugal, my person is more important, and above all, she’s thinking this because she’s the one who messed up.

“No. I proposed it. For now, shall we sit and talk over there?”

I pointed towards the table seats at what looked like a food and drink establishment near the fountain. Rosemary seemed concerned about the silverfish in the sky, but when she realized they weren’t attacking, she nodded.

Even after sitting down, no waiter came to take our order, but we sat facing each other at the table.

“To give you the conclusion first, we can get out.”

“How can you say that?”

Rosemary seemed somewhat uncomfortable. Maybe because she didn’t have the feather fan she always uses. Though she is wearing a dress.

“There’s someone who knows about the trap set in the book. The way out is apparently to defeat the guardian who is somewhere inside this book.”

“Guardian…?”

“The ruler of this world, but conditionally, they’re equal to us. That’s how they enhance the power of the Curse Magic.”

“…So by taking on a disadvantage, the effect is strengthened.”

“And, I’ve brought the Magic Tool to remove the Subjugation Magic… but it’s no use. If I don’t have it with me here, there’s no way to use it, so to speak.”

It’s a Magic Tool shaped like a key… but right now, I don’t have it with me.

“You brought out a Treasure? I have a prior record, you know.”

Is she suggesting the possibility that it was a trap set by Rosemary? That would be too crude for a scheme.

“I thought that was unlikely. It would mean you knew about the book’s existence in advance, were confident the Magic Tool would work even inside here, and even calculated that I would come to rescue you.”

“That’s true. Even as a gamble, it might be too optimistic. Even if it worked, whether in a fight or a Surprise Attack, I don’t think I could win in combat.”

Saying that, she shrugged her shoulders.

“Well, let’s move on. If we dawdle too long inside here, I hear the physical body weakens and dies. Either from Magical Power depletion, or else starvation or dehydration. The crucial Magic Tool—I’m trying to use it, but it seems to have no effect.”

“Adding insult to injury. I could manage the silverfish even without magic, but the guardian… I probably couldn’t handle that no matter how hard I tried.”

It seems she had been managing without magic until I arrived. They are fragile, sure, but they do fly around at considerable speed.

But if the Subjugation Magic removal Magic Tool isn’t effective, Rosemary’s power will remain sealed. …Well, I had anticipated that too. We’ll just have to manage somehow.

+++

# **204 – The Demon with the Owl Mask**

“Can I count on you two?”

I summoned Nemea and Capella from within the coat and asked. The lion and goat each nodded. Seems there’s no problem.

I took off the Chimera Coat and handed it to Rosemary.

“What an unusual magical creature. What about the decrease in your combat strength?”

“Being able to fight without worrying about my back is more significant.”

“I see.”

Rosemary tore the hem of her dress without hesitation to ensure ease of movement before putting on the coat.

“It doesn’t seem to move according to my will.”

Huh? Both Nemea and Capella are semi-autonomous magical creatures that should move according to the wearer’s will… When I send a command from my side, Nemea pokes her head out and looks at me.

“…Could it be because I’m the one who wears it outside the book? Well, I’ll order them to focus on interception and dodging.”

I’m not putting Rosemary in the vanguard, so this should be fine.

When I turned my gaze toward the castle visible at the city center, Rosemary asked.

“If there’s a guardian, would it be in that castle?”

“Probably. We could charge straight in, but let’s prepare a bit first. If you want to mix something for self-defense, I can do it for you, but what do you think?”

“…I wonder if anything here can be trusted.”

Rosemary frowned, but I don’t see it as much of a problem.

“I think the so-called guardian is actually fair. The reason silverfish exist here despite not being particularly strong is probably because of that.”

“Inside the book, to make us realize?”

She must have been investigating before I arrived, and I think Rosemary had been considering aspects related to the book too.

“Exactly. Normally, you can’t bring weapons or armor in. Yet it’s equal, which is strange. If it’s unavoidable due to the mechanism, then it means we’re free to use whatever’s in the town to compensate for the prisoners’ disadvantage as much as possible.”

And I think this is rather important information. The extent of that fairness makes this world more robust the more thorough it is… and apparently serves as the basis for the guardian’s power.

“Then let’s prepare something. I saw what appeared to be an alchemist’s shop over on that street. We should be able to quickly prepare some makeshift offensive tools.”

Rosemary stood up. Well then, we’ll continue our conversation while moving and mixing.

“If everything existing in this town has meaning… then what about these residents?”

The residents were just wandering aimlessly while letting out painful moans. …And they were running away from the golems too.

“…Victims, perhaps?”

“The souls of those who lost to the guardian? For a trap in a hidden forbidden library, wouldn’t the number of these victims be strange?”

“No. Apparently, magicians summon and contract guardians, incorporating them into spell formulas. So they might have multiple territories (..). In any case, it seems guardians have rules requiring them to fight prisoners.”

I’ve heard that book guardians with multiple territories can travel between them. In that case, the territory would be liberated over time if the guardian is absent, but well, it’s originally an interception trap. It’s not something that happens often – prisoners getting caught here and there to the point the guardian can’t handle it all.

At least regarding this book, if we assume the residents are past victims, then the guardian probably isn’t absent.

It would be better to share information about what’s inside the book. I’ll tell Rosemary.

“I see…”

“Though that’s only if my speculation is correct.”

“Probably, that’s right. After I came here and some time passed, the residents started appearing. The guardian must be carrying them around. In other words, it’s showing off the prey it’s captured everywhere.”

“How tasteless…”

“I agree. All the information coming out just confirms how powerful our opponent is, and it’s getting tiresome.”

When we entered the alchemist’s shop, Rosemary began browsing various items.

“Quite a good selection. With this—”

She arranged materials on the mixing table.

My work simply involved filling a flask with medicinal liquid, pouring in several types of powdered medicine, and sealing it with a cork. Rosemary gathered all the magic stones in the shop and stuffed them into a leather bag.

“What are you making with that?”

“It would be faster to show you. Let’s test it.”

Rosemary went out to the street and tried to throw a magic stone into the flask but stopped her hand.

“…No good. It violates the subjugation magic.”

“Just need to put a magic stone in, right?”

I can have Nemea or Capella help. I had them hold a magic stone in their mouth and drop it into the flask.

“With this, it might work.”

Saying that, Rosemary casually threw the flask, and the moment it shattered on the cobblestones, a rather spectacular green pillar of fire rose up. It seemed to have different properties from natural fire, and I could feel intense magical power radiating from it rather than heat.

“Flames that interfere with the magical power of whatever they touch, I suppose. Considering the material costs, it’s not cost-effective, so it’s practically useless.”

I see… So it’s like a makeshift grenade.

Well then, let’s make some more of the same without getting in Rosemary’s way, then head to the castle.

The castle interior was completely silent. Neither the residents that were in the town nor the silverfish flying around were present. No soldiers came out to intercept us either.

Put conversely. They’ve thoroughly constructed an environment that prevents any interference.

In that case, the guardian is probably neither running nor hiding, but waiting somewhere like the throne room.

“About the guardian’s true identity…”

“Continuing from our earlier conversation?”

This came up briefly while sharing information with Rosemary. Guardians can be spirits, magical creatures, or vary greatly depending on the magician who set the trap.

The only common point is that beings close to psychic lifeforms are chosen.

“The guardian here… no, the lord, I suppose. This one has clear malice.”

…Malice, huh. Certainly. Even though it should be a trap for interception and delay, it goes beyond that by not liberating the victims’ souls, treating them like a collection or trophies. It shows them off to prisoners and delights in it. Despite having such poor taste, it follows the rules. It prepared an alchemist’s shop with such a good selection that Rosemary was impressed. Probably other weapons and armor would be first-class too.

A psychic lifeform that freely travels between multiple territories, even though it should have a contract with a magician. With such a guardian, the candidates naturally narrow down.

“…A demon?”

“I thought so, and prepared tools that seem effective against that kind of non-physical entity.”

The magical flame bottle from earlier.

The Flame Demon of the Blazing Fortress was a being created by the labyrinth… but that one was quite physical.

Original demons are said to have properties close to spirits and cannot exist in this world without incarnation… but here, it’s probably in its true form. They say their intelligence is proportional to their power, so we can’t let our guard down.

That said, in this world I can apparently punch them away, so it’s true I don’t need to worry much about my attack methods, but the same goes for our opponent. In that sense too, it’s fair.

Eventually—we reached a large door that appeared to be the throne room.

When I pushed the door open, it was there in the vast throne room. Wearing a monocle and dressed like a noble, but with the head of an owl. Recognizing our presence, it spoke with theatrical, exaggerated gestures.

“Welcome to my castle, my territory. Are you enjoying yourselves? I am Orzius, the keeper of this book.”

“You’re the guardian of this place, right?”

Orzius narrowed his eyes. Perhaps he smiled at my response.

“It seems our current guest understands the workings of this world. As you’ve guessed, if you destroy me, you can return to your original world. To defeat me, feel free to use whatever is in the castle town. I swear upon my name that there are no tricks whatsoever.”

“Poor taste. You enjoy watching people run around in confusion, don’t you?”

“Kuku. Well, it’s one of my few pleasures.”

…Oh, is that so.

“…Sorry to disappoint your expectations, but this is fine as it is. I can’t say it’s a fair one-on-one since I brought tools from outside, but if you’re going to pretend to be fair, then me fighting with just this staff should balance things out.”

At my provocation, Orzius shook his shoulders and laughed.

“Hmm. I wouldn’t have minded if the young lady behind you came at me simultaneously too. If that’s what you want, very well. I promise to defeat you one by one. First, young man. You’re up first.”

Orzius’s eyes were twisted with delight as he said this.

He probably understands that Rosemary is a non-combatant too. If he just defeats me, he can leisurely enjoy watching the human struggle and despair.

“That’s the situation. I’d appreciate it if you watched from the back.”

“…I see. Even though I went to the trouble of making them, it seems I won’t get my turn.”

Rosemary shrugged her shoulders and stood in the corner of the room.

It’s just a verbal promise… but still, for demons, contracts and promises are absolute. Stray shots might fly her way, but she should be able to protect herself from that much.

In any case, it’s fortunate that I don’t have any worries about my back. All that’s left—is to focus on the battle before my eyes.

+++

# **205 – The Great Scythe of Shadow Cutting**

“Since you’re the only one left if you lose anyway… would you mind handling my share as well?”

Rosemary offers me a set of flask and magic stone.

“I don’t mind. Even if you accept that, it remains as we agreed earlier.”

Orjius shrugs and says such a thing.

…Completely unacceptable.

The magician who contracted with this bastard must have died long ago, yet to preserve his own enjoyment afterward, he probably didn’t set a time limit for guarding the book in the contract.

The result is what we saw in town. The remnants of people whose souls were worn down until they became mere wandering shadows. All those people challenged the demon, or gave up, dying in despair. Yet they remain unliberated, toyed with through unimaginable stretches of time.

This bastard—I won’t let him get away with it.

“…Understood. I’ll be right back.”

I deploy a Defense Field around Rosemary and accept the flask and magic stone. Reinforcing them with Earth Magic so the glass won’t break, I tie them to my waist with a cord. Then, at a deliberate pace, I walk toward Orjius.

Darkness coils in Orjius’s hand. From within it, a massive scythe is dragged out. So he uses weapons too. As if twirling a baton, the scythe spins rapidly in Orjius’s hand, cutting through the air.

I take stance with Ouroboros and amplify my magical power. The moment I brace to step in, Orjius slams the scythe’s tip into the shadow stretching from his feet. Responding to this, blades shoot out from the head of Orjius’s elongated shadow.

I stop the tip with a Shield and immediately press forward in one motion. Orjius, having withdrawn from the shadow, meets it. Ouroboros and the scythe clash, scattering sparks.

“Quite capable, aren’t you!”

Orjius’s voice sounds almost pleased at having been countered.

Despite preaching fairness, his opening move is a frontal ambush. From his perspective, even if he kills me in one breath, Rosemary remains, so he can still enjoy watching her struggle.

He said we’d fight equally, but that was a precondition. Once we face each other like this, rules become meaningless. Anything goes, as expected.

A double-edged scythe. He can freely use the inner edge for pulling cuts or the outer edge for sweeping attacks. After several exchanges of our weapons, the scythe’s butt cap flips upward. The sharply pointed tip, like a spearhead, passes through the space before my nose, then Orjius’s body spins completely. A blade attacks with a horizontal sweep from a blind spot hidden by his body’s shadow. A winding trajectory. If I step in to block, the blade will be pulled back from behind; if I distance myself, I can’t counterattack. So instead, I step in close enough to bodily crash into him.

I swing Ouroboros upward from below, aiming for the arm gripping the scythe. Striking around the elbow to disrupt the scythe’s path, I unleash a front kick. I only need to make contact. Regardless of whether defense is possible, my plan is to hammer in a magical shock at the moment of contact and then break through.

But Orjius doesn’t forcibly counter or defend. The moment his arm is struck upward, he releases the scythe and retreats significantly. A counterattack while evading. After a breath’s pause, the scythe returns, spinning from behind. I leap backward, shifting form mid-air. Clearing the scythe, I charge in by kicking off a Shield without waiting to land.

An owl’s wings appear on Orjius’s back. He flies into the sky to escape. I kill my inertia with Levitation, flying at a right angle to pursue Orjius.

“Truly, human endeavor is fascinating! Shall I ask your name?”

“Theodore!”

We clash mid-air. Several attacks cross. Ringing metallic sounds.

As we separate, Orjius makes a gesture as if sweeping upward with his wings. Feathers fly at armor-piercing speeds. A three-directional deviation shooting. I only strike down the feather coming straight at me with Ouroboros.

The remaining two feathers easily penetrated the marble floor.

We both charge into a fierce collision. We reach a deadlock, but the scythe’s blade retracts and a blade emerges from the opposite end—the butt cap side. I use a Shield like a rail to divert the scythe’s path upward as it slides and swings up from below. Into the exposed flank, I hammer the Dragon Staff.

“Guh!”

He’s knocked back significantly, but while being blown away, he scatters feathers to prevent pursuit. Form shift, form shift. Feathers thin as blades graze past, right before my eyes.

Splitting left and right with Mirage Body, we cross. No effect. I expected this since he’s a psychic lifeform… but he accurately targets me.

Multiple black spheres are released around Orjius. As if possessing will, they maintain a fixed distance from Orjius’s main body, flying around like satellites.

A black hole opens before him, and he slams the scythe into it. The scythe’s blade shoots out from a black sphere approaching in a circular orbit. Feather bullets are fired to block escape routes. I twist only my neck to evade the feathers, block the scythe with a Shield, and simultaneously counter with an impact strike. Orjius’s arm, which should be at a distance, is repelled.

The spheres tracing satellite orbits seem to pass through Ouroboros and Shield unaffected. They themselves possess no attack power—mere spheres of darkness. Their purpose is attack assistance. Probably the same technique he used initially to deliver slash attacks from shadow to shadow. Feather bullets had flown into the black spheres, but those didn’t transfer over. Whether he can’t or won’t is uncertain, but it’s definite that Orjius can transfer the scythe’s blade from shadow to shadow among those he created.

I distance myself and turn back. A hot sensation on my cheek. Seems a feather grazed me.

…He possesses diverse and irregular attack methods. Can’t let my guard down.

So, sharper and faster. Stronger, ever stronger. I’ll surpass this bastard too and move forward. Cycle cycle cycle cycle. Baring fangs in a grin, I sharpen and refine my magical power.

“I’m glad you seem to be enjoying yourself! I’m having fun too! It’s exhilarating!”

Orjius spins his scythe like a windmill. Eyes wide open, shoulders shaking.

“Kukuku! How you reached that level—my interest is endless! You—will surely become a most valuable addition to my collection!”

“Try it!”

We roar and charge at each other. Collision, impact. The scythe has no blade. It hasn’t moved to the butt cap side; instead, a dark sphere adheres to the tip, swallowing it. From another dark sphere flying from behind, the scythe’s blade emerges, aiming to bisect my body.

I deploy a Shield behind me. The moment it makes contact, I hammer in an impact, but this time, as if anticipating it, Orjius doesn’t retreat. He pins me down from the front, putting force into bisecting me from behind.

Multiple Shield deployment. As sparks scatter between Ouroboros and the scythe’s handle in equilibrium, I fire a Lightning Strike at Orjius’s face. At the exact same time, he releases a magical flash from his beak. An explosion occurs, repelling us. As Orjius retreats, the blade withdraws too. Immediate reversal. Slipping between feather bullets flying as if piercing through the blast, I fly at maximum speed, exchanging slash attacks and strikes.

Blades fly in all directions. A rain of feathers pours down. Evading, blocking, redirecting, I dive in and strike countless times. Though it should be a single weapon, Orjius’s skill in manipulating it as if separating handle and blade is considerable. Continuing to clash like this won’t get us anywhere.

Against Orjius, who blocked with the handle, I push in with my whole body and deliver a headbutt to his head. Since I’ve deployed a Shield on my forehead, I take no damage, but Orjius steps back looking stunned.

“You!!”

Fury. The scythe swings down from above. A dark sphere cuts into the slash trajectory, transferring the blade. The tip approaches directly from below. Trying to block, Ouroboros is knocked away as if being rolled up. Switching, this time the blade approaches from the side.

I raise my hand, but the Shield is penetrated. Without Ouroboros, the Shield can’t withstand it. Gritting my teeth, I receive the scythe’s tip with my palm. It penetrates my palm. Orjius narrows his eyes at the sensation.

“I’ll carve you up, arm and all!”

Saying this, he tries to put in force—but Orjius freezes. This much was within my calculations.

He doesn’t move. Gripping with my pierced palm, I fix him in place with Shields from all directions. Perfectly sealing his movements so he can neither withdraw nor cut through.

Leading him to believe the Shield couldn’t completely defend—that was my strategy. Seeing my grin, Orjius instantly releases the scythe and tries to escape. Since he can freely control the scythe, letting go isn’t a disadvantage. Precisely because of that—I anticipated he’d try to distance himself.

“Return!”

“Wha—!?”

He’s not the only one who can launch weapons. Ouroboros, charging from behind, roars as it gouges into his back from behind, pinning him and not allowing escape. Ouroboros can only move as long as the magical power I’ve imbued it with lasts—but that’s more than enough.

“Gaaah!”

Avoiding the flash released from his mouth by tilting my head, I toss the flask and magic stone with my open hand. Right in front of Orjius’s face, eyes wide in astonishment.

Clenching my fist, I deploy a Shield. Hammering in an impact strike, the flask and magic stone shatter simultaneously, green explosive flames engulfing Orjius’s face.

“Guooooooaaaaah!?”

Having his face directly burned by magical flames, Orjius writhes in agony. Covering his face, he flails his wings, trying to escape the spot while scattering feather bullets indiscriminately.

I ignore some hits. Deploying a giant Magic Circle, I charge the shortest distance. Feathers pierce my shoulder, graze my flank. Tracing an arc, I grip Ouroboros, which has now truly returned to my hand, and thrust straight—piercing through his body’s center, the solar plexus.

“Gah!”

Orjius’s body bends into a V-shape. I slam Ouroboros into the base of his wings, smashing him onto the floor. Still burning. Impressive, despite its simple construction. And—my magic is complete.

“Get crushed!”

At the tip of the raised Ouroboros, a giant rock glowing pure white appears.

9th Tier. Fire, Earth composite magic—Meteor Hammer. Matching the motion of swinging down the Dragon Staff, the boulder is fired from initial velocity with ridiculous force. The white-hot meteor approaches Orjius, shattering the sound barrier.

“O, ooooooaaaah!?”

Unable to evade, Orjius takes the boulder directly with his body. Piercing through the marble floor like paper, it collapses the throne room from the center. Engulfing everything on the lower floor, it drills straight down into the earth’s depths.

+++

# **206 – Contracts and Enforcement**

The force that had been trying to move vanished from the scythe still embedded in me. When I released the Shield’s restraint, it fell from my palm.

To destroy it or not? Whether the scythe could determine Orjius’s life or death was questionable, but if he were alive, there was no doubt he could manipulate the scythe.

Considering the possibility it had its own will, I tightly bound it with Earth Magic and Light Bind before packaging it, then placed it within visible range where I could deal with it if it moved.

I jumped over the large hole and headed toward Rosemary. She looked stunned beyond words.

Rosemary was unharmed. I had fired the Meteor Hammer with my back turned to keep her outside the magic’s range, and had double-insured with both Defense Field and Chimera Coat.

“That hand… your shoulder too. Show me your wounds.”

Rosemary cut the hem of her dress with a stiff expression, making an impromptu bandage. She had borrowed a dagger from the alchemist’s shop.

“…Yeah. Thanks.”

…I should just accept her kindness straightforwardly. I let her bandage my palm and shoulder.

“For the severity of the wounds, there’s surprisingly little bleeding.”

“I’m using Shield to stop the bleeding.”

At my words, Rosemary nodded as if understanding.

“I wonder how wounds work in this world?”

“They say as long as it’s not a fatal wound, you’ll be fine once you leave.”

That said, things like massive blood loss could lead to death in this world, and apparently that would mean dying outside the book too. So it’s not like getting injured is acceptable.

As for the pain issue, well, during battle I don’t really notice it much. After the fight ends, it gets pretty tough though.

“Do you always fight like that?”

While bandaging me, Rosemary asked.

“That depends on the opponent. If I can lure them by pretending to create an opening, I consider it a necessary expense.”

In evenly matched situations, it becomes a matter of luck or turns into a battle of attrition, neither of which I particularly welcome. So it’s better to guide them toward predictable actions and draw them out… but sometimes they take the bait without biting the hook, so it’s tricky.

“This is the first time I’ve seen you fight seriously, so you were holding back considerably against me. —There. This should do.”

Rosemary finished bandaging and stepped back. Regarding pain and ease of movement, it felt somewhat better. As long as I reinforce it with Shield, there shouldn’t be any problems.

“So then. How do we get out of here?”

“They said if we defeat the guardian, the maintenance would fail and we’d be released.”

Looking around, the noise occasionally running through the space had become quite severe. It seemed certain that it was on the verge of collapse.

“Ooohhhhaaahhh!”

Then, a pained voice came from the large hole in the throne room’s floor. An owl-shaped Aura-like thing was crawling up from below.

“Did he… survive that?”

Rosemary frowned. Well—I wonder.

Orjius didn’t leap at us, but stood facing us from a distance.

“Y-your victory. I’ll… let you out of here…”

Orjius painfully said such words. I… scoffed at them.

“Let us out? If you’re destroyed, we can get out, right?”

The noise running through the scenery intensified further. That it was on the verge of collapse was obvious to anyone, and Orjius himself looked completely battered.

“If I admit defeat, you will be released. Don’t you want this world? L-let’s make a new contract—”

“…Wrong. Lying isn’t good, Orjius.”

I laughed. When I pointed it out, Orjius clearly panicked.

“W-what do you—”

“Normally, no one should survive a direct hit from Meteor Hammer. Yet you survived like that and are approaching negotiations in your Ethereal Body. But even though you’re in Ethereal Body, you look pretty rough, don’t you?”

I chose the purely physical Meteor Hammer with this world’s rule in mind—that the more fair something is, the stronger it becomes. Meteor Hammer shouldn’t affect an Ethereal Body, yet Orjius was barely breathing. Perhaps because the body is constructed according to the rules, the damage taken by the physical body is reflected in the Ethereal Body too. But that’s probably not all.

“S-stop. No more…”

Orjius’s voice sounded almost pleading. Along with my words, not just noise but creaking sounds emerged as cracks ran through the space. And then. I spoke the decisive words.

“In other words… you’re still in the middle of the match. Moreover, right before the outcome was decided, you abandoned the body you should have in this world and escaped. Thinking that without a physical form, you could mitigate Meteor Hammer’s power. But that’s a contract violation, right? You have to properly receive Meteor Hammer’s full force with your physical body.”

I paused briefly, then said.

“Even if—it means dying along with the contract.”

“Gghh, hii—”

Flames burst from Orjius’s eyes and mouth, from inside him. If he weren’t a Psychic Lifeform, such an accusation probably wouldn’t mean anything.

But this guy is a Demon. If strict adherence to contracts is demanded, then settlement will occur retroactively.

In this case, that means he’ll be forced to properly pay the damage from the Meteor Hammer he tried to cheat.

“P-please… even now… contract renewal. Either way is fine…”

While spewing flames, Orjius reached toward us.

A contract loophole… insurance he left for himself to survive in case of defeat, probably. But I had no intention of letting him live.

After treating that many victims as toys, thinking he alone could survive—such a convenient story shouldn’t be allowed.

“Not needed.”

“I don’t need it either. This book reeks.”

The clear words of rejection from me and Rosemary. The next moment, Orjius scattered as if exploding from within. Simultaneously, the world also shattered to pieces, and the ground beneath us vanished.

Since I felt the sensation of falling, I took Rosemary’s hand and cast Levitation.

“Contracts are scary, aren’t they?”

“Absolutely.”

I quipped back at Rosemary’s wry smile. The sensation of rising. Our bodies floated upward toward the distant light in the sky.

Countless spheres of light surrounded us. The souls of the victims. Probably released now that Orjius was dead. They too rose upward, leaving behind phosphorescent light. It was a fantastical scene.

“…When we return, there’s just one thing I’d like to ask.”

“What?”

“I want you to remove the Subjugation Magic just once. Of course, you can recast it afterward.”

“Fine by me… but it’s not solely my decision.”

Rosemary nodded. What does she intend to do?

“You’ve saved my life twice now.”

“Twice?”

“This time, and when we fought before. Last time I thought I couldn’t complain even if killed, and this time even if rescue hadn’t come, it would have been getting rid of a nuisance.”

“When we fought before, you survived on your own.”

I had various reasons for not intending to kill her. The subsequent negotiations with King Melvin were probably Rosemary’s doing, and partly due to King Melvin’s virtue too.

“That’s after negotiations began. On the battlefield, it depended on your discretion. …Royalty shouldn’t bow their heads lightly. I believe that, but even so, this is too much. Not only did you save my life, but I made you get injured due to my failure.”

After confirming she wouldn’t fall even if I released her hand, Rosemary bowed deeply.

“My rude behavior since we first met. Involving Ambassador-sama and the Count’s family in my schemes, attempting to drug you, and pointing my sword at you—I humbly apologize. I know this isn’t something that can be forgiven with just a bow, but I beg your forgiveness.”

Since we first met, huh. For Rosemary, given that she had factions like Greg’s to consider, she probably couldn’t act subservient to someone of lower status in public, even if it meant making a bad impression on me.

She behaved according to the character she had established with those around her, while maneuvering behind the scenes. That was Rosemary’s strategy.

Well… if Father or others had suffered harm, things would have been different, but that’s just hindsight. As for receiving her apology, I too had aspects I couldn’t speak of lightly.

“Show me those words through your future actions.”

“Yes.”

Rosemary nodded. Perhaps she had expected to be told that.

“But well, your way of speaking can stay the same as before. Somehow, it feels awkward otherwise.”

When I said that, Rosemary’s eyes widened for a moment before she laughed.

“That way… is easier for me too.”

With those words—we were swallowed by the light.

+++

# **207 – The Treatment of Rosemary**

“…Mmm.”

I let out a sound and blinked my eyes. It felt like that drowsy sensation when waking up at an odd time.

And what came into view were everyone’s happy faces.

“…I’m back.”

“Theo! Thank goodness!”

“Welcome back!”

They spoke in unison, practically jumping to hug me. While being smothered, I gave a wry smile, stroking their hair and embracing their shoulders.

“Were you injured?”

“I got a bit hurt… but I seem to be fine now. There’s no pain either.”

I answered while clenching my left hand that had been stabbed. My shoulder was similarly unharmed.

Once they confirmed there were no particular problems with my body, Ashley finally seemed to relax.

One by one they separated, and I stood up too.

“Ugh…”

Rosemary, who had been seated on the living room sofa, let out a small sound. Then, light returned to her eyes.

“This is—”

Rosemary brought a hand to her forehead and shook her head slightly. Perhaps because she had been trapped in the book longer than me, there was a difference in the time it took to awaken.

“My home.”

“…I see.”

Rosemary stood up, albeit somewhat unsteadily, then bowed her head according to proper etiquette.

“I am deeply ashamed for having involved Theodore in danger due to my blunder. I would like to thank the person who provided the book’s information—might they be present here?”

“That would be me.”

When Claudia spoke, Rosemary turned toward her and bowed again. Then she politely offered her thanks and introduced herself.

I thought this was probably something Rosemary from a little while ago wouldn’t have done, but seeing her behave so politely seemed to come naturally to her—suggesting that if she put her mind to it, she could have conducted herself properly all along.

Now there were no faction eyes on her, and she had lost her right to the throne. There was also the promise we had just exchanged.

“That book… is it alright?”

Sheila said while looking at the book left open on the desk.

“It should be fine as long as no guardian is embedded in it. The problem is that this might not be the only book with such a Trap.”

“…Now that you mention it, that’s true.”

This time it was fortunate that Orjius was waiting in the Castle, but it’s also possible that a guardian could attack from the start.

Leaving the decoding to Rosemary alone while she can’t use Magic carries considerable risk. More than the guardian’s strength, the issue is that both sending rescue and meeting up inside would end up being delayed in various ways.

And the further back we go seeking information in ancient documents, the more likely we are to step on landmines.

“Countermeasures?”

“If Marlene and I are nearby… the book’s Spell Formula is powerful, so remote intervention wouldn’t work.”

Marlene blinked at Claudia’s words.

I see… So if it’s Curse Magic, it can be countered with Blessing. For now, we’ll need to send Rosemary to the Royal Castle and consult with King Melvin.

After contacting him via the Communication Device, Rosemary and I returned to the North Tower together. King Melvin let out a deep breath of relief before smiling.

“You have done me a great service. Are you uninjured?”

“As you can see, we’re both fine.”

“My apologies for the trouble.”

We sat across the table, drinking tea as I explained what we had discovered about the book’s Trap.

“I see… Then continuing as we are now would be difficult, I suppose.”

King Melvin crossed his arms, then brought a hand to his chin in a thoughtful gesture.

“Claudia has suggested a solution, though.”

“But to ask Lady Claudia to frequently trouble herself to come to the Royal Castle…”

Right. Claudia probably shouldn’t show her face at the Royal Castle too often. There is a way to resolve that, but I doubt King Melvin would ever mention it.

“…If she stays at my house, that would solve the issue.”

That would address the problem of her life being targeted too.

“That may indeed be so—but do you trust this person that much?”

“She did say she would prove herself through actions…”

Given that Rosemary has never shown her true intentions, it’s hard to say we can easily trust her. But there’s no one else who can replace her in decoding ancient documents, and to have her continue decoding, we need to prevent situations like this from happening again.

Rosemary didn’t even take out her feather fan, quietly closing her eyes and leaving things to fate, but then she spoke.

“I leave the decision regarding my circumstances to you… but there is a matter I would like to request of you, Father.”

“Speak.”

“Just for a moment, if I may. I would like to request the removal of the Subjugation Magic.”

“Why?”

When asked, Rosemary answered.

“I wish to impose Oath Magic upon myself. I believe that a Subjugation Magic imposed by command holds no value for reflection and does not contribute to my own credibility.”

Oath Magic. This is a type of Contract Magic, similar to placing Subjugation Magic upon oneself, but more robust. To remove it later, one must fulfill the conditions set when making the oath.

“You… what exactly do you intend to swear?”

When asked, Rosemary showed a slightly thoughtful gesture.

“Well now. I intend to swear that for my entire life, I will never betray you, Father, and Theodore Gartner-sama… my two lifesavers. Should I break that oath, I wish for it to cost me my life… but given the issues of interpretation and perception, accidental activation would be problematic. I’m considering whether there might be a better method.”

She said it as if it were natural. King Melvin and I inadvertently exchanged glances.

…Seriously? Just earlier she was saying contracts are frightening, and now this on the same day? This is Rosemary, who has repeatedly deceived and tricked people. In terms of “earning trust,” there’s probably nothing better than this… but precisely because she’s skilled at phrasing things to avoid giving verbal commitments… if she says she’ll do it, she’ll do it. This is extreme, to say the least.

…Still, interpretation and perception, huh? If we consider oaths and contracts the same, then depending on interpretation and perception, there’s a risk of activation in unintended situations.

I suppose it means even inner feelings can’t be falsified. The trigger for this magic is the person’s own awareness.

“…For example… if you unintentionally betray someone, there’s a risk it could lead to death when you realize it?”

“That would be the case.”

King Melvin remained with his arms crossed, eyes closed as if deep in thought for a while, then finally spoke.

“There are issues that need addressing… but for my part, if you wish to use Oath Magic, I am not unwilling to permit it. Trust cannot be gained except through foolishly honest accumulation. If one who has willingly destroyed it now seeks to cut off their own retreat, then we should acknowledge that resolve.”

“…But making life the price is problematic, don’t you think? I understand the level of resolve, but…”

Personally, I think she doesn’t need to go that far, but if King Melvin doesn’t stop her, then if Rosemary says she’ll do it, she’ll do it.

If my words could stop her, she probably wouldn’t have attempted such schemes in the first place. She was likely prepared for defeat to mean death too. Her resolve is just too complete.

“Would it suffice if the betrayal becomes clear and your actions are hindered? How about making it so that if you betray someone, you can no longer construct Spell Formulas and cannot move?”

“We would need to make it possible to lift the restraint through confession and obtaining forgiveness. Since treating serious and minor matters with the same measure would be problematic.”

“So you would leave the judgment to the other party? If you and I are unavailable, to whom would you confess?”

“…Perhaps someone with close ties. Also, we need to define what constitutes betrayal. It would be troublesome if it activated in situations where I simply couldn’t meet expectations due to lack of ability.”

They continued addressing various anticipated issues. Like how being unable to move during emergencies would leave one defenseless, which is problematic.

“What about making exceptions so the restraint doesn’t apply under exceptional circumstances?”

“In that case, we should use Subjugation Magic to supplement it, ensuring no harm comes to the person during emergencies.”

And so, Rosemary herself kept adding supplements to ensure there were no oversights.

They thoroughly examined all the issues, filling in the gaps. Writing it all down on paper—once they had roughly eliminated the deficiencies, they finally proceeded to remove Rosemary’s Subjugation Magic.

“Very well, I shall remove the Subjugation Magic.”

Using the key-shaped Magic Tool he held, he removed Rosemary’s Subjugation Magic. The Magic Stone in the tool flashed, and Rosemary’s body became enveloped in phosphorescent light as a sound like something shattering echoed. With this, the Subjugation Magic had likely been removed.

“Now then—I would like to perform the Oath Magic ritual. Afterward, I ask for your assistance with the Subjugation Magic.”

—And so… with all that, it was decided Rosemary would come to my house. The books from the forbidden library would be transported at a later date… but this probably means we’ll need to add at least one more hidden study.

+++

# **208 – The Master of the Doll**

“I’m going in.”

Ashley and Marlene faced the Golem with their Long Mace and rapier at the ready, beginning ground combat training. The Golem was modeled after a figure armed with armor and swords.

This was close-quarters, ground combat training. While unspectacular, it was effective for building fundamental strength. Once you could read an opponent’s movements, the skills could be applied to aerial combat or ranged shooting battles as well.

Given Ashley’s weapon choice, her fighting style was straightforward – she would strike areas likely to take damage or deliver powerful blows to stun her opponent before finishing them off in one go. However, she added her own unique flair to this approach.

She stepped right into the Golem’s range, dodging attacks while striking at its knee joints. She created ice spikes on her Round Shield to deliver a shield bash, then struck the staggered opponent’s dominant arm side to take it down. The entire sequence flowed with elegant grace.

In Ashley’s close-quarters movements, one could see Rosetta’s influence in her body maneuvering and attack methods. She seemed to have thoroughly studied human vital points and anatomy, delivering remarkably logical attacks. It was also noteworthy how ice would shoot from Ashley’s feet just before her attacks, freezing the opponent’s supporting leg.

As for Marlene, perhaps because she had an experienced rapier user like Mihaela as a mentor, her movements had visibly improved recently. She maintained a certain distance from the Golem, identifying gaps in the armor of approaching opponents to deliver slash attacks and thrusts.

If one wondered whether this was ineffective against heavily armored opponents, that wasn’t the case. Marlene’s rapier occasionally crackled with lightning, which made dealing with it without magic quite difficult. She would use feints involving weight shifts and subtle tip movements, needing only to land shallow thrusts. Once she shocked her opponent, they couldn’t dodge or defend against her follow-up decisive strike.

…Actually, given the nature of lightning, she didn’t even need to make contact. The Golem properly dodged, but electricity spread from the blade, effectively shocking it anyway. Marlene’s committed thrust had pierced a vital point through a gap in the armor. She was also beginning to channel Fighting Spirit, though still weakly.

“How was that?”

After defeating the Golem, the two turned to us for feedback.

“Good. Those movements were quite excellent.”

When I answered, Ashley looked somewhat bashful. Marlene smiled without reservation.

“Shall we try switching the Golem’s weapon and continue a bit more?”

“Yes!”

Thus the training continued. What weapon should the opponent have? Perhaps a spear for reach training. Well, since both could incorporate magic into their fighting, I doubted they’d struggle much.

Above the courtyard, Grace, Sheila, Irmhild, and Seraphina were conducting coordination training.

Sheila advanced toward the Golem with Grace closely overlapping behind her. From behind, Irmhild fired practice arrows with cloth tips. Sheila predicted the arrow trajectory by sound, positioning herself to avoid being hit while serving as Grace’s guide.

Just as Sheila closed in, she leaped upward while performing a vertical spin motion, releasing Sticky Thread to interfere with the Golem’s counterattack from behind. Simultaneously, the arrows hit their mark. Normally, Seraphina’s power would imbue them with Cursed Melody effects, but that was omitted this time. Finally, Grace flashed her axe, cleaving the Golem cleanly in two vertically.

We continued morning training in this manner for a while until Rosemary appeared in the courtyard. Though she hid her mouth behind a feather fan, her eyes were wide with surprise. She seemed astonished by the training scene.

“Good morning.”

“Yes, good morning.”

“Good morning.”

We exchanged morning greetings in turn.

“Thank you for last night’s late meal. It was delicious.”

“Not at all. Did you sleep well?”

“Yes. I must have been tired. I didn’t even dream until morning.”

Grace and Rosemary had that exchange.

Yesterday had been quite chaotic, and Rosemary hadn’t been able to eat dinner.

When I showed her to her room, she looked somewhat pale, so I asked about her health, but she only said it was unrelated to the book and she was fine… Then her stomach rumbled quietly, and I realized she probably hadn’t eaten.

I thought she could have just said so, but she apparently couldn’t bring herself to ask for food outright. So I asked Grace to prepare a late meal on short notice.

That said, perhaps because of such interactions, the two seemed to have warmed up to each other somewhat.

“…I’ve never cooked before. But it seems to be this household’s rule, so I’ll make an effort from now on.”

Covering her mouth with the feather fan and closing her eyes, Rosemary spoke.

“That said, everyone here is quite impressive in various ways… Catching up seems like it will be quite the challenge. I need to retrain this rusty body of mine.”

“Hm? Catching up, meaning you’ll delve into the labyrinth too?”

“That’s my intention… Was that unwise?”

“No, not unwise at all.”

For Rosemary’s outings, I had borrowed a different Disguise Ring from Anastasia to change her appearance.
