Or rather, ultimately, deciphering work would be dangerous unless Claudia or Marlene were present. If she’s going into the labyrinth, then having her accompany us would indeed eliminate redundancy. She’ll likely be quite busy, but asking for confirmation might be unnecessarily tactless.

“I’d like to understand your fighting style. Will you use dolls like before, or summon Dragon Fang Soldiers?”

“Unfortunately, the catalyst for Dragon Fang Soldiers was confiscated. However, while deciphering ancient documents recently, I found some interesting magic.”

“Oh?”

When I prepared a Golem, a Magic Circle appeared in Rosemary’s hand. From her fingertips extended thread-like strands of magic glowing purple.

“Dark Magic Fifth Rank: Strings Edge. And Dark Magic Sixth Rank: Marionette Jack.”

As she spoke the words and waved her hand, the purple threads tore through space, severing the Golem’s head. Threads then entangled the Golem’s limbs, and just as another Magic Circle glowed, the thread colors shifted to rainbow hues. But that was all. As the magic threads intensified their glow, they burst apart and scattered.

“Ah, as I thought, it won’t work on your Golems. The magical control is too strong, they get repelled.”

She said this while looking rather pleased.

“Puppet Strings, then.”

“Yes. I need to partially reconfigure the Spell Formula depending on the target, but it can handle most opponents. I’m considering applications too, but I’ll save that demonstration for another time.”

So it’s hard-to-perceive slash attacks from mid-range and manipulation of the opponent’s body. Quite fitting magic for Rosemary, one might say.

That said, Rosemary wants to accompany us into the labyrinth too. She probably has some rust to shake off, and I think the Blazing Fortress would be too Hard right away. Considering the order of Sealed Door releases… having her get accustomed to the labyrinth while warming up in the Magic Light Water Vein seems more appropriate.

Well, going to the labyrinth the day after yesterday’s events feels somewhat rushed. Let’s take it easy today to welcome Rosemary.

Rosemary looked at various items around the house and entertainment room, occasionally nodding as if impressed. Like Miriam, she probably had her own unique perspective and noticed different things.

“Master, Lord Alfred has arrived.”

Around late morning, Cecilia guided Alfred to us. Given yesterday’s incident, he probably came to check on things after hearing Rosemary had come to the house.

“Good afternoon. How are things?”

“Thanks to you, everything’s settled down.”

“–So it seems. As I mentioned on the Communication Device, I’m glad you’re unharmed. What was it like inside the book?”

He glanced at Rosemary playing billiards with Ashley and Marlene, smiling.

“Well, it wasn’t exactly pleasant. Giant silverfish and such – nothing comforting.”

My words seemed to make Alfred imagine the scene, darkening his expression.

“That’s a bit… Their fast movements are hard for me to handle.”

“Right? If I were designing a Spell Formula, I wouldn’t make such a gloomy place.”

“That in itself sounds like it would lead to something outrageous.”

Alfred laughed as he said this.

“By the way, I’d like to request a full equipment set for Rosemary. Is that okay?”

“Taking her into the labyrinth? We have some capacity at the moment.”

“That’s the plan. I think she’s more of a rearguard type… Well, we should consult her preferences too?”

When I looked toward Rosemary, she seemed to have finished her billiards session and came over.

“You’re Albert, right?”

“Yeah. Should I say it’s been a while?”

“Perhaps. It seemed you were discussing equipment – if it’s acceptable, might I make a request of my own?”

“Sure, what is it?”

“I want to create a Magic Doll. A unique piece I can use in the labyrinth. Besides payment, I can provide simple dolls that could serve as labor. What do you think?”

At Rosemary’s proposal, Alfred blinked in surprise. Those must be the ones she used at Anastasia’s mansion.

If it’s a specially made doll, it sounds interesting, and I’d like to be involved in the development too. After all, I have some Magic Stones left over that I haven’t decided how to use.

+++

# **209 – Goddess and Royalty**

Rosemary’s Magic Dolls are a type of Magical Creature. They create a doll’s base body and then house and anchor an intangible Magical Creature—essentially a Spirit—within it.

It’s like pouring a pseudo-soul into the vessel of a doll. Their performance varies immensely. This depends not only on hardware aspects like the quality of the doll’s base body and the materials used, but also on software aspects such as the type of catalyst used in creating the Magical Creature housed within, adjustments to the Spell Formula, and Improvements.

The dolls I fought at Anastasia’s mansion were designed with the philosophy of independence and Coordination between parts, allowing them to compensate for destruction by sharing components among multiple dolls. Even if partially destroyed, intact dolls could immediately combine and continue fighting.

Thanks to that design philosophy, multiple units could link together and operate as a single giant doll. They aimed to achieve both strength as a group and strength as individuals.

This time, we’re creating a one-of-a-kind piece that simply pursues strength as an individual. Apparently, since there were Dragon Fang Soldiers and they could compensate by combining, they postponed making such specialized dolls, but the concept itself had existed for some time.

“I’ll be assembling the doll’s base body, so I’d like you to create the armor,” Rosemary said.

When I offered to assist with development, Rosemary smiled as if she were plotting something mischievous. So, we spread out blueprints on the table in the recreation room and discussed various details.

We’re doing this in the recreation room because my place is filled with people rich in combat experience, and I wanted to hear their opinions as well.

The plan was to prepare some tea and sweets, relax, and proceed with the doll development discussion.

“What about the material?”

“Mithril Silver. We’ll engrave the reverse side with a Spell Formula for structural reinforcement and increased strength, then Enchant it.”

“I see. So, we balance lightness and strength while further supplementing with Magic.”

That certainly sounds like a job for Alfred. The Brightwelt Workshop could create custom-made Armor, and engraving Spell Formulas onto it would be a breeze for them.

“The defense aspect is fine with that… but if we keep the Enchant active, the Magical Creature housed inside might get… winded. If we incorporate a Magic Stone into the base body to supplement that, I think we could make it stronger and more agile.”

“If it’s a matter of mobility, why not incorporate Aerial Combat Gear from the start?” I suggested.

Physical strength, armor, plus mobility and flight capability… Yeah. Being straightforwardly strong is a good thing.

“Incorporating Aerial Combat Gear just involves attaching Magic Tools to various parts, so it’s not much different from what we’ve done before… but in that case, we probably shouldn’t use mediocre Magic Stones for the doll’s base body.”

“In that case, what about a Giant’s Magic Stone?” Grace, who had been listening, suggested.

“A Giant’s Magic Stone? Such a thing exists?”

“Grace took one down at the Blazing Fortress the other day.”

“Such a precious item… are you sure I can use it? I haven’t done anything for you yet.”

“If we can create something good, I believe it will directly contribute to Theo’s safety,” Grace replied.

Upon hearing Grace’s words, Rosemary closed her eyes and smiled gently.

“…That’s true. You’re absolutely right. I’ll use it carefully.”

“Yes.”

According to what Rosemary said yesterday, the residents of this house don’t need to read between the lines, so it’s relatively free of toxicity.

She thought she’d be blamed more since she’d put me in danger twice, so she was somewhat taken aback. Well… the book incident probably wasn’t Rosemary’s fault, and everyone knows she’s been cooperating in various ways.

Although she’s lost her right to the throne and her position is different now, I feel Rosemary’s interactions have softened, likely due to such factors. Grace also isn’t the type who would have been around the Royal Castle—especially around Rosemary.

“—As for me, I’m thinking of using a Flame Demon’s Magic Stone to create a Weapon for the doll.”

“A Weapon?”

“Would that become a Magic Tool? I’d like to ask Alfred to handle that as well.”

“I don’t mind, but I’m endlessly curious about what will come out of this,” Alfred remarked.

Hmm. It might be quicker to create a model with Earth Magic than to explain verbally. Given the doll’s design philosophy, it will likely be deployed as a Vanguard. In that case, something usable in close combat would be best. On top of that, we’ll utilize Fire Magic.

Considering we might challenge the Blazing Fortress, there will likely be more situations where using fire directly isn’t very effective. So, let’s specialize it in physical attacks to gain versatility. Rosemary can handle the magical support aspects.

“Is this… a gauntlet?”

It’s a Weapon resembling Gauntlets with Claws. Its somewhat rugged appearance can’t be helped.

“It can be used as gauntlets. We’ll embed the Magic Stone here, and when using it, hook the claws to secure it, then use Fire Magic to—”

Activating the Gimmick with a light Fire Magic spell causes a pile to shoot out forcefully from the gauntlet. Alfred and Rosemary’s eyes widened.

In essence—it’s a Pile Bunker. Normally, it serves as clawed Gauntlets for offense and Defense, and against larger foes, you drive the pile into them.

“For the pile’s core, we’ll use Valyus Silver to ensure weight. Surround it with Mithril and engrave a Spell Formula so that after driving the pile in, Magic can be activated from within… How about something like this? I think there’s plenty of room for Improvement, so I’ll need to discuss and experiment with Viola as well.”

There’s also the idea of firing it as a projectile, but with ordinary Metal, the power would be unreliable, and Valyus Silver or Mithril Silver are too precious and costly to use as disposable items. Moreover, explicitly developing a gun would have significant repercussions down the line.

In that regard, if it’s a Magic Tool using a rare Magic Stone, analysis would be difficult, and imitation would be hard. Also, since it doesn’t rely on Fighting Spirit or the like, it should be suitable as a doll’s Weapon.

“Activating Magic inside…”

“…It’s amazing you thought of something like this.”

The two of them were intently examining the model I handed them.

“For it to do this with Fire Magic… you’re utilizing the pressure from the blast, right? There’s no risk of the gauntlet itself rupturing?”

“That part uses an application of the Resonance Mine, giving the explosion directionality and concentrating the force to a single point to launch the pile.”

I’ll take charge of writing the Spell Formula, but in any case, we need to experiment first. Since the crucial power output is unknown, it would be problematic if we used a precious Magic Stone to create it, only for it to be too weak to be useful. Before embedding the Magic Stone, we should create just the launching mechanism and test its power.

For now, I have a rough idea of the types and quantities of Materials needed. I also need to have a tailor look at Arachne’s fabric, so let’s plan to go out for supplies another day. For today, we’re planning to relax at home, also serving as Rosemary’s welcome party.

“Speaking of which, you have quite a few unusual servants, don’t you?” Rosemary remarked, tilting her head as she looked at the servants resting in the recreation room after we reached a stopping point. She seemed genuinely curious. It’s probably because she’s meritocratic and doesn’t care about origins.

She hasn’t been told about Claudia’s background yet. She doesn’t know how things came to be this way.

“Ah, that’s—”

“Theodore. I’ll explain,” Claudia said, taking over from me.

Rosemary only knew the part about Claudia and Marlene using a Blessing to nullify the book’s Curse Magic, but given Claudia’s noble demeanor, Rosemary must have been curious.

After Claudia finished explaining her background, Rosemary was truly taken aback and left speechless.

“A contract partner in the Nation Protecting Ceremony… Even though I was unaware, I have acted disrespectfully.”

Rosemary performed a subject’s bow, kneeling on one knee and lowering her head to Claudia without the slightest hesitation. …Well, that makes sense. She’s essentially the one who granted sovereignty to the Verdgar royal family.

“Um… I’d be happier if you treated me normally.”

“If that is your wish. But before doing so, I wished to express my respect.”

“I have duly received your words.”

Upon hearing that, Rosemary stood up. Considering the contents of the Oath Magic, there’s no duplicity or maneuvering in Rosemary’s current words.

Respect. For bearing the responsibility of world regeneration? For subsequently supporting the kingdom for many years as a foundation of the Labyrinth? Even as someone born of the same royal lineage. As a member of the Verdgar royal family. And likely, from Rosemary’s personal meritocratic perspective as well, she must have various thoughts about Claudia.

But still… given this reaction upon learning Claudia’s circumstances, it seems she’ll likely help enthusiastically with analyzing the Labyrinth’s Spell Formula after defeating the Last Guardian too, which is a welcome prospect.

+++

# **210 – Alias or Nickname**

“Welcome.”

The seamstress shop owner greeted me with a smile the moment she saw me enter her store.

“It’s been a while.”

“Not at all. Thank you for your continued patronage.”

This was the tailor shop where I had previously purchased the Lunaworm coat. When I greeted her, she seemed to remember me and bowed politely.

“Long time no see, Daisy.”

“Oh, Miriam. Did you bring something unusual again today?”

As expected of someone who works as a merchant, Miriam certainly has wide connections. When I told her I was thinking of having some fabric examined at this shop, she mentioned being acquainted with the owner Daisy and offered to act as intermediary.

“No, I’m just an extra. Sir Theodore here has something he’d like to show you, Daisy. Sir Theodore, this is Daisy. Though it seems you two are already acquainted.”

“Let me reintroduce myself. My name is Daisy, as per the introduction. Pleased to meet you today.”

“Theodore Gartner. The pleasure is mine. This may be rather abrupt and rude, but I’ve acquired some somewhat unusual fabric and was hoping to get a professional opinion.”

“Not at all. I’m grateful for the opportunity to broaden my knowledge as well. Rather than standing around talking, please have a seat over there.”

I was guided to a table behind the counter.

“This is it.”

I handed Daisy the wooden box containing the fabric.

“Let me take a look.”

She said, opening the wooden box… and the moment she saw it, Daisy’s expression changed.

“…May I touch it?”

“Yes.”

I had brought both the woven fabric and the thread in its bundled form. Daisy, looking somewhat apprehensive, first gently picked up the silver-glittering woven fabric as if handling a fragile work of art.

“This texture—this luster… It’s similar to Lunaworm, but different…”

Daisy took the thread bundle, lightly pulling on the end to test its tension, then looked up with a serious expression to ask:

“What kind of thread is this, exactly?”

“Arachne Thread.”

When I answered, Daisy’s eyes widened. Arachne are apparently few in number, so their thread must be even rarer.

“Actually, I’ve opened a shop in the Eastern District, and we’re considering handling this fabric there. But I’m having trouble determining its value. I’d like to hear your opinion.”

“Th-that means… you can procure it in substantial quantities?”

“Only irregularly for now.”

Daisy gulped, took two or three deep breaths, then answered.

“…Y-yes, I see. Let me preface this by saying this is what I would do… but I think I would price it at five times that of Lunaworm.”

Five times? And that’s already quite a high-quality item.

“Um. While the fabric itself is wonderful… more than anything, it has rarity value. For example, if we were to make a dress from this… I honestly couldn’t even estimate the price. Since we handle Lunaworm here, I can tell—this cloth can be Enchanted too.”

“…I see. And there’s nowhere else selling it…”

“That’s right.”

The quality and novelty are there, but distribution is too limited. Indeed… the nobility and connoisseurs who love new things would jump at it, so as the seller, we could pretty much set whatever price we want.

“…Understood. Then I’ll try stocking it in the shop at the price we discussed earlier.”

“Yes. I think I’ll come inquire when it goes on sale. As a tailor, it’s something I’d like to work with at least once.”

Saying this, Daisy smiled. I had considered having Daisy handle it since the coat I got from this shop was of good quality… but if I were to supply it exclusively, I’d probably earn the resentment of other professionals in the trade.

Daisy seemed to understand that aspect too. That’s probably why she mentioned “when it goes on sale.”

Anyway, I need to announce the sales date to the tailoring district and adopt a sales method that doesn’t create too much friction.

“Though I don’t think there will be that many competitors.”

While I was pondering various things, Miriam spoke up.

“Is that so?”

“I think only shops that can handle Lunaworm to begin with would even consider it. The nobility seek high-quality materials and the latest trends… but they each have their preferences and loyalties.”

I see… If a shop doesn’t already have established noble clientele, even if they purchase at high prices, they might not get the crucial orders, and customers might not be able to afford it anyway. In that case, preparing only what’s needed and supplying it to various shops might be best.

Still. If it can be Enchanted… aside from the fabric, maybe I should ask the Labyrinth Village to provide clothing for the Party members. If worn under Armor and such, it should subtly boost Defense Power.

“Well then, I’ll be heading back now.”

“I can have the carriage take you.”

“No, that won’t be necessary. Don’t you have other places to visit? I’ve left my own shop unattended too.”

So after thanking Daisy and leaving the shop, I parted ways with Miriam.

When I returned to the carriage parked nearby, Grace and the others were enthusiastically styling each other’s hair.

“—Indeed. Claudia-sama’s black hair is lovely.”

“You tend to admire colors different from your own, don’t you?”

“Perhaps.”

I’d seen them doing something similar back at the workshop before… They seem to be having fun. Right now, Marlene is styling Rosemary’s hair into a chignon. Hmm… It seems Marlene and Rosemary have gotten quite close too.

“How did it go?”

Claudia, who was combing Grace’s hair, asked me. Though Claudia herself had her hair in twin tails too.

“About five times Lunaworm’s price, apparently. The quality is good and the rarity value is high, so it’s definitely a High Quality route.”

“I see… I wonder if the girls will be happy when we tell them.”

“I think so. But we should probably tell them not to overdo it. It’s their own thread after all, and if they get too enthusiastic about meeting demand, it could become overwhelming.”

“That’s true. Just spinning and weaving the thread takes considerable time and effort. Apparently, producing too much thread does tire them out.”

Is that so. That might be unexpectedly valuable information.

While exchanging such conversation with Claudia, I sent commands to the Golem driver to head to the next shop. We needed Materials for the Doll, so we were going to an Alchemist’s shop. By the way, regarding Metal Materials for Armor and the Pile Bunker, Alfred said he would handle those.

Not counting the time in the book… this is Rosemary’s first outing in a while. Since she was walking around everywhere in Anastasia’s guise before, this must be quite meaningful for her. As the carriage started moving, she stared intently at the townscape through the window.

Eventually, the carriage arrived at the Alchemist Beatrice’s shop.

“Welcome.”

When I entered the shop with Rosemary, Beatrice greeted us with her usual languid tone.

“I want to make a Magic Doll. May I see your catalysts?”

“They’re on that shelf over there.”

Rosemary went to look around the shelf Beatrice had pointed to.

“Ro—… Marie. Do you have everything you need?”

I almost called her Rosemary but corrected myself, and she looked back at me with a slightly puzzled expression.

“…No, that was too simplistic. Since Alfred does the same, I thought maybe I should change how I address you.”

We’re in disguise right now. Her appearance is different from Anastasia too, so maybe I should have discussed the pseudonym a bit more beforehand.

Rosemary shifted her gaze back toward the shelf and shrugged her shoulders.

“You can keep calling me that from now on. Wouldn’t it be confusing to change how you address me depending on the place?”

…Is that how it works? It doesn’t really feel like a pseudonym since it’s just part of her name extracted.

By the way, regarding the actual product selection, it seemed to be good enough to impress Rosemary. It appeared she had found everything she needed.

Well then. Now I can proceed with Doll Crafting without reservations. Let’s have a Golem modeled after a completed Doll hold a prototype Pile Bunker and conduct various experiments.

+++

# **211 – Knight Doll**

“…It’s hot.”

Some of it was due to the hot air expelled by the Pile Bunker… but the sunlight was quite strong today. While the morning had been cool, I could clearly feel the temperature rising as the sun climbed higher.

Lavigne seemed to dislike the heat, as she was lounging lazily in a cool, shaded spot. Seraphina was also taking refuge from the heat, leaning against Lavigne’s body. The break group seemed quite relaxed. I hoped they would continue their training at a leisurely pace while staying hydrated with shaved ice and carbonated drinks, since I didn’t want anyone getting heatstroke.

Well. Spring was ending, and it was practically summer already.

So what was I doing under this sunlight? I was developing a weapon that utilized Fire Magic. I’d love to be cooling off in the shade too, but given the nature of this project, I had to conduct experiments in a somewhat open area. Therefore, I continued my experiments while using Wind Magic and Water Magic to lower the surrounding temperature.

“Go.”

A square block of stone sat in the workshop’s courtyard. Upon receiving my command, an Earth Golem charged toward it.

On its arm was a crude gauntlet—. As it stepped forward, it drove in a claw like a body blow. As I timed it, a Magic Circle glowed in my hand, and with a blast, a pile was launched.

With that single shot— it punched a fist-sized hole through the stone block and further cracked it entirely with the impact. Well… the power was acceptable. The problem lay elsewhere.

“So, how is it this time?”

Alfred asked. After checking the Golem’s limbs, I answered.

“Seems fine. The adjustments are working well.”

“Wow, releasing a blast backward to cancel the recoil? That’s interesting.”

Alfred sounded impressed. It was the principle of a so-called recoilless gun. Because of that, firing the Pile Bunker had become quite a spectacle. Also, the heat made it pretty hot.

But well, the destructive power matched its appearance, so it could instill Fear in opponents—killing two birds with one stone.

…No. It had been quite a struggle to get to this point. During the initial experiments, the Golem’s arm that fired it would tear off or crack from the launch impact and recoil.

To reduce the recoil, we refined the gauntlet’s Form and tweaked the Spell Formula to adjust the blast’s spread… After numerous minor adjustments and fixes, we finally reached a point where even an Earth Golem could handle it without issues.

The actual Equipment for the Doll would use stronger Materials, so the power should be even greater.

The remaining issue— was ensuring the backblast didn’t catch allies in the blast.

For now, I was considering deploying a Shield to the rear to divert the blast upward, but that wasn’t finalized yet.

In any case, let’s consider the Pile Bunker itself complete for the time being.

“So, this Form is finalized. Next, we’ll need to fit it to the Doll’s arm.”

“Understood. I’ll take it to Viola.”

“Yeah. I’ll come too. I need to write down the Spell Formula on paper.”

Carrying the Pile Bunker, we moved inside the workshop.

“By the way, how’s the Armor adjustment going?”

We were engraving Spell Formulas into the Doll’s Mithril Armor— the Armor— to increase its strength, but balancing it with the output of the Giant’s Magic Stone required a lot of adjustments.

“Well, the Giant’s Magic Stone is quite impressive. I think we managed to enhance it significantly more than initially planned. Now it’s just a matter of where to prioritize… but I think we’ve reached a good balance.”

Where to prioritize. In other words, balance adjustment.

If we increased the strength too much, Magical Power consumption would become severe.

Should we prioritize thicker Defense even if it meant becoming more easily winded, or reduce strength to preserve stamina longer? We needed to fine-tune that distribution.

From Alfred’s tone, it seemed they were currently aiming for a balanced type. Since the optimal solution wouldn’t be clear without actual use, I thought that was correct.

“Ah, perfect timing.”

In one room of the workshop were Rosemary and Viola, along with the form of a reclining Doll. Noticing us, Rosemary smiled and said that.

“Perfect timing for what?”

When I asked, Rosemary answered while touching the Doll’s chest.

“We’re about to activate it. I’m looking forward to it.”

…Oh ho. In that case, I should call everyone training outside.

The Doll— had the appearance of a Knight clad in full Armor.

Apparently, appearance was important for Magic Dolls. If we wanted it to serve a Vanguard role, it needed to look the part.

Combined with its height of about 2 meters, it emitted considerable intimidation even while lying down.

If we solely sought the Pile Bunker’s power, making it larger would have been fine, but considering delving into Labyrinths and keeping it at home, this was probably the limit.

Besides, at this size, it could just barely pass as a burly Knight. By mixing in movements impossible for humans, it could exploit openings.

“Awaken.”

As everyone watched with bated breath, Rosemary deployed a Magic Circle at her fingertip. She then touched the Knight Puppet’s chest. From there, a ripple spread as the glow of Magical Power propagated throughout the Doll’s entire body.

At first, its movements were clumsy. After standing up, they became smooth. The Knight Puppet respectfully knelt before Rosemary.

“It seems good.”

Rosemary nodded contentedly, hiding her mouth behind a folding fan as she laughed. Somehow, perhaps because she was originally a Princess, she carried herself perfectly while commanding a Knight.

But, a Vanguard, huh. So this would charge into enemy lines alongside Grace and Dullahan?… Imagining it was quite something.

“…Ah, I thought of something.”

“What is it?”

“Nothing. I just thought, since it’s Knight-style anyway, we could use a Mantle for blast countermeasures. We could weave a Mantle from Arachne Thread and Enchant it with Water Magic to draw away heat.”

“That might also work as a countermeasure against the Blazing Fortress.”

“Hopefully. Also, since the Pile Bunker is finalized, I’d like you to adjust its size to fit this Form.”

“Understood.”

As I placed the experimental Pile Bunker on the table, Viola nodded.

“Is the Pile Bunker’s appearance acceptable like this? I tried to match it to the Doll, but due to adjustment considerations, some details have changed slightly.”

Specifically, the shape of the part that vented the blast backward.

“I think it’s fine.”

After comparing the Pile Bunker and the Doll alternately, Rosemary nodded.

“Then… this is mostly settled.”

“What about a name? Calling it ‘the Doll’ forever…”

Grace tilted her head. When I looked at Rosemary upon hearing those words, she made a somewhat subtle expression.

“I’m not good at thinking up names like this. Could I ask you to do it?”

She passed the task to me like that. Hmm. What to do.

“…Hmm. How about Ignis?”

After thinking a bit, I answered. I believe it meant flame.

“Decided. From today, your name is Ignis.”

Rosemary lightly tapped the Doll’s Armor as if knocking. The addressed Doll placed a hand on its hip and bowed.

“Now that we’ve reached a milestone… there’s one thing I’d like to ask.”

Turning around, Rosemary said.

“What is it?”

“I want to apologize to Count Gartner. Because of my scheme, I caused him a great deal of trouble.”

…Ah. To Father. That was probably something best done in person. It wasn’t the kind of thing to handle over a Communication Device.

But, Gartner County, huh. It wasn’t a place I particularly wanted to go… but if it’s around Mother’s house… well, fine.

“Yeah. We’ve been busy with Doll development lately, so maybe a group outing would be nice. Lindwurm would probably be happy too.”

It’s been hot recently, so it could double as a summer retreat. There’s a lake in the forest, so relaxing there wouldn’t be bad either.

+++

# **212 – Homecoming in Summer**

“Then, Master. Please take care on your journey.”

We prepared for the homecoming by unloading the dragon palanquin in front of the house and loading luggage. As we finished most of the preparations, Cecilia and Mihaela bowed their heads.

“Yeah. Mihaela-san, are you sure you want to stay behind?”

I thought she might want to see Father after so long.

“I believe I’ll be able to meet Henry-sama around autumn. I have my own duties to attend to,” Mihaela replied quietly, placing a hand on her chest. I see. If staying behind with Cecilia is part of her work, then I should respect that.

For home security, several of Rosemary’s simple dolls were deployed, along with nighttime alarm devices and the labyrinth village residents undergoing self-defense training – our home’s security system was quite substantial.

While nothing major was likely to happen, even if something did occur, as long as we had communication device contact, Claudia’s teleportation magic could bring us back immediately.

“Well then, I’ll be off for a bit.”

“I think the Pile Bunker will be completed by the time Theo-kun and the others return.”

“Right. If any problems come up, use the communication device as usual.”

“Understood.”

After exchanging such conversation with Alfred and Viola who came to see us off, I boarded the dragon palanquin. Marlene leaned out the window and waved to her brother. Alfred also smiled and waved back at Marlene.

Inside the palanquin, Irmhild immediately began playing her lute. Next to her, Sheila was moving her hands slightly to keep rhythm, perhaps doing image training.

…Now then. For this homecoming, including me, we had nine party members plus three familiars and one doll – quite a large group. The dragon palanquin had expanded from three dragons to four, becoming even more massive.

The three familiars were Caduceus and Lavigne, plus Rosemary’s doppelganger familiar, Ambrum.

Before transformation, he had a semi-transparent body like agar, with a human silhouette but no eyes, nose, or mouth. With his glossy, oddly rounded appearance, whether he looked charming or eerie depended on the person.

He had the ability to take the same appearance as someone when given their blood, which Rosemary had used to create shadow clones and sneak out into town using hidden passages.

After the incident, he was kept under royal castle supervision as evidence, but like the forbidden library books, I was allowed to take custody of him.

He was useful, but his low combat ability was a drawback. Taking him into the labyrinth would be impossible. The fact that we had to prepare clothes for him was also a minor problem. Currently he was wearing servant’s clothes.

“…What about Countess Gartner and her eldest son Byron? I don’t quite know what to say to the Count without knowing their current situation,” Rosemary asked, perhaps reminded of the incident when she saw me looking at Ambrum.

“They’re under house arrest with surveillance. Even without what happened with Marie, they’d done various things that would have led to the same outcome if discovered. So I don’t think you need to worry too much about their treatment.”

“I see.”

At my response, Rosemary showed a thoughtful expression.

Kathryn had been connected to the former Marquis Broderick behind the scenes and had done various things, and apparently Byron knew about it too. Perhaps he thought that after inheriting the family, he could team up with the former Marquis and reap benefits… but in that case, I suspect both families would have fallen together.

Regarding the second son Daryl, it seems Father is educating him quite strictly, so I’ll reserve judgment for now.

Still, Rosemary seems somewhat nervous. Certainly, even when trying to settle things, there are many matters that can’t be revealed, and she probably wants to at least handle things properly with Father.

Well, that’s that. No need to stay tense from now on. When my eyes met Ashley’s, she nodded quietly.

“Marie-sama. Would you like to play cards with us?” Ashley invited Rosemary to play. Rosemary showed a slightly surprised expression but smiled wryly and nodded.

We landed the dragon palanquin in front of Mother’s house. After carrying in luggage like clothes and food, we’d change clothes first before visiting the grave.

“It’s a beautiful place. Like the house earlier, it’s quite mysterious.”

“This was Lisa-sama’s favorite place,” Grace answered Rosemary’s comment with a somewhat lonely smile.

Colorful flowers bloomed around Mother’s grave. A flower garden dyed red by the sunset. A path had been made from Mother’s house.

Harold and Cynthia, who tended the grave, seemed to be doing their work quite thoroughly. You could see how well-maintained it was.

“Long time no see.”

“Good afternoon.”

Harold and Cynthia came to greet us. I had told Father I was coming back, so it seemed they were both waiting for us.

“Yeah. Long time no see, both of you. Thank you.”

“Not at all. This is our job. The Count visited around noon today,” Harold answered with a polite bow. A bouquet was placed at the grave. Father must have brought this. I too… placed the bouquet I brought.

I’m supposed to meet Father tomorrow evening… He’s a busy person, so scheduling must be difficult. Since we’re officially distant, even meeting requires various arrangements.

“I’m home, Mother.”

“Long time no see, Lisa-sama.”

Grace pressed her ring and closed her eyes before Mother’s grave.

Everyone else followed suit, closing their eyes in silent prayer.

After a while of this… I opened my eyes and spoke to Harold and the others.

“You two, would you like to stay for dinner?”

“…Is that alright?”

“Yeah. Even if you return to town now and prepare, dinner would be late. You’re welcome to stay overnight too.”

“I… I’ve wanted to enter that house once,” Cynthia said with a happy smile. Good. I’m glad she likes Mother’s house too.

“Speaking of which – there’s something that’s been bothering me a bit,” Harold said while we were talking about recent conditions in the county after dinner.

“What?”

“Well. Today we were brought to the grave by the Count’s carriage… While waiting in front of the mansion, I saw someone watching us from the shadows. That person was… um…”

Harold hesitated. This… doesn’t sound very good.

“They looked like someone who used to work at the mansion before. I hadn’t seen them recently and was wondering what happened to them…”

I couldn’t help but exchange looks with Grace.

Someone who used to work at the mansion and disappeared… Could they be among the servants Kathryn brought from the Marquis household?

“Have you told Father about this yet?”

“No, not yet. I was talking with Cynthia and realized, you could say. They were wearing a hood so I didn’t notice at the time…”

“So Cynthia saw them too?”

When I asked, Cynthia shook her head. “I didn’t see them then.”

“I saw them in a different place. They weren’t wearing a hood then. But they were with unfamiliar people in town, so I remembered well. When Harold told his story, I noticed they were wearing the same colored coat… so then.”

I see… Harold and Cynthia probably don’t know the details of the Count’s household situation. They likely don’t know why they were dismissed.

This is probably information Father should hear.

It’s hard to imagine Kathryn or Byron being behind this. I don’t think they left any room for external manipulation, and Father would be most cautious about that area.

So then… the former servants of the Count household acting on their own. Planning to reclaim something, resentment over being fired… there are several possible reasons.

Still… what should we do?

This time, with Claudia accompanying us, we can teleport to Termwills immediately in an emergency, and we originally planned to stay here for several days. Maybe I should check on Kathryn’s movements.

+++

# **213 – Express**

“—Go.”

After giving the command to Caduceus, he liquefied from his cat form and slipped out through the gap beneath the door. I had sent him to guard Father. Then, I contacted Father via the communication device.

“Information from Harold and Cynthia. It seems the former servant Godwin has been loitering around the Count’s estate. He was also witnessed with unfamiliar individuals, so caution may be necessary.”

“Understood. I’ll conduct some investigation on my end as well.”

After a short while, that message came back from Father. Godwin was a servant Kathryn had called over from the Marquis’ household.

We had identified him as likely being Godwin by having Harold and Cynthia match the facial features against a clay model of the servant’s face I’d made.

“What kind of person is this Godwin?”

“In my opinion… I don’t believe he’s an honest individual. It seems he would harass servants who didn’t conform to their ways until they quit.”

“…That figures.”

“Are you alright, Grace-sama?”

Rosemary and Ashley frowned. When Marlene went to Grace’s side with a worried expression, Grace smiled back at her and took her hand.

“I’m… a Dhampir. Since there were aspects that frightened people, I didn’t experience much direct harassment.”

“I see… So that’s the kind of person he is.”

Claudia let out a small sigh.

…I’ve heard people complaining about how a monster was staying at the Count’s household when Grace wasn’t around. Even if they didn’t harass her directly, they certainly wouldn’t be kind to her.

Still, the problem lies more with the unfamiliar individuals he was reportedly with than with Godwin himself. Possibility of collusion. Or possibility of being manipulated into running errands. We should consider all these possibilities.

“I’ve memorized his face. Can I move out too?”

Sheila, who had been glaring at Godwin’s bust with half-closed eyes, asked this.

“What are you planning to do?”

“Places where unfamiliar people are holed up—I think we can identify them with a bit of questioning. Godwin doesn’t know my face either, so it’s quite advantageous.”

“If Sheila’s going, I’m going too.”

Irmhild stood up.

“…Understood. Move in pairs and make regular contact via the communication device. If you’re discovered by the other side, don’t hesitate to fly away and disengage. Just that alone should serve as a deterrent against reckless actions.”

“Right. We’ll just identify the location. We won’t push ourselves.”

Since both of them excel at detection abilities, there shouldn’t be any worry about being surrounded.

Now then—Caduceus seems to have stuck to Father as planned. Father decided to go out by carriage with accompanying knights… but where is he heading?

…Given the timing of his departure, is it to the annex where Kathryn is?

I heard that to eliminate her influence on Daryl, she’s been confined to a separate residence from the main house. They’re being careful with servant selection too, and even for purchasing supplies, they’re accompanied and required to submit detailed expenditure reports.

Father, having alighted from the carriage, left his accompanying knights there, had the guards open the tall iron-gated entrance, and headed toward the house through the front garden where flowers were blooming.

Though it’s called the Count’s annex, it’s not a particularly large mansion. It’s about the size of a slightly large commoner’s house, but compared to its scale, it has high walls… and inside those walls, there’s a front garden with a gazebo.

Compared to the house and front garden’s appearance, the walls feel relatively new, as if they were built later. Whether it’s for confinement or seclusion… at any rate, it certainly functions as an isolated prison from the outside world.

“The master has arrived.”

The servant who came to greet him bowed respectfully to Father before withdrawing to the adjacent room.

“What brings you here at this late hour?”

Kathryn, who seemed to have been embroidering on a tapestry, asked this with a somewhat perplexed expression.

“I came to talk a little. Has anything unusual happened recently?”

He probably brought them from his study. He placed several books on the table. They were books of genres like fairy tales and stories.

“Aside from your coming at this hour, everything is as usual. Did you bring books instead of embroidery thread today?”

Father stared intently at Kathryn, but eventually nodded quietly.

“I see.”

Kathryn furrowed her brows and spoke.

“About Byron… couldn’t you release him from his cell?”

“That’s impossible. He tried to escape from this house, and he was voicing his dissatisfaction about Daryl becoming the heir.”

“I… see. If you’re going to this much trouble, you might as well dispose of us all at once. Or… do you think I would be

bound

by something like this?”

“That’s not it. You’re Daryl’s mother, and my wife. I believe I share responsibility for what you and Byron did. That’s precisely why I won’t casually discard you.”

“You still call me your wife?”

At Father’s words, Kathryn laughed self-deprecatingly. Her laughter lacked much strength.

…Somehow. I feel the impression is quite different from before. Well… judging from what I see, the judgment Father handed down feels like a lenient verdict, so perhaps with time and calming down, she’s had various thoughts.

“As long as there might be those who would try to carry you off, I cannot grant you freedom. As the lord, I must definitely draw a line there… but speaking solely of the relationship between you and me, I wish to rebuild it anew. If my presence is bothersome, I’ll try not to come as much as possible.”

“You may… do as you please. You are the lord, after all.”

Kathryn looked up briefly but answered indifferently.

“I see. Then I shall take my leave for today.”

As Father stood up, Kathryn started to reach out toward his back but ultimately withdrew her hand and shook her head.

“…I’ll see you to the gate.”

“Right.”

But Kathryn didn’t move until Father had left.

After Father left the house and the door closed momentarily, Kathryn muttered to herself. Caduceus, slipping out through the door gap, heard Kathryn’s murmur that should never have reached anyone.

“Apologizing now… what will that accomplish? Even if you forgive me… Lisa and her son won’t forgive what I’ve done. Is that… acceptable?”

So Kathryn doesn’t know that Father and I have reconciled. Since it’s being kept secret, if asked, Father would likely only say we’re estranged.

It doesn’t matter. I don’t feel strongly about Kathryn one way or the other.

You could even say I don’t care. Once I gained power and left the household, it became part of the past. I don’t expect apologies or revenge. It’s indifference—as long as we don’t get involved, that’s fine.

But Mother probably… no, if she could hear words of apology, she would surely forgive Kathryn. That’s the kind of person she is.

I shake my head and switch my thinking. At the very least… it seems there’s no connection between Kathryn and Godwin.

Kathryn followed after Father and came out of the house. Suddenly—the sound of someone collapsing could be heard.

Father and Kathryn looked up and saw.

Smoke was billowing at the gate, and the gatekeepers and accompanying knights were collapsing as if their strings had been cut—.

“Sleep Cloud!?”

The moment I confirmed that scene, I stood up and gripped Ouroboros.

“Wh-what happened?”

At my demeanor, tension ran through everyone. Before leaving the house, I need to have Grace’s Cursed Tool in its Released Form.

“Father’s being attacked. I’m heading to the scene immediately. Everyone else, stand by here!”

“Understood!”

As I rushed out of the house, I pondered.

Indeed, even with the watch soldiers and accompanying knights—it was the minimum personnel. Is that why? Thinking they could force it now if they had a Magician?

They investigated Father’s movements and lifestyle patterns, and calculated that with the reduced personnel now, they could launch an attack?

Then, for what purpose? What’s the target? They’ve even mobilized a Magician. If it were just a resentful former servant or a rescue attempt, the quality of the personnel involved doesn’t make sense. Among those connected to the former Marquis Broderick who’s lost power, is there someone who could pull such strings? Even if there were, would there be reason to try to rescue Kathryn while leaving the former Marquis behind?

Or perhaps… it’s a different group. For example—involving Silvatoria.

Questions remain, but I ride Lindwurm and rush to the scene at top speed. Meanwhile, Caduceus continues to relay the situation there to me.

Whether Father and Kathryn understood the situation at the entrance, their eyes widened.

“Is that Water Magic!?”

“Da-damn, tricky!? Re-regardless, get inside the house!”

“That would leave us with no escape route!”

“B-but…! Even if we stay in this garden…!”

At Father’s words, Kathryn frantically scanned her surroundings as if seeking an escape route, then froze.

I follow her gaze. On a thick branch of a tree higher than the wall. There was a man dressed entirely in black with an arrow nocked to his Bow, aiming directly at Father.

The arrow was being drawn to be released. Seeing this, Kathryn—pushed Father aside and stepped forward, spreading her hands as if to block the way.

“I… I…!?”

Kathryn’s expression showed she was astonished by her own actions. By then, the arrow had already been released—flying straight toward Kathryn’s chest.

Bracing for the impending impact, Kathryn tightly closed her eyes. But—the arrow was Deflected in a different direction. Caduceus had knocked it away. It happened in an instant. Whether the Marksman saw it in the darkness of night. He widened his eyes and nocked another arrow.

But.

“Don’t think there’ll be a next time!”

From directly above.

I jumped down from Lindwurm’s back and Charged.

Expanding Shield to the front. Breaking both branches and trunk while engulfing the assassin. Falling straight down to the ground as if to Smash him. The sound and sensation of bones cracking and breaking. Another one! The Magician who used Water Magic!

Using the crushed man as a stepping stone, I leaped up while employing Levitation. Closing in on the Magician in black Robe on the commoner house’s roof. Swinging Ouroboros while Charging.

The enemy also used Levitation to Jump and disengage. With just that… do they think they can escape?

I’ll make them properly repay the courtesy of their pointless interference.

Lindwurm, having circled around from behind, body-slammed with his massive frame and sent the Magician flying back toward me.

“Whoaah!?”

He screamed and deployed a Shield but—.

“Sink.”

I drove a Palm Strike directly from the front. The Magical Power shock transmitted through the Shield captured the Magician’s head. Spinning him once in the air. As he rolled his eyes white, Lindwurm flew in and bit his leg, capturing him.

+++

# **214 – At the Count's Mansion**

I applied Sealing Techniques to both the Marksman and the Magician to prohibit their use of Magic, then restrained them by hardening the ground with Earth Magic. I don’t know if the Marksman can use Magic, but I did it just to be safe.

I’ll deal with their punishment later. First, I used Levitation to move the unconscious gatekeeper and Knights inside the wall. I notified everyone via the Communication Device that the enemies had been subdued.

Then I landed in the courtyard with Lindwurm and greeted Father.

“It’s been a while, Father.”

“Theo… You came to help me?”

“Forgive my presumption, but I obtained information about suspicious individuals and have been keeping watch over your safety. Are either of you injured?”

“I’m… fine. Kathryn, you…”

Father was holding Kathryn’s shoulder as she trembled with a pale face, speaking to her about something. Kathryn nodded, and Father looked at me and said.

“She seems to be alright. Are you okay? It looked like you jumped off the Wyvern’s back…”

“I’m fine as well.”

At any rate, I’m glad neither of you seems to be hurt. Scanning the area, I spotted the fired arrows lying on the ground. I collected them as evidence.

…Something’s coated on the arrowheads. Poison, perhaps? Judging from the angle and trajectory, the arrow aimed at Father was targeting around his shoulder area…

If it’s poison, it would be a surefire assassination attempt. If it’s something like a sleeping drug or paralytic, then this was likely an attempted kidnapping. If we can identify the type of poison, we might be able to determine whether it was meant for murder or abduction.

“…Why… would you… for someone like me…”

Kathryn looked stunned. She had clearly seen the arrow being fired, so she seemed to have realized that I was the reason it unnaturally veered off course.

“Because I wanted to protect Father.”

“Th-that was just… instinctive…”

“That’s not an issue.”

Even if it was an action she herself didn’t expect… that precisely means her concern for Father’s safety outweighed her own self-preservation, and that there truly is affection for Father within her.

“I… I… after treating you so… terribly… I… to you…”

She trailed off, bowing her head.

Kathryn seemed to want to apologize to me… but not out of pride—rather, she appeared unable to form the words due to a childlike weakness, as if afraid of being scolded.

…That’s right. Kathryn is surely weak. That’s precisely why she couldn’t resist the interference from the former Marquis Broderick. There might be other factors too, but her awareness that she’s betraying Father has distorted their relationship.

Certainly, I suffered because of that weakness too. So from my position, I won’t defend her now, but neither will I condemn her.

“Please consider not betraying Father’s kindness and trust as your apology to me. I choose to believe in your earlier action of protecting Father.”

When I told her this, Kathryn bowed her head, tears streaming down, but nodded and clearly spoke.

“…I’m… sorry.”

“…I accept those words as well.”

But let’s leave this matter here for now.

Since the situation isn’t yet resolved, I need to switch gears.

“First, let’s move to the mansion. We don’t know the enemy’s objective. It would be best to bring the personnel here along too. I’ll provide escort to the mansion.”

Leaving Kathryn here as she is would be problematic. More importantly, Harold and Cynthia are still in my care. First, I’ll contact everyone via the Communication Device and arrange to gather at Father’s house.

“…I’m sorry, Theo.”

“Not at all.”

“Please use this room. If you need anything, have the servants prepare it.”

“Yes.”

We headed to Father’s mansion. I was shown to the parlor and had to wait a while until everyone arrived. I sat facing Father, drinking tea while we waited.

“I’d heard various rumors… but your movements earlier surprised me. As your father, I don’t want you taking too many risks.”

Come to think of it, this was the first time Father had seen me fight.

“Thank you for your concern. However, for this matter, could you leave it to me and coordinate the soldiers’ movements? I want to capture all the enemies without any casualties on our side.”

If we mobilize the soldiers, the personnel movements would inevitably become hectic, and the fact that their comrades were captured around Kathryn’s house would also be revealed to the enemy.

And more than anything, I won’t be satisfied until I’ve thoroughly crushed those who dared to pull such a ridiculous stunt with my own hands.

“Do you have some leads?”

“Our comrades are gathering information to locate the enemy’s hideout.”

There were regular communications from Sheila and Irmhild via the Communication Device too. I’ll trust that they’ll deliver results.

“…You work quickly. It hasn’t been long since you contacted me.”

Then Father bowed his head to me.

“At any rate, you saved us. Not just me, but… regarding Kathryn too, I must properly thank you.”

“Not at all.”

“And not just for this incident. I must have some softness as a lord. Because of that, I’ve caused you hardship.”

Soft… huh. Perhaps that’s true. But Mother described it with different words.

“No, that’s—”

Just as I started to say that, a knock sounded at the door.

It seemed the servant had brought Grace and the others. I see. Well then, let’s leave this conversation here. I’ll save what I want to tell Father for after the incident is resolved.

“It’s been a long time, Henry-sama.”

“It’s been a while.”

“Indeed. It’s good to see you’re well, Grace. Ashley-sama, you look unchanged as well…. But to have so many distinguished guests arrive at once… Under normal circumstances, I would be in a position to offer my utmost hospitality, but…”

Yeah. Looking at the assembled group, I understood that hosting—or rather, proper reception—would be difficult.

Grace is a Knight, and Ashley is also a lord. Marlene and Rosemary have their own circumstances, but royalty is royalty.

So we had planned to visit Father’s place a day later to avoid causing a commotion, but with this unforeseen situation forcing us to gather, it’s only natural that preparations aren’t complete.

Well, this isn’t the time for such formalities. Still, from Father’s position, he can’t be discourteous.

“We appreciate the Count’s consideration. However, this is an emergency. Moreover, I have already lost my right to the throne.”

Rosemary said quietly and bowed. Marlene, for her part, picked up the hem of her skirt in greeting and smiled.

“As for me… once this matter is concluded, I must offer my apologies to the Count.”

“To me—no, I understand. Let’s set that matter aside for now.”

After brief greetings to Father and introductions to those meeting for the first time, we moved on to countermeasures.

Rosemary’s apology to Father would have to wait, but with thieves hiding in the territory and having made their move like this, we need to act quickly. That can’t be helped.

“Marie. Can you tell what this is?”

I laid out the Marksman’s belongings on the table and brought forward several small bottles containing chemicals and the actual fired arrows.

Rosemary examined the arrowheads and the Marksman’s possessions. She wafted the scent from the chemicals adhering to the arrowheads and those filling the small bottles.

“…From this smell, and judging by the types of antidotes… this appears to be some kind of paralytic. This bottle here… might be a sleeping drug.”

“A paralytic and a sleeping drug… So the objective isn’t assassination but kidnapping?”

“In that case… could it be for ransom? Or perhaps…”

Ashley frowned.

“I don’t know. Neither the Marksman’s sniping skills nor the Magician’s movements were bad, I think. They should have plenty of legitimate ways to make a living without crossing such a dangerous bridge.”

Kidnapping for ransom. I wouldn’t say it’s impossible, but it feels somewhat unsatisfying. I suspect there might be another reason.

“I also considered the possibility of it being related to Silvatoria. While sending a Thief group could be part of sabotage operations, if they’re attempting a kidnapping in Gartner County with such small numbers—”

—Don’t tell me. Could this be related to Mother? If there’s something connecting Gartner County and Silvatoria, that would be the only link. If Mother’s something-or-other is the target, it wouldn’t be strange for them to think Father knows about it.

But my various speculations had to end there. Because a communication came through the device.

‘Enemy hideout discovered.’

From Sheila and the others. They really do good work. I informed everyone of the communication’s content, we exchanged looks, and nodded. We can extract information from those guys and do all sorts of speculations later, after we’ve crushed them.

+++

# **215 – The Hunting Town**

“I’m off now.”

“Hmm…”

Father looked rather worried, but he seemed to accept it since there were many magicians in our group. Ignis and Dullahan were particularly convincing. I’d also shown him me fighting beforehand, which probably helped.

Count Gartner’s mansion had a decent number of personnel and heightened security, making it less likely to be attacked, but I left Caduceus and Lavigne behind as defense.

“Be careful, Theodore.”

“Yeah. I’ll be back.”

I nodded at Claudia. She would serve more as an emergency evacuation role via teleportation to Termwills rather than base defense.

Ambrum wasn’t a combatant either, so I had him stay at the mansion. Being able to monitor our situation with three familiars would make quite a difference.

I left the Count’s mansion with everyone and traveled through the Count’s territory. Since it was midnight, there were already few people coming and going.

…Well, I wouldn’t want to walk around during the day either. I don’t particularly want to meet the residents face-to-face.

Grace was looking at me with a somewhat worried expression, but when I told her I’d be fine and smiled back, she also smiled quietly and nodded.

“Sorry to keep you waiting.”

“Mhm.”

When I headed to the town square where we’d arranged to meet, Sheila and Irmhild were waiting.

“It seems they’re using an inn near the gate as their base. Godwin appears to be staying there too.”

“That would be convenient for escaping if something happens. The stables are nearby too, so they might be considering stealing horses.”

The outskirts of town, huh? An inn is somewhat troublesome. They might take other guests hostage, so completely trapping them like with Randolph would be problematic.

“What will you do?”

“Block key points, flush them out and corner them.”

If they’ve set up base in a logical location, that means they plan to escape as expected if attacked. The optimal solution naturally narrows down. I know more about the Count’s territory than they do. No way I’m letting them escape.

I created a model of the district using Earth Magic and explained it to everyone.

“Here and here. Also, block the entrance to this alley with earth walls or ice.”

“Then let’s split up and block them.”

I nodded at Ashley’s words.

“What about opponents trying to escape by flying?”

“There’s a difference in mobility. It would require sorting out the magicians, and if they have proper situational judgment, I think they’d give up on escaping by air after we shoot down a few. If they still don’t stop, I’ll blow them all away with a tornado. Now, about how to conduct the assault—”

Ashley, Rosemary, and I split up to quickly create walls in alleys that could serve as escape routes and block them. Once the blockade was complete, all that remained was attacking the base. We approached the inn where they were hiding, confirmed that everyone was in position, and began the operation.

“Alright then, Seraphina. I’m counting on you.”

“Okay. Leave it to me.”

Standing at the inn’s entrance, I mass-produced Golems. Then I had Seraphina amplify my voice volume and shouted.

“To Godwin and his gang! You are under arrest on suspicion of plotting to kidnap Count Gartner! Surrender peacefully and all will be well! Otherwise, we will show no mercy!”

After shouting that, I sent the Golems charging into the inn. Assigning one Golem per guest room, they roughly knocked on the doors, and the gang burst through the windows out into the street. Well, the flushing out was complete.

Their response showed no hesitation whatsoever. Their movements indicated they had anticipated the situation being discovered. I myself jumped out into the street after the escaping gang and looked back at the inn.

“Th, Theodore…?”

Godwin was—still inside the inn. Unable to keep up with his companions’ movements and the situation’s development, he looked out the window with a dumbfounded expression.

“Go.”

“W, whoaaa!?”

I made the Golem step into the room. Capturing the screaming Godwin, I embedded him into the Earth Golem so he couldn’t move. I’d get the story from Godwin later. More importantly, his companions.

I created a spear wall with Golems and advanced, herding them. At the forefront of the Golem advance were Ignis and Dullahan. Residents who stuck their heads out to see what was happening quickly closed and locked their doors in panic, while Godwin’s companions fled with terrified expressions.

“What is this!? Th, there’s no path!?”

“W, walls—Earth Magic!?”

The group turned into an alley, heading for the stables, then stopped. Unfortunately, their escape routes were anticipated. I prepared easy escape paths, but they were all within my control. They probably knew that too. They’d struggle to escape before being checkmated… but well, that’s also pointless.

“Break this magic! Hurry!”

“I’ve been trying! Their interference power is stronger…! They’re suppressing it from the other side of this wall! Damn it!”

“Just climb over and take out the magician, damn it!”

As expected, there seemed to be a magician mixed in, as one tried to use Levitation to get over the wall from above… but after being knocked away by Marlene’s Saucer, they became the target of Irmhild’s Light Arrow. The magician who was shot down received Ignis’s literal iron fist and had their consciousness harvested without any chance to speak.

Even if they managed to avoid Marlene and Irmhild’s initial attacks… Sheila and Lindwurm were waiting in the air. Furthermore, Marlene’s illusion magic tool was inflating the number of wyverns flying in the sky. It should be enough to make them give up, seeing that escaping from above was impossible.

We firmly controlled air superiority. Not a single one would escape.

“Don’t fly! You’ll be targeted!”

“It’s no use! Escape that way!”

“Earth walls have been created! That alley!”

“The waterway! There was a waterway, right!? If we jump into that and swim to escape—!”

“Damn it! It’s frozen! What is this!?”

At this point, they were like sheep chased by dogs. They could only be herded as a group toward the unblocked paths. Since the route was predetermined and we controlled the air, we could easily get ahead of them.

Some tried to break into houses, but that was also anticipated. Their actions were blocked by Marlene’s remote Shield while she waited above, and then they had both arms and legs pierced by Irmhild’s arrows. It’s not like we had extra hands either… but we made sure to crush only those who strayed from the prepared course.

Eventually, Marlene’s illusions even created fake windows and doors. Those who tried to open the phantom doors ended up rubbing against walls or performing useless actions, only to be caught up by Ignis and crushed.

That’s right. I only prepared two choices: escape along the prepared path, or stand and fight. So stop doing unnecessary things and move along quickly. Otherwise, prepare yourself.

Their movements weren’t bad. Not bad, but retreat battles are difficult.

You can’t simultaneously escape and fight, and even if you tried to leave a rearguard, the Golems made it many against few. Moreover, since our goal was to capture them and extract information, having a rearguard was meaningless in the first place.

The place where they were finally cornered was a slightly open area at the edge of town. Surrounded by towering walls of earth and ice that complemented the town’s outer walls, it was a dead end with nowhere to escape.

Ashley constructed a Defense Field at the only exit. Ice walls formed a ceiling. There. Now—completely enclosed.

“This is the end. Resist if you like. Even if you surrender without resistance, considering there are magicians among you, I’ll harvest everyone’s consciousness thoroughly.”

I faced the group and declared while holding Ouroboros at the ready.

“Y, you…! Do you think this is some kind of fox hunt!? How far will you mock us!?”

One of them glared at me and spat out those words bitterly.

…Mockery, he says. As if such people who resort to kidnapping have any pride to speak of.

There’s no need to exchange any more words with these people. Spark Light of magical power scattering, I opened my eyes wide, bared my teeth, and laughed.

The man’s face twisted in astonishment at the amount of excess magical power being emitted. I charged straight in, swinging Ouroboros overhead. But that movement itself was a feint. The moment he tried to block it, he took Capella’s headbutt full force and was sent flying.

As I stepped forward, Grace and the others also moved.

“I think it would be better not to try blocking carelessly.”

Grace casually threw a kick. An acceleration and destructive power unimaginable from such a casual, small movement. A man who misjudged and failed to block had his arm broken and was screaming.

Ashley’s Sleep Cloud spread, crawling along the ground, stealing the consciousness of the man who’d been knocked down.

“Y, you witch!”

Another man tried to throw a knife at Grace—but just before releasing it from his hand, his body turned in an unexpected direction, and he threw it toward his companion’s back. With a throwing knife in his back and fallen, the sleep cloud gathering at his feet ensured he wouldn’t get up again.

Entwining around the stunned man’s limbs were rainbow-colored threads of magical power. Floating above was Rosemary. Hiding her mouth behind her feather fan, her shoulders shaking as she laughed merrily.

“Bayle!?”

“I, it wasn’t me! It wasn’t me!”

The man called Bayle, unable to comprehend the situation, was controlled and attacked his companions. Dullahan charged in and sent them flying together with the man who had blocked the dagger.

Ignis dealt with the magician. With ridiculously high defensive capability, it scattered various spells, charged straight in, and drove a fist into the magician’s stomach. The magician bent double, scattering stomach fluids, writhing on the ground.

Shade, summoned by Marlene, shrouded the enemy group in darkness, and Irmhild fired arrows into it. For Sheila, projectiles and darkness were no problem at all. From within the darkness came a chorus of anguish, screams, and shrieks.

“You bastard! At the very least, you—!”

One man charged at me in a rage. He was the one giving orders during the escape too. Seems he’s the leader type. And apparently a Magic Swordsman. Clenching his teeth, showing a determined expression, he approached me while manipulating a water blade like a whip.

The movement of his hand transmitted to the water blade, approaching my neck from an unexpected direction. No problem. A thin Shield Barrier deployed in all directions. The moment it made contact, I grasped the direction and angle. Without slowing my charging speed, I knocked it away with another Shield deployed on the inside.

“Wha—!?”

The man barely managed to block Ouroboros with his sword. The next moment, the leader’s expression twisted in agony. Nemea had leaped out and bitten his shin.

“Gah!?”

He tried to scream, but Ouroboros joyfully growled from below and slammed into his chin.

“Sleep.”

Since his leg was bitten, he couldn’t be sent flying. With one motion, I struck his head down and harvested his consciousness.

“L, Lord Elmer!?”

“Next!”

Using Capella’s hind legs for a great leap, I swept through the flank of a man who wasn’t paying attention to me. With the sensation of ribs breaking, I sent him tumbling and writhing in agony.

“Next!”

Like a pinball. Using my own legs, Nemea, and Capella’s legs, I kicked off from Shield to Shield, flying around. Repeating high-speed movements like ricochets, I sent anyone I touched flying with Ouroboros, with magic, with Nemea, with Capella—knocking them away indiscriminately.

“Gah!”

“Ugh!”

“M, monster—eek!!”

After roughly sending flying most of those I noticed, I applied Levitation for an emergency stop. Drawing an arc in the air, I landed. Following belatedly, several sounds of humans hitting the ground overlapped.

Those who had been voicing their anguish were also enveloped by the Sleep Cloud and quickly fell silent. When I scattered the sleep cloud with Wind Magic, what remained were the figures of the gang, unconscious and sprawled on the ground. A scene of heaps of corpses, so to speak.

Haa… I was pretty angry, but… I’ve vented my frustration a bit, I suppose.

Now, as usual. Solidify with Earth Magic and seal the magic. Let’s finish this area quickly.

+++

#  **216 – Imposter**

“Ugh… ghh… It hurts…”

The man groaned as he cracked his eyes open, his face contorting in pain. His body must have been wracked with agony. Though he tried to put strength into his limbs, he remained lying down. Moreover, the pain in his body seemed to prevent him from moving.

“Awake, are you?”

The man turned his gaze toward the voice’s direction. There stood Elmer, the group’s Leader. Elmer too had been rolled over after being immobilized by Earth Magic. Seeing this, the man seemed to understand the position he himself was in.

“Are you… unharmed…?”

“Hard to call this ‘unharmed.’ Look at this state. Can’t use Magic. My head and jaw hurt. It’s a bit hard to talk, but well, I’m alive somehow.”

Elmer, with bandages wrapped around his head, gave a pained smile.

“Magic is… that means…”

“Lower your voice. We don’t know who might be listening.”

At Elmer’s hushed tone, the man looked startled and hurriedly scanned his surroundings. The place he was in. The situation he was placed in.

He realized they were in some unfamiliar mansion, with quite splendid interior decor. Only the man and Elmer were around. No one else was present.

“This is… what’s going on?”

“Don’t know. Probably, this is a room in Count Gartner’s residence. The others were here too, but they seem to be taking them out one by one. Whether they’re being interrogated or transported, I don’t know… For some reason or another… our plan was exposed, we were defeated, and here we are.”

The man showed a thoughtful expression at Elmer’s words, then said:

“Ah, r-right! That Bayle…! Could he have betrayed us!?”

“He was likely just being controlled by some kind of Magic. I don’t know the Magic, but such things probably exist. The enemy was simply better. That’s all there is to it.”

The man’s eyes widened at those words. Then he let out a deep breath and said:

“…What’s going to happen to us now?”

“Rescue is hopeless. The guys we had stationed at the annex were taken out by a Mechanism and defeated. Bringing Godwin along was so we could insist it was for ransom if exposed. All we can do now is keep quiet and solemnly accept our punishment.”

At Elmer’s words, the man looked dejected and gave a weak laugh.

“To think those two misread the opportunity…”

“If they judged it was something the two of them could handle, it must have truly been a good chance. One that wouldn’t come again if missed. Then, it just means we were short on hands…. It was my misjudgment.”

“That’s not…”

“If it had gone well… perhaps we might have achieved our objective too…”

“The recovery of Patricia’s possessed Magic…?”

Just as the man said that much, the expression vanished from Elmer’s face.

“Elmer-sama?”

Ignoring the man’s puzzled question, Elmer stood up casually as if it were nothing.

The man was speechless. The stone coffin that should have been binding Elmer was like a prop, hollow inside, with just the lid placed on top. If he’d wanted, he could have moved at any time.

Why? Had the Magic Seal been lifted, allowing him to break the bindings?

Such were the questions and hopes the man harbored. The answer to them was a change in Elmer beyond his expectations.

“Ghk!?”

From his face. From his hands. The color drained away. His eyes, nose, and mouth became indistinct in shape, and his hair receded as if being sucked back into his scalp. In a short time, what had been Elmer transformed into something semi-transparent. In other words—the true form of a Doppelganger.

Then the room’s door opened. The man looked at me as I entered, his eyes wide.

“Good work, Ambrum.”

Ambrum placed a hand on his hip, bowed slightly, and left the room. Caduceus was with him. Their exchange just now, though in low voices, had been clearly audible to me.

Apparently, Ambrum can’t speak when not in human form because he lacks vocal cords. Even in human form, his responses aren’t that skilled, so if you want him to speak elaborately beyond prearranged replies, Rosemary needs to directly control him.

Rosemary being strict with the surroundings was also a precaution to keep the servants at a distance, preventing the Shadow Clone’s flaws from showing.

And directly controlling him results in that.

“Wh-what was that!?”

“No need to talk. I’ll tell you this much: that was a confirmation check. You’re not the only one who leaked information, so no need to feel particularly guilty.”

The man finally realized he’d been tricked, his mouth opening and closing wordlessly. He seemed at a loss for words.

Compared to preparing things like Magical Inquisition or Magic Potions, this method is quicker. Besides, Rosemary, upon my suggestion, seemed to put considerable effort into controlling Ambrum, thinking it might serve as some form of atonement toward Father.

Anyway, I’ve heard what I needed to. Using Sleep Cloud to make him lose consciousness again, I levitate him to the entrance hall with Levitation.

“Is this the last one?”

Claudia asked.

There, the packaged kidnappers were piled up like luggage. Everyone was waiting nearby.

“Yeah. Termwills side seems to have their reception ready, so please handle it.”

“Okay. Leave it to me.”

A Teleportation Magic Array spread from Claudia’s feet, and the group was neatly shipped off to Termwills. Left behind was—only Godwin, his face pale.

This guy can’t use Magic either, and his connection to them is weak. Since there’s no need for Magic restriction with Subjugation Magic, this is more a matter to be left to Father.

Former servant Godwin will play the role of being publicly denounced for attempting to guide criminals for monetary gain, serving as a stern warning to prevent others from following.

“I-It’s a misunderstanding, Master! … Th-Theodore, young master too! I-I was just—told I’d get money if I guided them around the county…!”

When Father and I looked at Godwin, he said such things with a strained smile.

…Guiding, huh.

“Heard you were grumbling in a tavern and got approached?”

When I said that, Godwin started trembling violently.

We have multiple testimonies from the group. Godwin apparently resented Father for being fired so easily after years of service. Even so, Godwin was effectively a spy for the Marquis’s family, betraying the Count’s family, so it’s his own fault.

Seems he was spotted by their information-gathering team while drunkenly grumbling with misplaced resentment, and was approached about helping steal the Count’s family treasures.

But their method was kidnapping. And—their objective wasn’t treasures, but Patricia—likely Mother’s Magic Formula. Those two set their Mechanism there because they thought they could kidnap both Father and Kathryn simultaneously.

They figured they could use Kathryn’s safety—someone Father shows kindness to—as a Shield to prompt Father’s confession. A chance to kidnap two people under night’s cover without drawing attention isn’t something that comes often.

Well, Godwin probably wasn’t told that, but even so… he apparently leaked the Count’s family internal affairs to them, and using his familiarity, loitered around so that even if seen, it would seem like he was there to request reemployment.

He wasn’t given information… but there’s no doubt he was quite actively assisting them.

“I heard plenty from the next room. Disappointing, Godwin.”

“N-No! I was! Just tricked by them!”

When Father sighed, Godwin’s eyes widened and he started piling excuse upon excuse, but it was unbearable to listen. He was carried off by soldiers while screaming.

“Patricia, huh… Between that and Silvatoria…”

Father made a sour face and put a hand to his forehead. Ah… He’s tired.

Well, it’s been one thing after another; can’t be helped.

“—Mother probably didn’t want to drag you into her own affairs.”

“…That’s… about Lisa. Surely that must be it.”

He narrowed his eyes and smiled wryly. …Come to think of it, I couldn’t say it to Father earlier.

“Something I forgot to mention earlier—you said you were too soft, right?”

“Yes.”

“Mother called that ‘kind.'”

That’s what I like about you, too.

Father’s eyes widened slightly, then he showed a gentle smile.

“Thank you, Theo.”

Saying that, Father quietly closed his eyes.

“Right after arriving… various things happened, but I’m looking forward to tomorrow’s banquet.”

“That’s right. That should proceed as scheduled.”

Rosemary’s matter will come after that, I suppose.

“Then we’ll return to Mother’s house for now. Let’s start fresh tomorrow.”

“Yes. Until tomorrow. I’m looking forward to it.”

Before then, we need to organize and properly compile what we learned from their testimonies. Grace and the others, who had been smiling during my exchange with Father, nodded back with serious expressions when I looked at them and nodded.

+++

# **217 – Heir of the Count's Family**

After returning to Mother’s house, we took time to discuss matters while drinking tea around the table.

Once we return to Termwills, we’ll need to report to King Melvin, so we should organize the key points. Since we came partly for vacation or rather to escape the summer heat, it’s better to properly finish what needs to be done before switching our mindset.

“Is this related to Silvatoria again?”

“Marquis Zilbolt’s name came up. As usual, they claim it’s just someone they helped once before and that any official connections have been erased.”

“They’ll probably play dumb even if we protest.”

Rosemary shrugged her shoulders.

“Most likely.”

To be this blatant and yet try to feign ignorance… Well, it might be effective in situations where we can’t reach them directly.

They haven’t mentioned anything about the connection with the Crown Prince either. Either the lower ranks haven’t been informed, or there’s no relation. It’s unclear, but we should probably operate under the assumption that there is a connection.

“Why… would they come to Lord Henry’s place now of all times?”

Grace tilted her head in puzzlement.

Right. That’s another issue. Where did they get their information?
