If they have information about me, it would be normal to assume I’ve inherited Mother’s magic. If they’re trying to track down Mother’s magic, they should target me first. Naturally, their goal should be my home rather than the Count’s territory, but that didn’t happen.

As for Mother’s house… it seems they tried to break in but were easily stopped by the barrier.

According to Godwin’s information, they eventually gave up on entering Mother’s house and, following reports that household items and books had been moved to the Count’s family, began investigating the Count’s mansion instead. If they secure Father, they might gain access to Mother’s house too, so the order makes sense.

“What were they saying?”

“It seems they only learned about my information after joining up with Godwin.”

“So they were initially targeting the Count’s territory and learned about it there, I suppose?”

Claudia put her hand to her mouth and spoke while pondering. Well, that’s probably what happened. The reason they didn’t come to me directly was likely to avoid extra work.

“Did they think they could use your father as a hostage if they kidnapped him?”

Even though we’re estranged, taking a blood relative hostage could be useful for luring someone out or making moves. Well, thanks to all these circumstances, it’s fortunate that reports about me haven’t reached them yet. The information connecting Mother heading to the Count’s territory and me being the Count’s Illegitimate Child hasn’t reached them.

Anyway, they were originally searching for Mother. They must have obtained information about Mother’s whereabouts somewhere… unrelated to me, and sent operatives.

Where and how did they manage to track her down? Beyond this point, we can only speculate. After all, they’re just pawns who don’t understand their superiors’ intentions, and having King Melvin protest should serve as a deterrent for the future.

“Well, we should probably protest using Marquis Zilbolt’s name. For this to happen again after the previous incident is a bit too convenient to dismiss as coincidental actions by someone who just happened to resign.”

They might be able to explain away one incident… There’s a possibility that the previous Failure hasn’t been reported to Marquis Zilbolt yet. If Silvatoria takes the situation seriously, they should show some reaction.

The next day. As scheduled, a welcome banquet was to be held, so we headed to the Count’s mansion.

Since the improvement in my relationship with Father is being kept secret, it would be an informal gathering with only those involved privately, without informing the retainers.

Riding in the carriage that came to pick us up, we headed to the mansion where the great hall was decorated with flowers and candlesticks, with food laid out.

“Thank you for coming all this way. I apologize for my incompetence in being unable to properly welcome you last night… I’m truly happy that you’ve come to this welcome gathering. Though modest, I believe we’ve prepared dishes made with care. I would be delighted if you could relax and enjoy yourselves.”

After Father’s greeting, applause broke out, signaling the start of the banquet.

A banquet at the Count’s mansion. With me as the guest of honor… feels somewhat strange. When my eyes met Grace’s, she smiled at me. Hmm.

“Normally we would call for musicians,” Father said with a wry smile as we took our seats. Well, since outsiders can’t attend, there’s no helping it.

“If I would suffice, might I offer a song, though it may offend your ears?”

“That would be most appreciated. Please let us hear it later.”

At Irmhild’s offer, Father nodded.

“Speaking of which, Mihaela-san is at my house.”

“Oh?”

“She said she’s looking forward to meeting in autumn.”

When I conveyed Mihaela’s words, Father showed a happy smile.

“Understood. Please tell her that I too am looking forward to our autumn reunion.”

“Understood.”

Being a grain-producing region, the animals grow plump as well. Processed products like cheese and meat dishes are surprisingly abundant. Various dishes appeared – meat pies, stews, herb-roasted local chicken, and more.

The banquet continued in a peaceful atmosphere. Lavigne also seemed quite pleased, receiving bone-in meat from Ashley and Marlene.

After the meal reached a natural break, my eyes met Rosemary’s. Right. Let’s get this matter settled.

“Father. About what Rosemary wanted to discuss with you that we mentioned yesterday.”

“Yes. Everyone, please continue your conversations for a while.”

Nodding, he stood up. Father, Rosemary, and I left the great hall and headed to the reception room.

“You said you had something to discuss with me?”

At Father’s question, Rosemary closed her eyes, took a deep breath, then looked straight at him with a serious expression.

“Yes. I must apologize to you, Count.”

“An apology…?”

“Last autumn in Termwills, both giving Lord Byron information about Theodore-sama and providing medicine to your wife were my schemes.”

At Rosemary’s words, Father’s eyes widened.

“…Why would you do that?”

“I desired the throne. To that end, I attempted to draw Theodore-sama into my faction. Theodore-sama exposed my scheme, and my father ordered me to be confined.”

“…I see.”

Father had probably heard about Rosemary advocating meritocracy. Therefore, even when told about Rosemary’s goals, he wasn’t that surprised.

As for Rosemary, she had already explained to King Melvin that she intended to apologize, so this much wouldn’t constitute betrayal. Though she was apparently told not to reveal the medicine’s effects due to the Oath.

“I apologize for the tremendous trouble I caused you, Count, and the members of your family due to my selfishness.”

Saying this, Rosemary bowed deeply.

“…Please raise your head.”

Father closed his eyes.

“Regarding Byron and Kathryn’s actions, they are partly my own fault and due to inadequate supervision. So, there’s just one thing I’d like to ask.”

“Yes.”

“What are your current feelings toward Theodore?”

Asked by Father, Rosemary answered without hesitation.

“After that… due to my own blunder, I endangered Theodore-sama’s life, and then had my own life saved. While I could claim it was for the country’s sake, I believe I owe Theodore-sama an immeasurable debt. The reason I’m outside now is because I swore with Oath Magic never to betray my father and Theodore-sama for life, and only through their mercy. If I don’t repay that feeling, I would lose even my pride as a member of the royal family.”

“To go as far as using Oath Magic…”

Whether due to that level of resolve or because of Rosemary’s severity, Father seemed genuinely surprised by her words. Even though she’s former royalty, for a princess to use Oath Magic is certainly no ordinary matter.

“I understand the extent of your resolve. With that, I have nothing more to say. I accept your apology.”

At Father’s words, Rosemary bowed her head quietly once more.

Then, a knock sounded.

“What is it?”

When Father prompted entry, a servant entered and bowed.

“Pardon the interruption. Lord Daryl insists he must speak with Theodore-sama and is requesting a meeting.”

Huh? Daryl wants to meet with me…? What could it be about?

I instinctively looked at Father. After thinking for a moment, Father made a suggestion.

“What if I… wait in the adjacent room? On the condition that Daryl isn’t informed I’m there, would you meet with him?”

…I see. He wants me to see the results of his education of Daryl while also judging Daryl’s current way of thinking with his own eyes.

For the Count’s family, the progress of Daryl’s education is something that can’t be neglected. After all, Daryl is now the Count’s heir.

“Understood.”

“Then, please make preparations accordingly.”

Receiving Father’s order, the servant bowed and left.

Once preparations for the meeting with Daryl were complete, I waited in a room in the Count’s mansion. Then a knock sounded in the room.

“Come in.”

When I answered, the door opened and Daryl was guided in by a servant… Huh?

Behind the servant stood a slender boy. He appeared slightly older than me. His face bore some resemblance to Kathryn—

“—It’s been a while.”

When our eyes met, the boy bowed. That voice. No mistake. While people change… Daryl looked quite different from when I last saw him.

+++

# **218 – Longing**

“First… allow me to apologize for my numerous past acts of disrespect.”

As he said this, Daryl bowed his head. Rather than resolute, his expression showed signs of tension.

He’d probably heard that I’m the Otherworld Ambassador and treated as King Melvin’s direct retainer…

“Um. Why don’t we sit down and talk first?”

If I didn’t say something like that, the conversation didn’t seem like it would progress.

Since he was quite different from my previous impression of Daryl, before even considering whether to forgive him or not, I needed to hear what had happened and how he’d ended up like this to make any judgment about the current Daryl.

As for what Daryl had done… well, it was unpleasant, but that was about it. If he had the will to apologize, there was no reason not to forgive him.

After sitting facing Daryl, a servant brought tea. While tilting my teacup, I waited for the servant to leave before asking.

“…You’ve changed quite a bit. What kind of life have you been living since I left here?”

Father had said he would reeducate him, but I hadn’t heard the specific details.

“Father… Father said I should first learn about the lives of the people in our territory. Until winter came, I helped with land clearing and farm work.”

I could still see he was forcing himself regarding his speech patterns. Well, that might be a minor issue. But land clearing, of all things.

“Cutting down trees, digging up roots?”

“I helped with thinner trees. Cutting felled trees into smaller pieces and carrying them, then making them into firewood. After that, removing stones from land to be made into fields, tilling, scattering seed rice, pulling weeds, exterminating insects… basically everything until harvest. …I don’t think I was much help though.”

…I see. No wonder he lost weight.

“It was hard work… but they let me eat bread baked with the harvested wheat. That was delicious.”

Daryl smiled proudly, happily. For Daryl… farm work might have been more enjoyable than expected.

Certainly… if he’s to become the Count of this territory, he should probably know about the lives of the people.

“But… that…”

Daryl seemed to have difficulty speaking, his gaze wandering as he hesitated.

“…What is it?”

When I urged him to continue, Daryl still seemed uncertain, but eventually spoke as if he’d made up his mind.

“I… had something I wanted to say to you, Theodore.”

Daryl took a deep breath and spoke. Traces of his former self overlapped with him now. With a somewhat desperate appearance, his true face was showing, not that of a noble.

“Since long ago, I’ve always been protected by my brother. Since other people listen to what my brother says too, I think I got carried away with that.”

That’s right. Daryl used to follow behind Byron. That was the impression I had. When they did something to me, Byron was the main instigator and Daryl was the follower. He often went along with Byron.

“But you… even when my brother and I did various things to you, you somehow didn’t seem to take us seriously, which was a bit different from how you were with others. That… how should I put it?”

Daryl chose his words carefully.

“That made me… envious, I guess… I—might have wanted strength like yours.”

“That is…”

Strength like mine?

Was that referring to the current me, or the old me who couldn’t do anything…?

…The old me hated my own powerlessness. That’s why I read magic-related books in the study, hoping to be able to use magic and leave home someday.

That was because of Mother and Grace. Ah… yes, indeed.

Kathryn, Byron, and Daryl. They might have been reasons that motivated me to learn magic, but they probably weren’t the fundamental reason.

No matter what my relationship with those three had been, I would have still learned magic—hoped to gain greater power someday, and left home.

“You’re overestimating me. I was just—completely preoccupied with my own affairs.”

No matter how Daryl perceived me, it wasn’t that I wasn’t taking him seriously—I just didn’t have the capacity to do so.

“But you’re producing results now, aren’t you? Even when Father told me you’re working as His Majesty’s direct retainer, I wasn’t that surprised. I thought, of course you would. When you became able to use magic and left home, I hated myself for being someone who couldn’t do anything without my brother. So… I think that’s why I was able to work hard at farm work and such.”

“I see.”

“Yeah.”

Daryl laughed self-deprecatingly.

“Well—I understand now.”

“Ah, no. That’s not what I meant to talk about. I went off on a tangent, but the reason I asked Father to let me meet you was different.”

Daryl shook his head.

“Huh?”

“It’s… about Mother.”

…Ah. That’s what it is. Even without him elaborating, I understand well enough now.

“You saved Mother. So I absolutely wanted to thank you for that.”

Nodding at his words, I extended my right hand.

“I’ll forget about the past. Please become a good lord.”

“…Thank you.”

After that exchange, Daryl and I shook hands.

“Would you like to make an appearance at the banquet too?”

“Is that alright?”

“Well… Father was probably being considerate of me. I’ll ask Father about it a bit.”

Since we’ve let bygones be bygones, I don’t see any reason to refuse Daryl attending the banquet.

“How was it?”

Daryl had returned to his room until called. When I went to Father’s room next door, he asked me about my impression of Daryl.

“He’s changed quite a bit from before, I’m surprised.”

Or perhaps—his inner self hasn’t changed dramatically, but only a little. Father’s treatment of Daryl. The influence of being separated from Kathryn and Byron. His perspective on me.

“It might be more due to Theo’s influence than any achievement of mine.”

“I wasn’t conscious of anything like that. Perhaps I became a trigger for change, but Father created the environment for it, and Daryl was the one who continued.”

My influence from just leaving home… probably wasn’t that significant.

“Maybe so. Surprisingly, it might have suited Daryl.”

If he learned about the lives of the people after I left, there must have been a period when Byron was doing farm work too… but that guy prefers things that look impressive. He probably hated that kind of work.

As for Daryl, it seems Father’s intended effect worked as planned.

“About Daryl and your wife attending the banquet…”

“Are you fine with Kathryn being there too?”

“Even if I reconcile with that person, you’re not going to revoke her previous treatment, are you? In that case, having such breaks occasionally might be good. Daryl… probably hasn’t seen your wife for a while either.”

When I said this, Father smiled somewhat troubled.

“That’s… true. If I’m present, having them visit Kathryn’s separate residence together… might be fine occasionally.”

“Ah. That’s right. I have a small proposal regarding this house and the separate residence.”

“What is it?”

“I imagine you’ll be strengthening security from now on, but could you let me create hidden doors and connecting underground passages? I’ve learned Magic Construction.”

Father blinked. It would be similar to the Revolving Concealment doors and underground shelter room I made at the Orphanage.

Yeah. I’ll send Father an Alarm Device magic tool later too. Combined with increased security, I think it will be quite effective.

“Well then, Father.”

“Ah. You said you’ll be staying at Lisa’s house for two more days?”

As the banquet ended and it was time to leave the Count’s residence… Father came to see me off all the way to the entrance hall.

At the banquet, Irmhild performed singing while playing an instrument, and it was quite lively. Kathryn and Daryl also seemed happy to reunite after so long.

“Yes. I think we’ll probably spend tomorrow at the lake. We plan to depart around noon the day after tomorrow, but regarding the Magic Construction, I thought I’d do it all on the final day, going over first thing in the morning.”

Creating an underground passage connecting the Count’s residence and the separate residence… and making a shelter room along the way with locked hidden doors should serve various functions when combined with the Alarm Device.

“…Can you complete it that quickly?”

“Well, yes. It’s just digging and hardening.”

It’s not like I’m adding decorations. As long as it’s sturdy, that’s good enough.

“I keep imposing on you for everything.”

“Not at all. Well, if you have anything to discuss or need anything, please come visit anytime.”

“Even though you’ve come here with everyone for summer retreat, it would be bad if I disturbed you. I’ll just come to see you off before you leave.”

Father said with a wry smile.

Hmm. Well, if that’s the case. I’ll relax with everyone tomorrow then.

+++

# **219 – Summer Lake**

“What a beautiful lake,” Claudia remarked admiringly, watching the water’s surface sparkle under the sunlight, mirroring the blue sky and green forest like glass.

“It really is beautiful!”

Seraphina exclaimed happily, darting out to fly just above the lake surface, kicking off the water and soaring upward.

We had all cooked together since early morning before heading out to the lake. It wasn’t far from Mother’s house – not particularly large, but with remarkably clear water.

Small flowers bloomed across the green carpet of the lakeshore, creating a peaceful scene.

A pier extended from the shore where one could set up and fish leisurely. Though I’d fished here before, I had no memory of swimming here. When you’re a bit older, I’ll teach you how to swim… or so Mother had said, I recalled.

“We have not just lunch but also baked sweets and drinks.”

“I’ll make sure everything’s ready for whenever anyone gets hungry.”

Grace and Irmhild cheerfully spread a cloth on the pier, arranging baskets as they prepared for lunch and snacks.

“Shall we all eat together a bit later? Until then, let’s do some swimming.”

“That sounds good. I’ll join you once I finish arranging these.”

Grace smiled in her swimsuit, her translucent white skin and golden hair shining under the sunlight.

…As usual, I should deploy a Dark Magic defense field overhead to prevent sunburn. And the underwater breathing Magic too.

This part was similar to when we went to the sea last year. Since we planned to swim this year too, I’d brought swimsuits made from water spider silk. We were also planning to visit the Magic Light Water Vein, so learning to swim wouldn’t hurt… but. Well, let’s just say it’s quite the visual feast. I’m having trouble knowing where to look.

“I want to play music after lunch, so I think I’ll swim until then.”

Once preparations were complete, Irmhild released her Humanization Spell, removed the cloth wrapped around her waist, and entered the water. She swam by undulating her tail, moving at considerable speed. With Seraphina riding on her shoulder, she seemed to be having great fun.

“I brought fishing rods too.”

Sheila showed me her fishing rod.

“You can catch quite a bit here. Besides fish, there are things like river shrimp.”

“Are they edible?”

“If properly cooked.”

“Mhm. After swimming a bit, I’ll fish from the other side of the pier.”

Her expression was as usual, but she seemed quite determined. Though she was in swimwear too.

“It’s cold and feels wonderful.”

Ashley slowly entered the lake from the pier, acclimating feet first, then lay on her back floating on the surface, gazing at the sky before quietly closing her eyes.

Her silver hair spread across the lake, creating quite a fantastical scene.

“So Ashley learned how to swim too.”

“Grace-sama taught me before, and since the bath became larger… I practiced a little by myself sometimes.”

Blushing slightly, Ashley smiled somewhat bashfully. I see. So she’d been practicing secretly.

“I’ve also gotten quite good at moving using water flow manipulation.”

She said, using Magic to glide across the water’s surface.

“Impressive.”

She really does have high aptitude for Water Magic. At my words, she smiled shyly.

“What about everyone else? Can you swim?”

After completing a lap around the area, Ashley asked the group on the pier.

Marlene, who met her gaze, shook her head, but perhaps because of the underwater breathing Magic, she entered the water with Lavigne without much fear. While holding onto Lavigne’s waist area as she dog-paddled, Marlene moved her own arms and legs to stay afloat.

Marlene wore a light blue one-piece swimsuit. It was a modest design, but it suited Marlene’s innocent impression rather than merely pure.

“I can swim a little too, so I could teach Marlene swimming, but…”

Claudia, who had a cloth draped over her shoulders, was blushing. Claudia seemed to be more overwhelmed by the embarrassment of showing her skin…

“Mhm… that’s right. Theodore is my fiancé after all.”

Saying this, she removed the cloth with some hesitation. A black swimsuit. It matched Claudia’s hair color well. It had frills and was a relatively modest design, but it was a two-piece. Apparently, they couldn’t find a one-piece that fit properly, and Claudia was apparently unhappy about the increased exposure. Well… swimsuits made from water spider silk are quite valuable items in their own right.

Claudia entered the water with slightly reddened cheeks. Once in the water, perhaps her embarrassment halved, as she swam over near Marlene. She’s quite a good swimmer.

“With underwater breathing, why not try learning to swim?”

At Claudia’s offer, Marlene happily nodded repeatedly. She separated from Lavigne and, holding Claudia’s hand, began swimming practice. Last year, Grace had been teaching Ashley.

“Where did you learn to swim, Claudia?”

“Deep within the Magic Light Water Vein. As a pastime against boredom, I suppose. That place has beautifully clear water…”

I see. Claudia doesn’t get attacked by Labyrinth Monsters. In that sense, the Magic Light Water Vein has quite a fantastical beauty, and might be a good place for swimming.

And then there was Rosemary, dressed in a bikini-type swimsuit with a straw hat and a pareo around her waist.

“I can’t swim,” she declared quite frankly. With her good figure, she carried herself confidently… I suppose. Well, if you can use Magic, you can use Levitation, underwater breathing, water walking… indeed, there might be no need to learn. Marlene also has Blessings, so she can handle falling in the water.

“But one should challenge themselves with new things.”

She placed her straw hat in a basket with the brim tucked in so it wouldn’t blow away, then entered the water while holding onto the pier’s edge.

“If you can glide like that with Water Magic… then. For just floating, you could use Wind Magic, right?”

Saying this, she manipulated water and wind Magic, creating a bubble sphere with strength and elasticity, then holding onto it to float. It probably felt like holding onto a beach ball. She was trying to move with it, but didn’t seem to be doing very well.

“If you relax, you’ll float naturally. Like this, use your hips too, move your legs from the thighs, and kick with the tops and soles of your feet. Feeling the water’s resistance means you’re kicking the water properly—”

The basics of the flutter kick. I demonstrated along with the front crawl.

Marlene, listening nearby, nodded seriously with a earnest expression. There were various other points to pay attention to for swimming fast, but being able to do it to some extent should be enough.

“Theo’s swimming style is beautiful.”

Well, it’s from Earth’s side, what’s commonly called modern swimming technique.

“Um. Like this, perhaps?”

Still holding onto her wind ball, Rosemary also swam with a flutter kick. Was she moving more smoothly than before?

“Not shrimp, but I caught a crab.”

Sheila surfaced from the lake bottom, holding up crabs in both hands triumphantly.

“Can we eat these crabs?”

“If properly cooked.”

With the underwater breathing Magic, an underwater stroll seemed like it would be enjoyable too.

When we went to the sea last year… I was gliding on the water’s surface, wasn’t I?

Ah, I just thought of something. Maybe I’ll try something different this year.

“Is something the matter?”

Grace asked me as I emerged from the water.

“No. Just thought of something.”

Since I’ll remove it after we’re done playing, the landscape shouldn’t be an issue.

From the somewhat shallow area beside the pier, I began using Magic Construction to build a waterslide. Making it half-pipe shaped and winding, smoothing the surface like marble, then using Water Magic to draw water from the lake surface and flow it through… yeah. This should work.

“Climb the stairs and slide from here—”

I tried sliding as a test. Carried by the water’s momentum, I flowed through the pipe. There were places where centrifugal force threatened to throw me out, but by making small adjustments while sliding, I completed a somewhat short but functional waterslide. I made the endpoint slightly upward so you’d be launched lightly before landing in the lake.

…Yeah. Not a bad result.

“You make interesting things.”

Everyone came up onto the pier and, looking quite interested, took turns sliding down. They seemed to be enjoying it quite a bit, which was good.

“Is it okay if two people slide together?”

Sheila asked from the top of the slide. It seemed she planned to slide with Irmhild.

“There are no sharp parts, and even if you’re thrown outward, it’s set up so you’ll fall into the lake, so I think it should be fine.”

“We’ll try it then.”

Irmhild clung to Sheila’s back and slid in a prone position. Even if she used her Humanization Spell, she could probably slide normally.

Seeing this, Ashley and Marlene smiled at each other and slid down together. Perhaps because they’re close in age, the two get along well.

“Going in pairs seems fun too. Marie, would you like to go together?”

“If Claudia-sama says so.”

It seemed Claudia would slide with Rosemary. Rosemary got behind Claudia, and the two slid down together.

When I headed back up thinking to slide again, it was Grace’s turn.

“Theo, would you like to go together?”

“Me too!”

Grace smiled, with Seraphina even climbing onto her shoulder. Um… this pattern means I’ll end up sliding with everyone once each.

“…Mhm. Please.”

I was in the front position. With Grace behind me in this arrangement. I shouldn’t think too deeply about things like Grace’s hands touching my shoulders, and various other matters. Twirling around inside the slide, we were thrown into the air accompanied by Seraphina’s cheerful laughter. After the sensation of floating, the three of us landed together.

Claudia, watching this, blushed.

“W-well, I… um… ah, later is fine. Why don’t you two go first?”

The yielded Ashley and Marlene smiled and nodded. With me sandwiched between them – Marlene, me, Ashley in that order – we slid down as a trio again. Yeah.

After being thrown from the slide and surfacing on the water, Marlene showed me a carefree smile.

“Claudia-sama, please.”

“Y-yes.”

“How should we arrange ourselves?”

“…I-I’ll go in front.”

After such an exchange, I slid with Claudia. Claudia kept herself curled up small the entire time.

Up to that point, well, it was business as usual, so to speak.

When we surfaced, as a result of the female members’ discussion, since I’d been with Seraphina first, it was suggested that Sheila, Irmhild, and Rosemary also slide with me.

“Um…”

“We thought that would be fine for us.”

Looking around, everyone seemed to agree… It’s mysterious. Would things go more smoothly if I didn’t refuse?

“Let’s go.”

“Fufu. It’s fun, but somehow I feel bad.”

In an arrangement where I was sandwiched between Sheila and Irmhild. The density of skin tones felt too high, and I felt my thoughts gradually becoming paralyzed. Due to Irmhild being in a prone position, we inevitably ended up leaning against each other.

“You have it rough in various ways too,” Rosemary said, covering her mouth while laughing happily.

Next time, I was in front. The problem was that we ended up pressed close together every time upon landing. Somehow, I felt like various things were being whittled away. I should cool my head underwater for a bit.

——We swam and played to our hearts’ content.

After having a slightly late lunch, we all lay down on the pier. The sunlight, appropriately weakened by Dark Magic, warmed our bodies that had cooled slightly from swimming.

Sheila was fishing. Irmhild was playing music, and everyone else was sunbathing. Caduceus and Ouroboros, the Chimera Coats too, seemed quite relaxed in the sunny spots.

Whether the Cursed Melody gathered fish or not, the catch was excellent. Irmhild said she learned it from Justia.

Lavigne was also gathering shrimp and crabs from the lake, tossing them into a bucket. Tonight’s dinner would probably be all about fish, shrimp, and crabs.

“—The sky is beautiful, isn’t it?”

“Yeah, it is.”

Grace, lying upside down, smiled at me.

Blue sky with summer clouds. The sounds reaching our ears were Irmhild’s Lute playing and clear singing voice. The nostalgic sound of insects.

It was a calm, leisurely time, as if we’d returned to the past. It was so comfortable that when I closed my eyes, aided by the warmth, I was able to fall into a pleasant sleep.

+++

# **220 – On the Way Back to Termwills**

“Good morning, Father.”

“Yes, good morning.”

After resting thoroughly to restore my energy, I headed to the Count’s mansion from morning to create an emergency underground passage.

“Where should we start constructing the underground passage? Should we begin from the study as usual?”

“Is that… the standard approach?”

“Well, you could call it a matter of aesthetic convention.”

It’s fairly close to the bedroom too. I’ll reinforce the door to make it stronger so it can be used for barricading.

I’ll use Levitation to float the bookshelf and incorporate it into a Revolving Concealment mechanism. Behind that space, I’ll form stairs leading underground and create the passage.

I’ve grown quite accustomed to this work by now – it’s simple labor involving turning the earth into Golems to carry it out, then solidifying the passage to ensure its strength.

However, while it must be usable for evacuation during emergencies, it needs to be completely separated from the Count’s mansion and the annex during normal times. That will require some ingenuity.

So I’ll create adjacent evacuation rooms – one on the Count’s mansion side and one on the annex side.

By creating a locked door connecting the two evacuation rooms, I can simultaneously establish three functions: a connecting passage, evacuation rooms, and a partition wall.

“There’s one problem. If we’re attacked and flee into the evacuation passage from the study or annex, since there are no other exits, intruders might detect the existence of the hidden passage.”

“Hmm. That’s certainly true.”

“So I’ll create a Mechanism that can trap intruders in the hidden passage.”

If there are pursuers, I’ll create corners to break their line of sight. Then immediately after turning the corner, I’ll place a Revolving Concealment hidden door leading to the evacuation room.

And beyond the corner – at the very end of the passage, the most noticeable spot – I’ll create a fake evacuation room.

“The real evacuation room can be locked from the inside with a bolt after entering. Meanwhile, the fake room – even if the door can be opened from outside, it should be designed so that those inside cannot get out without a key.”

“…I see.”

Father looked somewhat astonished. Indeed, opportunities to receive explanations while watching Magic Construction in real time probably aren’t common.

For the evacuation room, I should create a small room that can be used as a toilet so people can hide for some time. Since it’s for emergencies, it will be a simple toilet with just a small vertical hole dug.

“I’ll create a similar underground passage from the annex side as well – but since it would be troublesome if someone got trapped in the fake room, please explain this thoroughly to Mother and Daryl.”

“Yes. I’ll definitely do that. We’ll also need to store non-perishable food and spare clothes in the evacuation room.”

“For clothes, it might be useful to have disguises that would allow you to blend in with servants or commoners. Since we haven’t installed water pipes here, we’ll probably need Magic Tools for water creation too.”

“That’s true. I’ll arrange for that.”

Considering who would use this place – probably just Father, Kathryn, and Daryl – and installing Alarm Devices in both the Count’s mansion and annex should make for quite substantial security measures.

I completed the passage and evacuation rooms as planned, then checked for any defects or strength issues.

“Everything seems fine. Well, sorry for the rush, but I’ll be heading back. I have some things to take care of before departing.”

“Understood. I’ll head to the forest later too. I’ll see you off.”

“Yes. See you later.”

I nodded to Father, promised to meet again later, and left the Count’s mansion.

After finishing lunch and preparing for the return journey, Father arrived, so we decided to visit Mother’s grave once more before leaving.

We all offered silent prayers at the grave, then turned to face Father, and Harold and Cynthia who had come to see us off.

“Are you leaving already?”

“Yes. I’ll be staying in the Barony of Silun too, and I’m concerned about things back home.”

When I answered, Father smiled wryly, looking somewhat lonely.

“You’re quite busy.”

“You are too, Father. Please take care of your health.”

“Yes.”

“Well then, Henry-sama.”

Starting with Grace, everyone bid farewell to Father before boarding the Dragon Palanquin.

“Harold and Cynthia, thank you too. Next time – I’ll probably come again in winter.”

“Yes, Theodore-sama.”

“We’ll be waiting.”

The two gravekeepers bowed deeply.

“Lindwurm.”

When I called out, the Dragon Palanquin rose into the air. I waved from the palanquin window.

As we gradually gained altitude, their figures grew smaller.

“It’s been a while, everyone.”

“Long time no see, Kennel-san.”

As we disembarked from the Dragon Palanquin, Kennel, the butler of the Silun household, greeted us.

Before returning to Termwills, we planned to stop by the Barony of Silun just like before.

“Old man, it’s good to see you looking well.”

“Ashley-sama, your complexion looks even better than before.”

Kennel narrowed his eyes as if looking at something dazzling.

“We stopped by before returning to Termwills.”

While part of it was to pay respects since it’s between the Count’s territory and Termwills, I had another purpose this time.

“Would that be the item we discussed?”

“Yes. The details are as I communicated via the Communication Device.”

In Ashley’s hands was a potted Evil Weed – not Harvesta, but another individual brought from Termwills. This was to show Kennel the actual specimen.

“Hmm. Let me take a look.”

Receiving the pot, Kennel stroked the docile Evil Weed and observed it from various angles.

If we’re going to utilize Evil Weeds in the future, it’s better to lay the groundwork early. I had already explained the general idea to Kennel via the Communication Device, but seeing is believing.

“I see… This is indeed quite docile. When I was young and working in the fields, I got bitten by these fellows many times…”

“It seems they become accustomed to humans if you raise them from seeds using Water Magic. We’re continuing experiments regarding crop cultivation using Evil Weeds.”

Kennel nodded, looking impressed by Ashley’s words.

“My, my. Evil Weeds have long been disliked… But could they become Guardians of agricultural crops?”

“I’m hoping for that too. I think we should have results by early autumn.”

Kennel nodded with a gentle smile.

Well. Judging from Ashley and Kennel’s Communication Device exchanges, the Barony of Silun seems generally peaceful… but just in case, I’ll create an underground passage and evacuation room here too. Better safe than sorry.

“—Coexistence with friendly Monsters, is it?”

Beryne from the Adventurer Guild’s Silun branch was also invited to the dinner table.

Since Ashley and I are engaged, and considering the future, the policies I advocate will inevitably concern the Barony of Silun too. So it’s necessary to properly communicate our intentions.

Bringing the potted Evil Weed also served the purpose of making this reasoning easier to understand.

“That’s right. The Kingdom of Verdugal is also moving forward with such policies. I’m not too worried about the Adventurer Guild’s side, though.”

“Indeed… Stories like adventurers drowning at sea being saved by Sirens and falling in love are quite popular among them.”

Beryne smiled wryly.

“So you’re saying the Monster’s temperament becomes milder depending on the environment? Judging from the Evil Weed, that seems correct.”

“Yes. I thought showing actual examples would be quicker than lengthy explanations. Besides, she’s a Lamia too.”

When I introduced Irmhild, Kennel and Beryne’s gazes turned toward her.

“I’m honored by the introduction. I’m Irmhild the Lamia.”

Irmhild sat up slightly straighter, looking somewhat shy, then smiled bashfully and bowed. Kennel and Beryne seemed surprised, perhaps not having expected this, their eyes widening.

“Um. Should I release the Humanization Spell?”

She tilted her head slightly, looking at Ashley and me.

“Yes. It would be quicker to show the old man.”

With the head of household’s permission, Irmhild moved slightly away from the dining table and released her Humanization Spell.

“This is… astonishing. I see. Indeed… she’s quite a gentle young lady.”

“There are many things you can’t understand unless you actually interact with them.”

“That… I’m keenly aware of that, since I have more opportunities to speak with adventurers these days.”

Kennel smiled wryly like that.

“Um, if it’s alright, I’d like to play a song for you.”

Irmhild took out her Lute, apparently wanting to begin performing. Well, that makes sense. If she wants others to understand her, this is probably the fastest way for her, and an area where she has confidence.

“That… sounds interesting.”

“Indeed.”

Beryne laughed cheerfully while Kennel nodded with a serious expression. Of course for Kennel, but this might be Beryne’s first time meeting a Lamia too.

“Well then…”

Irmhild smiled and began her performance.

The simple sound of the instrument and her clear singing voice. The two immediately became captivated by the melody, listening intently. Yeah. This is going quite well.

Though we had some trouble in the Count’s territory, things seem to be progressing smoothly in the Barony.

+++

# **221 – Marquis Zilbolt**

“Welcome home.”

“We’re relieved to see you safe and sound.”

As the dragon palanquin was lowered in front of the house, Cecilia and Mihaela came out to greet me.

“I’m back. Anything unusual while I was away?”

“Everything’s been peaceful. Everyone worked diligently while you were gone.”

Cecilia smiled happily.

Good. That’s what matters most. We divided up the luggage in the dragon palanquin among ourselves and quickly carried it into the house.

“…Well. I’m sorry to say I’ll need to go out again soon, but I have to visit the Royal Castle for a bit. I also need to return the dragon palanquin.”

“Understood.”

I also need to make my report. I boarded the dragon palanquin and gave Lindwurm an order, who then commanded the other wyverns, and the palanquin began gaining altitude.

The Royal Castle is quickly reached by dragon palanquin. After having the palanquin lowered in front of the stables, I disembarked at the Royal Castle.

Immediately, stablehands gathered and busily began the work of removing equipment from the wyverns and storing away the dragon palanquin. The wyverns, once freed from their gear, were each led by reins back into the Dragon Stable.

As for the temperamental Lindwurm… well, it seems only certain experienced handlers can manage him.

“Welcome back, Ambassador.”

“Ah, Matthew-san.”

Matthew, one of those experienced stablehands, greeted me with a friendly smile.

“How were the wyverns performing?”

“They were quite obedient. Lindwurm seems to be maintaining good control, so I didn’t have much to do.”

“I never thought this one would become so diligent.”

Matthew laughed cheerfully while stroking Lindwurm’s shoulder. Lindwurm seemed to understand he was being talked about and turned his head away. Matthew and I exchanged wry smiles.

“Lindwurm, I have business at the King’s Tower. If you want to come to my house later, feel free.”

At my words, Lindwurm turned his head toward me and vocalized as if in response.

“We’ll handle feeding them here.”

“Thank you, I appreciate it.”

After that exchange, I headed toward the King’s Tower.

This time I’d already communicated my approximate return time in advance, so I probably wouldn’t have to wait long.

As usual, I was shown to the salon to wait, and I noticed some play equipment made by Labyrinth Trading Company artisans placed in one corner.

Hmm… Quite sturdy construction. Since it’s for the Royal Castle, the artisans must have put considerable effort into it.

So this is where they placed the items delivered to the King’s Tower. I heard they were also placing them at the Knight’s Tower, barracks, Guesthouse, and other locations.

“Theodore. You’ve returned.”

While examining the quality of the play equipment, King Melvin arrived in the salon.

“I’ve just returned.”

“Hmm.”

King Melvin nodded and sat at the table. I sat across from him and we proceeded as usual.

“This was your first return home in quite some time, yet here I am being rather ungracious.”

“Not at all. I prefer to think of it as putting out a fire before it could spread.”

When I answered like that, King Melvin gave a wry smile.

“I’ve received the report. Based on that, we’ve also obtained corroboration from those individuals. Marquis Zilbolt’s name has come up again.”

“The connection to the previous incident remains somewhat unclear.”

“Hmm… About that previous incident…”

King Melvin’s expression darkened slightly.

“We were unable to deliver the personal letter to King Eberhart.”

King Eberhart. The king of Silvatoria. According to King Melvin, the king himself is said to rule with good governance.

“Is that… because something unfortunate happened?”

“No, not because of any particular trouble. It seems King Eberhart is bedridden with illness. The envoy simply couldn’t get an audience.”

That’s… Indeed, matters concerning Marquis Zilbolt’s operations and the relationship between Beriondora and the demon aren’t something that can be shown to just anyone. Especially since we don’t know what would happen if the Crown Prince found out.

“Given the nature of the matter, entrusting the personal letter to someone else seems problematic too. Silvatoria’s internal situation is somewhat opaque.”

“Hmm. Actually, I prepared two versions of the personal letter for the envoy. I instructed the envoy that if an audience with King Eberhart couldn’t be arranged, he should deliver the letter with the harmless content. Information that we’ve captured Marquis Zilbolt’s agents could leak before reaching the king, so we must be cautious.”

Conversely… if there are those who would steal and read the personal letter, this would make them think the Kingdom of Verdugal has no information about Marquis Zilbolt, luring them into complacency.

“The bedridden excuse is suspicious too. Could it be a result of the Crown Prince’s blindness?”

“That’s also a possibility we’re considering. Our outreach to Silvatoria will be temporarily suspended. I plan to notify the domestic lords that foreign spies might be operating within their territories engaging in privateering, and urge them to be vigilant.”

“I see…”

It’s a symptomatic treatment, but an effective move. No lord would be happy to see their territory plundered, and even without incidents, attitudes toward bandits would become stricter.

Since it’s specifically about unspecified “foreign spies,” there won’t be any official deterioration of relations with specific countries.

“There’s another problem that’s emerged. The man himself, Marquis Zilbolt, has proposed visiting Termwills to broaden his perspectives.”

“Is that… to make contact with the operatives he sent into Verdugal territory?”

“That’s highly likely.”

…I see. King Melvin’s moves are defensive strategies. If there’s an opportunity to make contact with Marquis Zilbolt, I’d like some… offensive moves.

“…Could I meet with the agents Marquis Zilbolt sent?”

“Hmm. Do you have something in mind?”

“To some extent, yes. I’d like you to hear my thoughts.”

I headed toward the Royal Castle’s underground prison. Naturally, I couldn’t go with King Melvin himself, so Knight Order Commander Mildred accompanied me as escort.

“…You.”

In the cell was Elmer, the Silvatorian Magic Swordsman who had led the operational team. The moment he saw my face from the cell’s bed, he made an indescribably subtle expression.

As prisoners, they’re apparently being treated relatively humanely. After all, we can extract information through Magic Potions and Magical Inquisition. Since they can’t use magic, there’s no need to cause them pain. They seem to be receiving medical treatment too.

I had the cell opened and entered alone to face him.

“I came to ask you a few things.”

“…I have nothing to say, and if it’s what we know, you’ve probably already extracted it. Or is it still not enough?”

“Does the name Donovan or Lionel ring any bells?”

I cut straight to the point without preamble, but Elmer’s expression didn’t change. Those two are also imprisoned… well.

“There’s still important information I haven’t asked about. Both you and Donovan. Why… do you follow someone like Marquis Zilbolt? The Marquis is fully prepared to discard you from the start if you fail, isn’t he?”

At my question after a pause, Elmer made a bitter face.

If it’s because of loyalty to Silvatoria… well, since they’re keeping their relationship secret, they probably can’t talk about it…

Trying to vandalize Mother’s house, attempting to kidnap Father and torture Kathryn to force a confession… I certainly dislike their methods… but despite using such methods, with that many people, not a single one resorted to betrayal or self-preservation.

That inconsistency bothers me. That’s precisely why there’s something I need to confirm here.

In this environment where I’ve handed them over to King Melvin and Magical Inquisition can be used, I don’t have to worry about being deceived.

If these guys have unavoidable circumstances, I’ll arrange some convenience for them. If not, that’s fine too. In that case, as I told King Melvin, I’ll just extract information from them, then borrow Ambrum’s form without reservation and make contact with Marquis Zilbolt to extract information.

“Is there some kind of restraint?”

When I asked, Elmer turned away. A reaction suggesting he wouldn’t answer anything. Well then, I’ll proceed with the conversation as I please.

“For example—are your family members being held hostage?”

The moment I said that, Elmer’s eyes widened and he scrutinized my expression. This—reaction.

“If betrayal is discovered, your family members will be killed? Or that they were executed as kidnappers… Would spreading that kind of information be more beneficial for you guys?”

“You…”

“I have no intention of approving your methods. Even if you had such circumstances, you tried to do the same to us, so frankly, I don’t like it. But… since there’s Magical Inquisition, if you speak honestly, I can trust your words and actions.”

When I said that, Elmer seemed to struggle internally for quite a long time, but eventually opened his mouth.

“That’s… not it. It’s not us who have hostages taken… it’s the Marquis.”

At those words, Mildred and I unintentionally exchanged glances. Mildred, seeming to grasp the situation, had an unpleasant expression mixed on her face. Marquis Zilbolt being held hostage. By whom, exactly?

A foolish question. Probably by Silvatoria’s Crown Prince. Meaning the Marquis is taking on all the dirty work on behalf of the Crown Prince.

“Indeed… Considering what we tried to do… I’m fully aware this is a self-serving request. But… could you please help the Marquis? If a magician of your caliber would help him… perhaps…”

Saying this, Elmer deeply bowed his head and prostrated himself.

+++

# **222 – Witch**

An impromptu Magical Inquisition was conducted on Elmer, Donovan, and Lionel, confirming the details regarding the Marquis Zilbolt incident.

Though Donovan and Lionel initially hesitated to testify, when Elmer and I informed them that if their claims were true, I would work toward helping Marquis Zilbolt, they admitted the facts. After confirming they weren’t spies for the Crown Prince’s faction, we moved the three from their cells to another room for questioning. Mildred continued to accompany us.

“…First, allow me to thank you for our current accommodations,” Lionel said quietly, bowing his head. All three wore solemn expressions.

After baths, shaves, and changes of clothes, their demeanor… indeed appeared to be that of nobility or those close to such status.

Regarding Elmer’s subordinates, they were currently undergoing Magical Inquisition. Once their claims were verified and deemed trustworthy… well, even if we couldn’t remove surveillance and Subjugation Magic, they’d likely be released from their cells.

At the very least… if they were willing to speak in detail about their personal motivations rather than their affiliations, our response would change accordingly.

“I’ll convey your gratitude to His Majesty,” Mildred said.

“Now then… about these hostages – who is holding whom, and how? I’d like to clarify that first.”

“The hostages are… the entire Zilbolt Marquisate.”

The entire territory. What exactly was happening here?

“…That witch… was brought by the Crown Prince,” Elmer murmured haltingly.

“Witch?” Mildred asked with a puzzled expression.

“There’s no other way to describe her. The witch cast Curse Magic on the Marquis’s wife and daughter. While tormenting the two of them, the Crown Prince laughed and said he could crush their hearts anytime, anywhere.”

Elmer’s face twisted bitterly. Apparently, the Crown Prince and the witch had said this to the Marquis while he embraced his suffering wife and daughter.

“You were present at the scene?”

“I was. Donovan and the others haven’t seen the witch’s face,” Elmer said, looking down.

“According to that witch, she also cast Curse Magic on the Spirit protecting the volcano near the Marquisate. She said if we betrayed them, the Spirit would suffer similarly, and the volcano would erupt with lava destroying the town. We don’t know if it’s true or not… but the lives of the Lady and her daughter would certainly be lost. We cannot risk testing this.”

…I see. Marquis Zilbolt is the territory’s lord. Taking just his wife and daughter as hostages wasn’t enough, so they took the entire territory and its people hostage too.

But once they played the eruption card, there would be no turning back or stopping it. By casting Curse Magic on the two members of the Marquis’s family as well, they were threatening gradual destruction if he resisted.

“Since then, we’ve been dogs. We’ve been forced to dirty our hands with various tasks as ordered…”

“The Marquis was targeted because he maintained an Intelligence Unit like ours, I suppose.”

All three wore similarly dark expressions.

“I see… What about Curse Magic on Marquis Zilbolt himself?”

“He shouldn’t have any cast on him. Things like Curse Magic, Subjugation Magic, Contract Magic…”

Right. As a public figure, there would be ways to check if such things had been used on him. That’s precisely why they aimed for indirect control.

“…I see. Then—” That meant contacting Marquis Zilbolt himself was possible.

“D-do you have some method?” Lionel asked, perhaps detecting something in my reaction.

“First, we’ll research how to break or counter the Curse Magic. Then contact Marquis Zilbolt. Work with him on the curse removal. I’m thinking of proposing this approach. For that… I might need your cooperation too.”

“If that’s necessary… we have no choice in the matter.”

Marquis Zilbolt would be coming to Termwills… and during that time, the Crown Prince would likely have surveillance on him. We could have these three make false reports that everything was proceeding smoothly… Well, I’d need to discuss with King Melvin and devise a proper plan.

“Crush their hearts?”

“That’s what the Curse Magic supposedly does. They say the Spirit has also been cursed.”

After reporting to King Melvin, I returned home and made time to consult with everyone. We agreed with King Melvin that curse removal should be our approach.

If we could secure Marquis Zilbolt and Elmer’s cooperation after resolving the problem… it would benefit Verdgar too. Sitting around the low table in the Japanese-style room, I explained what we’d learned.

“Regarding such Curse Magic… I believe it shouldn’t be a problem if we can apprehend the caster. The ability to activate it anytime from anywhere means it’s a Spell Formula activated by the caster’s will. Such methods cannot be incorporated into Contract Magic, right?” Rosemary said.

Right. Indeed.

Apprehending the caster… was a strategy unavailable to Marquis Zilbolt and his associates.

But since we had no apparent connection to Marquis Zilbolt, we could take the hard approach of crushing the witch, the caster, ignoring the hostage situation and its authenticity.

As for neutralizing the witch, there might be differences between taking her life or sealing her magic. But as an opening move, cutting her consciousness down without discussion would probably be best.

“However, to do that, we must first locate the witch herself,” Grace said.

“Yes. If we can solve that problem, that approach should work…”

Creating such a situation proactively might be somewhat difficult, though?

The Crown Prince’s faction probably couldn’t make the witch’s existence public either. Once the hostage problem was resolved, there would be an opening there.

“Do we need the Thieves Guild’s cooperation?” Sheila asked.

Ah, right. The Thieves Guild had someone who could draw facial composites from descriptions.

“That’s right… We should also learn the witch’s appearance. Can you handle that?”

“Leave it to me.”

We could have Elmer and the others describe her appearance to that person later… But we should consider other measures too.

Marlene wore a serious expression, placing her hands over her chest.

Yes, I understood what Marlene wanted to say.

“What about using Blessings to protect those under Curse Magic?”

When I turned my gaze to Claudia, she nodded.

“That’s possible too. If the cursed person or the caster is nearby… we can repel or suppress the Curse Power itself. In that case, we’d need to ensure the Blessing doesn’t break…”

We wouldn’t need to identify the specific Spell Formula or type of Curse Magic.

Since the witch held the command authority to activate the Spell Formula, we just needed to block either the source or the commands themselves.

“Regarding the two members of the Marquis’s family, couldn’t we arrange to have them summoned here?” Ashley said.

Using balls or other events as excuses, we could maneuver for the Marquis to bring them out himself. Since they’d be coming here under the pretense of deepening understanding or promoting friendship, they’d have no choice but to accept invitations.

“I think that’s possible. Then… the biggest problem would be the Spirit, right?”

“If it’s a Spirit capable of controlling a volcano, we know its location and origin. I think we could summon it using Summoning Magic. However, within Termwills, it would be confined by the Barrier. In this case, we might need to perform the ritual outside the outer walls.”

“…Spirits and Summoning Magic. We might need Auria-san’s cooperation for this too.”

“I’ll help as well!” Seraphina said, clenching her fist and standing up on the table. When I nodded, she nodded back. Perhaps she had thoughts about the volcano lord’s current situation. She’d likely be helpful in communicating with the Spirit too.

Blessings would also be necessary. That meant we’d need to coordinate with Penelope and work to cover both the Marquis’s family and the volcano Spirit.

Anyway, the advantage was that we didn’t need to go out and set traps. Ideally, by the time they noticed, the hostages would be freed and the witch’s composite sketch prepared.

The hostages protected. By the time the witch realized countermeasures against her Curse Magic were in place, we’d have already issued warrants throughout the Zilbolt Marquisate.

Marquis Zilbolt would arrive slightly before the Magic Light Water Vein’s gate opened. That meant we could continue preparing for both situations in parallel.

Creating a ritual site to summon and contain the Spirit. A place for the Shrine Maidens to stay. We’d also need barracks for soldiers and Knights to protect the Shrine Maidens.

We might get somewhat busy, but the burden before Marquis Zilbolt’s arrival wasn’t actually that heavy. More importantly, we should meticulously arrange the steps for after he arrives.

+++

# **223 – Ritual Site**

“They’re coming!”

Along with Sheila’s words, countless twisted spear-tip-like shells shot out from the water, drilling forward at high speed while spinning like drills.

Lance Shells. Shell monsters that inhabit the Magic Light Water Vein. Regardless of whether they’re in water or on the surface, these monsters propel themselves by spraying water from their bodies and impale their targets with their shells.

Their shells are distinctive—essentially, they’re giant turban shells.

They were caught in the sticky net Sheila released and Rosemary’s magic threads. When their movements stopped, Dullahan and Ignis charged in from the side and shattered them with a flash of their greatswords.

This was combat-style training in the Magic Light Water Vein. The plan was to fight in both underwater and waterway environments to get accustomed to the terrain and combat here. The area we stepped into was a large chamber. There was a small island in the center, surrounded by water on all sides. It was terrain that obviously looked like a trap, but that’s exactly what made it good training.

Facing the Gillmen emerging one after another from the water were Ashley and Lavigne, plus the team of Irmhild and Seraphina.

Unlike the Merfolk with their fish-like lower bodies, the Gillmen were bipedal Fishfolk. This meant they could operate on land as well. Like the Merfolk, they wielded tridents as weapons, and they could also shoot water bullets, making them capable of both close and long-range combat.

“Seraphina-chan!”

“Mm-hmm!”

But we weren’t going to fight them properly. An arrow wrapped in a cursed melody passed through the Gillmen with a high-pitched sound, causing them to become confused and start attacking each other. Then came the ice storm from Ashley and Lavigne.

The Gillmen that escaped the effect of Irmhild’s arrow tried to retaliate by throwing their tridents or shooting water bullets—but they were either attacking illusions created by Marlene, or their attacks were deflected by saucers when aimed at real targets… None of their attacks reached us.

Our side’s defense was perfect. Dullahan and Sheila, having dealt with the Lance Shells, charged in. They scattered them with their charge, and Sheila sliced up any Gillmen that escaped. At this rate… the Gillmen would be wiped out soon.

Grace was facing a giant mantis shrimp about human height—a Grand Squilla. It approached Grace while swaying its brightly colored body in vivid reds and blues.

Despite its size, it had impressive speed even on land. The so-called mantis shrimp punch was still effective at this size. Back in the BFO days, there were scenes where tank roles who failed to block it would get sent flying.

The giant twin fists struck at Grace with bullet-like force. Grace met them head-on. Fist and axe collided, producing an absurdly loud impact sound.

The mantis shrimp’s upper body was thrown back, and Grace was also sent flying backward. Both immediately recovered. They clashed again. The mantis shrimp twisted its body, slamming down the edge of its tail shell like a blade.

“Haa!”

She deployed a shield from her magic tool onto the sole of her foot. She kicked to stop the tail, then stepped in. With a flash of her axe wrapped in fighting spirit, she sliced off the mantis shrimp’s bulging eyes, sending them flying through the air. The mantis shrimp thrashed about wildly.

“Ignis!”

At Rosemary’s call, Grace retreated by jumping back, and as if switching places, Ignis charged in with perfect timing. It plunged in from the direction of the sliced-off eyes—the blind spot—and slammed down its great hammer, which had the appearance of a crude metal block. The hammer crushed through the shell and smashed about half of the body before the mantis shrimp stopped moving.

That great hammer was a weapon that functioned in conjunction with the pile bunker. The concept was to pulverize into dust whatever was pierced through the armor.

As for me—I was dealing with the Thunder Kraken while jumping around on the water’s surface. True to its name, it was a giant squid that attacked with lightning strikes.

I weaved through the tentacles emerging one after another from the water. While blocking the lightning strikes bursting from the tentacles with my shield, I jumped left and right as if threading between them.

The lightning strikes seemed to require charging. I identified the opening after each strike and leaped high, timing it with Nemea’s bite.

The tentacles pulled taut, tangled, and formed knots. I froze them in place with water magic, connecting them to the wall. With it unable to dodge or escape, I raised Ouroboros and deployed a magic circle.

“Penetrate.”

Sixth-tier earth magic, Crystal Lance. A spell that launches a giant crystal spear. I fired the spear toward the Kraken’s head peeking above the water. Without any resistance—it pierced through both the tentacles that tried to block it and impaled the Thunder Kraken’s head. The Kraken struggled briefly to escape but soon went limp and lost its strength.

“Are you injured?”

After roughly eliminating the monsters, Grace asked.

“I’m fine. What about everyone else?”

“We’re fine. No injuries,” Ashley reported after checking everyone’s condition.

“What about Ignis?”

When asked, Rosemary checked Ignis by having it raise its arms and various other parts before answering. “No problems here either.”

Hmm. No particular losses, then. That’s good. All that’s left is harvesting… but as usual, what we get from the Magic Light Water Vein is mostly ingredients.

Lance Shells taste like turban shells, and both the mantis shrimp and squid are edible, of course. I’ve heard that giant squid aren’t very suitable for eating, but there’s no problem with Krakens.

Well… Gillmen don’t really whet the appetite… I’ll just collect their magic stones.

“Can… this be eaten?”

“Ah, the Grand Squilla? Despite its appearance, it’s delicious… I think.”

Sheila seems to have more trouble with the mantis shrimp than with Gillmen. I can understand that.

Still, it’s an amount of seafood that we definitely can’t finish eating. Well, we can just sell the excess at the Guild, so let’s finish the harvesting quickly.

“Hello.”

“Hello, Theodore-san.”

We headed to the Guild to sell the ingredients. The receptionist Heather smiled and processed the purchase of the ingredients for us.

After receiving the payment, Heather said, “Theodore-san, I have a message for you from the Guild Master. She asked me to tell you that preparations at the construction site are complete.”

“…Meaning?”

“Yes. It seems all the materials have been gathered. The Guild Master said she was going to contact Penelope-sama at the Temple and go see the construction site, but…”

The construction site referred to the planned location for building the ritual site to summon the volcano spirit.

We had been collecting the necessary materials. I planned to handle the ritual site construction using magic construction. Referring to Claudia and Auria’s opinions, I also created a scaled-down model using earth magic.

“Then I’ll go check it out.”

“Is that so? In that case, could you please tell the Guild Master to come back early after having lunch? Since it’s cooled down and become pleasantly cool today, I think she’s just using the preliminary inspection as an excuse to go out and have fun.”

Heather smiled wryly as she said that. I got the impression that she was quite accustomed to Auria’s behavior and how to handle her.

“Is that so?”

“Well, Auria-sama may be like that, but she works hard when it really counts, so it’s fine.”

I see. It seems she’s trusted by Heather and the others.

So I headed outside Termwills’ barrier—to the planned construction site for the ritual site.

“Hello.”

“Oh, Theodore.”

“Ah, Theo-kun.”

“Hello, everyone.”

At the planned construction site, there was a rest hut and gazebo I had made beforehand. Auria and Penelope were there, along with the Forestbird members who had probably been asked to serve as guards. When I greeted them, they returned the greeting with relaxed expressions. Marlene happily ran over to Penelope. Penelope welcomed Marlene with a smile.

The necessary materials were all gathered and stacked by type. All that remained was to assemble them according to the blueprint into a summoning ritual site for welcoming the spirit using magic construction.

“Heather-san was calling for you. She said she’d like you to come back after having lunch.”

“Hmm. Understood.”

When I relayed Heather’s message, Auria smiled wryly.

“But it would be bothersome to go back now just for lunch, wouldn’t it? We got various ingredients from the Magic Light Water Vein—how about it?”

“Oh ho.”

As expected, Auria showed interest.

We had plenty of seafood today—turban shells, squid, and mantis shrimp. Along with other ingredients bought from the market, we began cooking.

I made a hearth with earth magic, lit a fire with wood and fire magic, and placed the turban shells and squid on a wire grill bought from the market to roast them.

As for the mantis shrimp, we boiled the cut pieces and then mixed them with pasta and sauce, or made them into fried dishes. Grace was in charge of making the sauce.

The savory aroma of turban shells and squid roasting on the wire grill wafted through the air. Hmm. It looks like we’re going to have quite a luxurious lunch.

“Mmm. This sauce is exquisite.”

Monica of Forestbird widened her eyes as she tasted the food. The tomato-based sauce sprinkled with herbs had a vibrant color that was pleasing to the eye as well.

“Thank you.”

Grace smiled gently. It was lunchtime, with everyone gathered around the circular table in the gazebo.

“Lance Shells are tasty too. Eating stuff like this makes us want to go to the Magic Light Water Vein as well.”

“If you’ve got countermeasures prepared, aiming for it might not be a bad idea.”

We were using magic tools with built-in magic shields too, and with proper underwater combat preparations, I thought Forestbird could probably handle it.

“Only when Alfred-kun isn’t busy, perhaps.”

Lucian smiled wryly.

Hmm… Alfred is quite busy making the magic tools for the equipment around the ritual site.

“Theo-kun, you’re doing magic construction again, right?”

“Ah. The ritual site.”

“I slipped out because I wanted to see that. Since the materials are gathered, it’ll be done in no time.”

Auria said with a somewhat disappointed expression. Ah. So that’s why she slipped out.

“Then I’ll get started after lunch. I don’t think it’ll take that much time either.”

Since they seem to be expecting it, I’ll treat it as a service.

Not just the ritual site, but I also planned to build facilities where shrine maidens could stay to keep the spirit contained.

It would be wasteful to just abandon it after it’s served its purpose… Maybe I should think of some way to repurpose it.

+++

# **224 – Visit**

Well then. First, the ritual site.

I compress the foundation with Earth Magic, then reinforce it by solidifying it with Petrification Magic. I carve grooves into the foundation, sprinkle finely crushed Magic Stones into them, and draw a Summoning and Barrier Magic Array to contain the Spirit.

“Please check it from above for now.”

“Understood.”

Claudia nods and ascends to a height where she can oversee the entire area along with Rosemary. Auria follows suit. I’m having them verify the Magic Array as a precaution. Since this is the core part of the ritual site, mistakes would be troublesome to fix, and when it comes to Summoning Magic, the three of them are more knowledgeable.

“Rise.”

I make the Earth Golems stand up and have them transport materials one after another.

I lay cobblestones in a circular pattern, build an altar facing the direction of the volcano, and erect walls and pillars.

Once that much is completed, the three descend from above.

Next is the roof. I create a dome-shaped roof, carve a celestial chart on the inside, and embed Magic Stones at positions corresponding to major stars. Changing the size of the Magic Stones according to the size of the stars is subtly tedious and complicated.

This is a celestial chart of the summer night sky—matched to the season for summoning the volcano’s Spirit.

It’s a reinforcement to create a pseudo-cycle of the stars, sustain the effect of the Summoning Magic, and keep the Spirit within the ritual site. Well… it does somewhat resemble a planetarium.

“How about this for the celestial chart?”

“Yes. It’s well done.”

After that, I add decorations to the walls and pillars to reinforce the Spirit’s power and weaken Curse Power. The Emblems of the Four Great Spirit Kings and the symbol of the Moon Goddess.

“What about the building’s strength?”

“It’s fine. Hmm. Somehow… I feel power welling up when I’m here.”

Seraphina nods and happily flies around inside the ritual site.

“I’d imagine so. I think this could almost be called a Temple.”

“The Magical Power and Spirit power gathering here are being Cleansed.”

Penelope and Auria say. Well… I’ll have to alter the Labyrinth’s system later on, so I need to be capable of at least this much.

“I suppose that covers the ritual site. Next, I’ll develop the area around it.”

“What else will you do?”

Penelope asks.

“I’ll recreate a scaled-down version of the terrain around the volcano in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory. The ritual site corresponds to the location of the mountain itself… and after that, I plan to create something like a garden surrounding the ritual site.”

I’ve grasped the surrounding terrain through interviews with Elmer and the others. This is also just a matter of building according to the Blueprint. I’m magically preparing an environment where the volcano’s Spirit can reside long-term without stress.

Once the garden is made, I plan to build facilities where Shrine Maidens and Clerics can stay, as well as facilities where their Escorts—Knights and soldiers—can reside. The temporary huts currently in place are actually positioned corresponding to locations in the Marquis’s territory, so it should be fine to proceed by renovating those temporary huts.

“Hmm… I would have liked to see it through to completion if possible, but I’ve seen enough interesting things already. I’ll save the rest for when it’s finished. I’ve already been treated to lunch as well. I must repay you in some form eventually.”

Auria seems quite pleased.

“Yes. I’ve thoroughly partaken of your hospitality.”

Penelope bows deeply. Since the two give the impression they’ll be returning to the city soon, Forestbird and the others also begin preparing to withdraw.

“Yeah. Theo-kun, Grace-san. It was delicious, thank you.”

The members of Forestbird also bow.

Lately, they’ve had work like escorting Justia and Dominique, so their income seems stable. They’ve also become acquainted with Auria and Penelope, and their adventurer business appears to be going well.

“Well then.”

“Yes. Please be careful on your way.”

With that, we part ways with Auria and the others. Well, even though “on your way” is said, Termwills is just a stone’s throw away.

“Is that the Witch’s bust?”

“Well, yes. I modeled it in 3D based on the portrait…”

Since the facilities around the ritual site that can be done with Magic Construction are completed, the rest is Alfred’s job.

While reporting the ritual site’s progress after stopping by the workshop, I’m creating the Witch’s bust from the portrait entrusted to me by Sheila.

First, I make a prototype sculpture from stone, have Elmer—who knows the Witch’s face—check it, and make adjustments. Then I create a mold, and after that, it’s just a matter of mass-producing plaster busts.

“You’re making quite a number of them.”

Viola says.

“Well… I plan to deploy them all over the place. Using Curse Magic for threats—if that happened to us, it’d be unbearable. It’ll have to wait until the hostages are protected, but I’ll make it so widely known within Verdgar that movement and shopping become difficult.”

Setting aside the connection with Silvatoria’s Crown Prince, I’ll publicize it openly so she can never operate in the shadows again.

“Theo-kun is as thorough as ever…”

“I plan to have Marquis Zilbolt take some with him after it’s resolved too. To the extent that even Silvatoria’s Crown Prince can’t protect her… or rather, I intend to do it with enough force to undermine the Crown Prince’s standing.”

When I answer, Alfred gives a slightly strained smile and says,

“It seems there’s been a reply from that Marquis Zilbolt too. In a letter, he says he’d be delighted to accept the invitation.”

“Then I suppose we can consider the preliminary preparations complete.”

“I need to prepare Magic Tools for the ritual site, though.”

Saying that, Alfred stretches. Things like Alarm Devices to install in the lodging facilities and setting up Defense Fields in the underground shelter rooms.

There are also Magic Tools for heating, cooling, and baths, but those areas don’t require relying on Alfred.

“Won’t that be quite tough starting now? You mass-produced the Amulets of Evil Repulsion too, right?”

Since the opponent is a Witch who can use Curse Magic.

While the Amulet of Evil Repulsion might not completely block powerful Curse Magic… there are parts where synergy with Blessing can aim for improvement.

“Not really. Talcott and Cindy are helping too, and there are Rosemary’s Dolls, so it’s relatively manageable.”

“I see.”

“What about reusing the ritual site? Can it be utilized as a facility for Summoning Rituals?”

“I haven’t decided on that yet. Since it’s specialized for accommodating the volcano’s Spirit, if we want to make it a versatile summoning facility, we’ll need to renovate it after the resolution.”

In any case, Marquis Zilbolt’s visit is coming soon.

The liberation of the Sealed Door is also schedule-wise close, and I must not neglect preparations like training.

And then—the day of Marquis Zilbolt’s visit to Termwills arrived.

The Marquis is said to be coming by ship, using the sea route. I wait at the port with Elmer, who has his hood pulled deep over his eyes. Mercedes from the Knight Order is also accompanying us as Elmer’s supervisor.

If we were ensuring absolute safety, we’d give Elmer a Disguise Ring or something… but that’s originally for the Verdgar royal family.

Once the incident is resolved, Elmer and the others will likely be returned to Marquis Zilbolt’s custody, so I can’t reveal the Ring. Lending it to me is truly an exception.

“He’s here.”

From beyond the horizon. A ship carrying Marquis Zilbolt approaches, bathed in the setting sun.

…Hmm.

I create a lens and tube with Light and Dark Magic, magically reproducing a telescope. Let’s magnify and scout the deck. It’s blurry, but I’ll adjust… is this good?

“Wh-what is that Magic…?”

“Th-this is…”

Elmer’s eyes widen. Mercedes’s too. Mercedes is also from the Knight Order, and Elmer is from a special unit, so they undoubtedly understand its utility. It would certainly be useful for Scout purposes.

“Hmm. Well, improvised. More importantly, any familiar faces?”

“Uh, well…”

Elmer watches the circular, floating image of the deck with a slightly strained expression.

“…It’s the Marquis.”

The man who came up from the cabin to the deck was well-built. A man of average height and build with white mixed into his hair. The one led out by Marquis Zilbolt holding her hand is the Marchioness. Next to the Marchioness is the Marquis’s daughter.

The Marchioness and the daughter look pale and not very healthy. The daughter’s hat is about to be blown away by the wind, but the Marquis catches it and, narrowing his eyes as if looking at something troublesome, returns it to the daughter.

The daughter, receiving the hat with a shy smile, clings to the Marchioness as if frightened of something.

I follow where her gaze is directed.

“…This bitch… this bitch is…”

Elmer gasps and grits his teeth. Who it is—I know without him saying. I know that face too. I mass-produced it in the workshop.

It’s the young woman dressed all in black who came up from the cabin. Glaring at the Marquis’s family, a cold smile plastered on her face.

“So she came aboard herself.”

I have Caduceus operate the Communication Device to notify all locations of the Witch’s visit.

I had assumed this might be possible. Since she’s bringing the two hostages along, it’s entirely possible that she herself—who can activate Curse Magic—would come as the supervisor.

The agents dispatched by Marquis Zilbolt—Donovan and Lionel—their objective was securing a base.

They seemed to have been told that their purpose was to disrupt public order within Verdgar—but it can’t be just that. Considering that the Witch is behind this and looking at the map… it’s known that there’s a dormant volcano near the town where Mihaela lives.

It’s highly likely they intend to do the same thing in Verdgar as in the Marquis’s territory, while also surveilling Marquis Zilbolt.

I can’t afford to be careless here. I’ll need to place surveillance on the Witch and move early, before she acts, to protect the hostages.

…It seems the Witch has a companion too. A man with a sword is standing by as if guarding her. I should put surveillance on him as well.

+++

# **225 – Spirit of the Volcano**

“First—the spirit, I suppose.”

“What about the witch?”

“I’ve contacted them and left surveillance behind.”

After answering, Elmer glanced around, but Caduceus had already moved on.

The companions seemed to be guarding the witch’s surroundings… and in the town, the Knight Order and Thieves Guild had posted wanted posters and were keeping watch. We won’t let her escape.

First, we’ll summon the spirit at the ritual site. The spirit has the highest priority. Contacting Marquis Zilbolt and ensuring the safety of his wife and daughter would be the next stage.

“Then let’s move. Elmer-san, we’ll need your help when explaining things to Marquis Zilbolt.”

“Yes.”

We had planned to have them submit false reports and conduct information manipulation operations… but since the witch herself came, we won’t let her escape Termwills, so there’s no need to make them think things are going smoothly.

Taking the two with us, we boarded the carriage and headed to the ritual site.
