Marquis Zilbolt, who had arrived at the docks, also seemed to be heading to an inn by carriage with the witches. A high-class inn catering to nobles in central Termwills. Well… this is also according to plan.

Originally, they were supposed to visit Termwills at the same time, with Elmer and Donovan reporting to Marquis Zilbolt, or so the arrangement went.

We passed through the gate and headed to the ritual site. All the Party Members were gathered there with Auria, Penelope, and the Shrine Maidens. Given that important figures were currently gathered at the ritual site, we had everyone provide escort assuming it might become a target for attack.

“Did the witch herself appear?”

Grace asked with a somewhat tense expression.

“Yeah. I saw her with my own eyes. But it went according to plan.”

“Understood.”

We need to go meet Marquis Zilbolt directly, taking Claudia and Marlene with us. That way we can counter the witch’s Curse Magic on the spot. Which means there’s a high possibility of combat. Having Elmer and the others arrange the meeting and storming in with Party Members would probably be the quickest way.

“First, the volcano spirit—Tephra.”

The volcano spirit of Marquis Zilbolt’s territory is called Tephra, after the mountain itself. For the people living in Silvatoria to the north, it seems to be a volcano that provides blessings to overcome the harsh winters.

“Then—shall we begin?”

“I’m ready.”

“Same here.”

“We’re fine too.”

At Claudia’s words, Rosemary, Auria, and Penelope nodded.

“O dweller of the distant northern lands, master of the fiery mountain. Spirit Tephra. Answer my call. By the guidance of the moon and stars, appear before me.”

I raised the Ritual Rapier toward the Altar and began the incantation. Claudia, Rosemary, and Auria stood one step behind, chanting the same words. Marlene and Penelope knelt, offering prayers to the spirit. Then the Shrine Maidens.

The Magic Array glowed in the center of the ritual site. The stars in the celestial map twinkled. In the center of the ritual site, a flickering flame. At first a small flame. Then it became raging infernal flames, taking form while raining ash around as it manifested.

It was a half-human, half-beast woman with blazing fiery hair. Though she stood on two legs, her lower body had goat-like hooves. Mt. Tephra has wild goats, and they’re said to be the spirit’s messengers.

Mountain worship, I suppose. Given she’s revered by the locals, you could tell she was a spirit of considerable status. Perhaps it would be better to view her as closer in nature to an earth mother goddess or local deity rather than just a spirit.

As Tephra manifested, Claudia and the others’ chanting changed. That is, to words for casting a Barrier to keep the spirit in this place.

“Who… summons me?”

Tephra groaned, clutching her chest along with the flickering flames.

Something like a black rose could be seen on her chest. It felt alien and discordant with the spirit’s form. —That was probably the Curse itself.

“Human… child. Not content with driving a curse stake into me, now you seek to bind me… further?”

Seeing me holding the Ritual Rapier, Tephra furrowed her brows in pain.

Being a volcano, blessings and calamities are two sides of the same coin, and people’s fear and reverence probably gave Tephra such qualities.

So, Tephra, who had been cursed, wouldn’t harbor good feelings toward humans even if summoned by Summoning Magic.

That’s precisely why, during the Summoning Ritual, I stand at the very front holding the Ritual Rapier. Because the one holding the Ritual Rapier receives the most attention from the summoned being.

If we anger the volcano spirit, she’d probably launch lava bombs or volcanic bombs without hesitation. As expected, she seemed to be growing distrustful of humans.

“That’s not it. I summoned you here to destroy the stake piercing your chest and free you from the curse.”

Flames swirled. Blazing flames seemed to be born in her palm, then she swung and released them. But before reaching the Altar, they were blocked by an invisible wall and scattered.

The flames themselves weren’t on a trajectory to hit us either. Rather than malice, it should be seen as showing rejection or intimidation. Room for negotiation—there’s plenty.

“You speak boldly from a safe place protected by a barrier. Do you expect me to believe a magician’s words?”

“Are you dissatisfied that I’m outside the summoning barrier?”

When I stepped into the summoning barrier, Tephra seemed taken aback, as if she hadn’t expected it, showing a bewildered expression. Anyway, this way I’m neither protected by the Spell Formula nor at a disadvantage; we’re equal.

Since she’s been betrayed once, I have to show sincerity too. Especially in my case, since it’s hard to say I’m acting purely for Tephra’s sake.

So I leave the role of calming the spirit and easing her pain to Marlene and Penelope and the others.

My role as the summoner is different from Penelope and the others. It’s to confidently state our position and be recognized by the other party as worthy of forming a contract or such as the summoner.

“Do you… mock me?”

“No. I’m doing this so you’ll know I speak only the truth. The one who drove the curse stake into you is using the threat of eruption as a Shield to intimidate others. If things don’t go their way, they threaten others by saying they’ll use that stake to make you erupt with that pain and anger.”

“The affairs of human children… are none of my concern.”

Scorching heat. Blazing air dyeing the ritual site crimson. Paying it no mind, when I took a step forward, Tephra took a step back. That—didn’t seem like she was intimidated by me.

“Even though those who adored you will weep, and those who mocked you will laugh without a single scratch? Even your anger and pain are in the palm of their hands. Would a spirit with such power accept that?”

Though a volcano, she brings blessings. Hence feared and revered. Then Tephra must also harbor qualities of compassion. Because I stepped forward, she stepped back to avoid burning me. That’s how her earlier movement looked.

To make her believe my words, I have no choice but to believe in Tephra. We faced each other, staring for a while, but Tephra shook her head and spoke.

“…What… do you ask of me?”

Tephra glanced behind me for a moment. There stood Seraphina, praying together with Marlene. Along with the Shrine Maidens’ prayers, Seraphina’s feelings must be reaching her too.

“I want you to stay in this place for a while. I will definitely break that curse. Won’t you believe that?”

“Break the curse—”

The heat weakened. Her blazing hair calmed down, now merely clad in a soft, warm phosphorescence.

“Did you… prepare this place?”

Tephra looked around and asked.

“Yeah.”

“To welcome me, and keep me here? Well done, indeed. No wonder that little Fairy adores you.”

Tephra narrowed her eyes and laughed. Then she became serious and said,

“Can you swear you will not deceive me? If so, you and I shall be allies. Only if it’s a request from an ally could I obey your words.”

—An alliance contract.

“Upon my name, I swear. Theodore Gartner makes Spirit Tephra his ally and will speak no falsehood to you.”

“—Very well. Then I shall remain in this place.”

Tephra nodded. The contract was established, so the Summoning Magic barrier was released. The Shrine Maidens’ prayers enveloped Tephra in a Blessing. A radiance to counter Curse Magic.

“An alliance with a High Spirit, huh. Stepping inside the barrier during the ritual—that takes some nerve-chilling courage.”

Auria said with a wry smile.

“Well, she’s not a Demon but a spirit revered by humans.”

If she’s revered, she must have the magnanimity to match. Mt. Tephra also seems to have a relatively calm nature rather than being a raging volcano. Apparently, hot springs are famous in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory.

“Then, we will take turns offering prayers for the blessing.”

“Yes. For a while, it’ll be troublesome, but please take care of it.”

I nodded back to Penelope.

“Tephra, it’s fine if you walk around the garden surrounding the ritual site.”

“Understood.”

The gazebo outside and such were made so Tephra could stay there, and we arranged the garden so she could feel at ease. As long as she receives the blessing here, she should be alright for now.

But this doesn’t mean we’re done. First, the spirit. Next, the members of the Zilbolt household. If the witch detects us, there’s a risk she’ll activate her Curse Magic. It’s still a situation where we can’t let our guard down, a phase requiring swift action. I made eye contact with everyone, and we nodded at each other.

+++

# **226 – Curse**

“I heard the witch has appeared.”

“Yes. We’ve also secured the spirits’ safety.”

Chester and others in civilian clothes, along with the Knight Order and Mage Corps, appeared in the ritual site. It was time for the guard shift. After conveying the necessary information, we headed toward the central district.

Everyone being in civilian clothes was intended to avoid detection of personnel movements. Weapons and armor had been transported to the lodging facilities at the ritual site beforehand. Though few in number, we carefully selected personnel skilled in aerial combat gear and made efforts to ensure the city’s movements wouldn’t become noticeably hectic.

“So we’re heading over there now… The ambassador works quickly as always.”

“We don’t want to give the other side time to gather information.”

When I answered, Chester gave a wry smile.

“Is she that spirit?”

Looking toward Tephra chatting with the shrine maidens in the gazebo, Chester asked.

“Yes. Her name is Tephra. While she has a gentle personality, please don’t forget she’s a High Spirit. The shrine maidens are knowledgeable about interacting with spirits, so if you have any questions, it would be best to ask them.”

“Understood.”

At my words, Chester and the others nodded with solemn expressions.

Heading to the central district inn where Marquis Zilbolt was staying were all the party members including myself, Elmer, and Donovan.

Since Ignis and others would stand out regardless, we would travel by carriage.

We anticipated possible combat. Grace was in her Released Form. We covered conspicuous items like weapons with cloth and used Marlene’s Lantern to make them appear as small hand luggage.

“Welcome. Welcome to Kotosoutei. Are you here for lodging?”

It was a large inn. True to its high-class nature, the staff carried themselves with the dignity of aristocratic household servants. While it featured the stone architectural style typical of the central district, the interior seemed considerably modified, giving off a mansion-like atmosphere.

“We’d like to see Marquis Zilbolt. Please tell him Elmer has arrived.”

“Understood. Please wait a moment.”

When Elmer conveyed this, the inn employee bowed and headed toward the guest rooms.

Now. The real problem begins. According to Caduceus’s surveillance, the Marquis Zilbolt household had taken three rooms at this inn.

First, the room for the marquis’s family to stay together. Next, the room for the servants they likely brought to attend to their needs. And finally, the room for the witch and her escort – three rooms total.

The question is how Marquis Zilbolt will react upon hearing of Elmer’s visit.

That is, where will they talk? And will the witch be present?

We need to carefully investigate with Caduceus, closely watch the movements of the marquis and staff, and time our actions to match their return from the guest room to the front desk.

If the witch is to be present, we’re prepared to take rooms as guests rather than as Elmer’s companions. Depending on the situation, we’ve even considered using Teleportation Magic to take the marquis’s family away late at night when everyone is asleep, then explaining the circumstances at our leisure. In that case, well, we’d just have to convince them it was an emergency.

From the shadows in the ceiling, Caduceus continued monitoring the guest rooms.

An employee emerged from Marquis Zilbolt’s room. Caduceus continued surveillance, but the marquis – didn’t come out. This likely means we’ll be called to his room.

After a while, the employee returned from the guest room. With an elegant bow, they said:

“Marquis Zilbolt has instructed me to escort you to his room. Please, this way.”

Following the employee’s guidance, we all headed toward Marquis Zilbolt’s room.

“Marquis. I’ve brought Lord Elmer.”

“Enter.”

When the employee knocked and called out, a response came immediately from inside the room. Well then.

“Excuse us.”

Following Elmer, we entered the room.

The guest room was quite spacious. Besides the main bedroom and living room, there seemed to be several other rooms, but only the marquis appeared to be in the living room. When he noticed our presence, he looked puzzled.

“I’ve come with my subordinates.”

While having Elmer continue with appropriate words, I used Wind Magic to block sound so we wouldn’t be heard from the witch’s room side.

“My apologies.”

“…Oh? You’ve silenced the sound?”

The moment he saw my Magic Circle, Marquis Zilbolt grabbed the staff by the table and took a defensive Stance. So the marquis himself is a magician.

Though I wasn’t using any disguise, being able to discern the spell’s nature from the Magic Circle shows he’s truly worthy of being a Silvatoria noble.

“‘Subordinates’ is just a convenient explanation. We don’t want the room next door hearing our conversation.”

To show we meant no harm, I handed Ouroboros to Grace and bowed.

“What does this mean?”

The marquis remained on guard. Meanwhile, Elmer was outside the sound-blocking range, telling fabricated achievements about the mission going well. Donovan stepped forward to take over Elmer’s words.

“We were defeated by Sir Theodore here and captured by the Kingdom of Verdugal. We failed our mission and even sought help from a neighboring country. We will certainly accept punishment for our failure. But please, listen to what Sir Theodore has to say.”

“…Very well.”

Marquis Zilbolt nodded, then stepped outside the sound-blocking range before speaking.

“Well done, Elmer. I can’t offer much reward here, but at least let me serve some tea. Please relax and take your time.”

“Thank you, Marquis Zilbolt.”

Elmer bowed.

The marquis temporarily set his staff aside with a “for now” expression, then gestured for us to sit at the table.

Now, persuasion must be done quickly. Direct and concise. And if rejected, we’ll resort to force. We can get their understanding afterward.

If he chooses the crown prince over his wife and daughter, or rejects our proposal out of loyalty to Silvatoria – then we’ll simply detain him as an enemy.

“Due to the dangerous situation, I’ll explain the process later. I heard about the hostage situation. We’ve taken countermeasures using the Moon Goddess’s Blessing to deflect Curse Magic. The spirit Tephra is protected at the ritual site.”

“Wha-at?”

Taken aback by the sudden information, the marquis looked shocked.

“We’d like to protect your wife and Young Lady who were taken hostage by the witch’s Curse Magic using similar methods.”

At my words, Marquis Zilbolt shifted his gaze to Elmer and the others. Elmer and Donovan looked straight at Marquis Zilbolt and nodded.

“If I want to change the current situation, I should bet on you. Is that what this means?”

“Yes.”

Seeing is believing. I should show my hand.

“Marlene, can you do it?”

When I glanced at her, she nodded and made a praying gesture. The blessing’s effect reached everyone in the room.

“Th-this blessing’s strength…? M-Marlene – Third Princess, Your Highness?”

He seemed to have figured it out, but probably couldn’t believe it. As the marquis stared wide-eyed, Marlene smiled and picked up her skirt hem to make a greeting gesture. This part was impressive – truly befitting royalty. For a girl Marlene’s age, this wasn’t a gesture that could be learned overnight.

Well, the blessing’s strength was partly due to Marlene’s own abilities as a shrine maiden plus Claudia’s full cooperation, but there’s no need to reveal that.

The marquis seemed dumbfounded but then pressed his hand to his forehead as if enduring a headache, let out a dry laugh, and stood up. By then the smile was gone, replaced by the face of a lord.

“The two of them are in the bedroom. Please help us, help our people. I no longer have the power to do so.”

“Leave it to us.”

I nodded at his words.

When the count called out to the adjacent room, his wife and daughter peeked out.

That’s when it happened. Wind blew into the room through a window gap, making the curtains sway.

There – I saw her. Beyond the terrace. Floating in the air – a woman dressed in black – the witch. Our eyes met. Seeing us enveloped in blessing light, she showed an expression of shock.

Though we had soundproofing… camouflage isn’t perfect either. She must have sensed something abnormal in the adjacent room.

“A blessing? Are you prepared for this, Marquis?!”

The witch widened her eyes, bared her teeth, and laughed.

“Wha–!?”

Marquis Zilbolt cried out as a Magic Circle glowed in the witch’s hand. A spell formula I’d never seen before. Probably that was Curse Magic –

When I made a Magic Circle glow in my hand, the witch seemed to hesitate for a moment between dodging or activating her curse.

But. The witch thrust out her hand and clenched her fist. That likely had the effect of crushing the target’s heart.

However – the witch then showed a stunned expression. She must have felt no resistance.

“Y-you bastard!”

She gritted her teeth as if grinding them, glaring at me.

Yes. Once Marlene activated her blessing. And once we directly met the wife and daughter. That already meant our victory.

Blessings come through prayer. To make them stronger, you need to know the other person more deeply and specifically. For example, knowing their face, circumstances, or the issues they face.

We had to counter the witch’s Curse Magic. That’s exactly why we needed to meet directly.

“You didn’t forget the other curse–“

“Rather than worrying about the spirit, why don’t you worry about yourself?”

The witch started to say something, but I cut her off. Even if I hadn’t stopped her midway, it would have ended up that way.

Black mist began coiling around the witch. Curses come home to roost. The curses with nowhere to go – return to the caster.

“Guhh!”

The curses began Eroding various parts of the witch’s body. Staining her blood vessels black, eating away at her body.

Whether it caused pain or not, the witch let out an anguished cry. Probably, that would have reached the heart and crushed it –

“Annoying!”

The witch shouted irritably and made a shaking-off gesture.

She forcefully expelled two curses from her body, then – swept them away.

“…Demon.”

Sheila’s voice. Both expelling the curses from her body and sweeping them away was done with miasma.

It wasn’t worth being surprised about. I came out here precisely because I’d considered this possibility, and that’s why I blessed everyone here.

The man who served as the witch’s escort also seemed to have followed his master. Remaining airborne, he looked toward us. Unmoved by the witch’s miasma. He too – should be considered a demon.

“Claudia. Preparations?”

“I need just a little more time. I’m using Life Sense to identify everyone in this area so I can teleport them to both the ritual site and labyrinth simultaneously.”

“Understood.”

In short, we just need to restrain those demons so they can’t make any unnecessary moves until Claudia’s magic is complete.

“Theo – be careful.”

“May fortune favor you.”

“We’ll handle the other demon.”

“Understood. Everyone, be careful too.”

We nodded to each other, then turned our gaze toward the demons.

“I see, I see. So you had grasped our movements? Kukuku. We’ve been made fools of.”

The witch… no, the demon floated a tearing smile with eyes brimming with anger, rising miasma from her entire body as she looked down on us. On her back, enormous – iridescent butterfly wings shimmered.

Seems she’s motivated. That’s exactly what we want too.

“Come. I’ll smash you to pieces.”

I laughed in response to the demon, taking a Stance with Ouroboros. When I raised my magical power and emitted Spark Light, it also deepened its smile happily.

+++

# **227 – Knight of the Sand Beast**

“I’ll handle that magician. Belzelius, don’t let the others approach me. You can kill them, but keep the Marquis alive.”

“Understood.”

Belzelius’s body, having received instructions from the witch, began transforming into something inhuman. With massive horns and hard skin—it was a form indistinguishable from either a crustacean or a knight in full-body armor.

“Sand—?”

Marquis Zilbolt’s suspicious voice.

Yes. It was sand. From the gaps in the armor, sand continuously flowed out. The spilled sand solidified in the air one after another, taking shape—creating packs of sand beasts that resembled winged wolves.

Miasma leaking from the armor’s gaps was turning into sand and spilling out. This demon must possess such characteristics. It was sealing subordinate miscellaneous spirits that easily synchronize with negative emotions into vessels of sand.

“I am Belzelius of the Dust Fang. I shall take your lives.”

Just as a knight would. When Belzelius raised its sword before its face, the packs of sand beasts began moving simultaneously.

Grace, Sheila, and Ignis met the sand beasts head-on. Absurdly large mouths revealed jagged teeth. However, anything that touched Grace was destroyed in a single blow. Sand beasts split cleanly in two by the axe’s single strike returned to miasma, vanishing into the void as if evaporating. It was a scene reminiscent of a demon’s disappearance upon death. But the sand beasts held an overwhelming numerical advantage.

“To my side!”

Ashley and Marlene created defensive positions around Claudia and the Zilbolt Marquis household. Defense Fields and Ice Walls. Furthermore, they blocked approaching sand beasts with Saucers. Into this, Dullahan charged in and swept through with its greatsword.

Rosemary’s magic threads sliced through sand beasts with a whistling sound.

“There are too many enemies! We won’t get anywhere just defending!”

Irmhild shouted while firing arrows in rapid succession.

“I’m going in!”

Grace leaped from the terrace, stepping into the midst of the beast packs. Sand beasts were torn apart as if replaying the earlier scene, but the moment beasts that should have vanished touched Belzelius’s miasma, they reformed into their original shapes and bared their fangs.

The decision was instantaneous. Rather than charging at Belzelius itself, she drew a large arc as she jumped back, throwing her axe.

The chain wrapped in fighting spirit entangled the sand beasts like living creatures, hurling them far away. There, Irmhild’s arrows struck them. Arrows carrying Cursed Melodies shattered the sand beasts into dust.

“They regenerate when they touch the miasma!”

Even as she said this, Sheila charged into the enemy’s midst. Grace also reversed direction. Straight into the beast packs—flying directly toward Belzelius.

“Oh.”

At this sight, Belzelius let out an impressed sound.

Thinking about it differently, this meant that letting Belzelius approach the defensive positions would be troublesome. They had to hold back Belzelius itself amidst the regenerating beasts.

“Advance!”

At Rosemary’s voice, Ignis also leaped out to the front lines. The great hammer swung like a storm, blowing sand beasts to dust. Rosemary herself also stepped forward. Taking position in the Midguard, she met the beasts head-on.

“If they regenerate—how about this?”

Rosemary’s rainbow-colored threads entangled the approaching beasts. As Rosemary’s fingers moved complexly, as if playing a string instrument with a faint smile, she hijacked the sand beasts’ movements. Then she made them charge toward Belzelius itself.

“Quite entertaining!”

Belzelius, showing delight, shattered the controlled sand beast with its fist.

Sand gathered around the sword in Belzelius’s hand, taking a stance as if to sweep toward Rosemary.

“Your opponent isn’t over there!”

At that moment, Grace broke through the sand beasts and charged in. Belzelius’s sword swung while avoiding the roaring, approaching axe.

It was a sand tsunami. The wave of sand released along the sword’s trajectory, however, missed its target, completely shearing off the roof of a stone building. At its power, Rosemary frowned.

A composite magic of earth and wind, similar to Grind Dust. A technique that scrapes away everything with a torrent of hard sand. Moreover, it seemed to possess properties that crush with mass. The attack range was wide too, making it difficult to emerge unscathed even if blocked with a Magic Shield.

That’s precisely why Grace closed the distance. The current strike required charging time; if she kept attacking at close range, there would be no opportunity to launch it toward the rearguard. The axe strike was released with a storm-like roar, but it was deflected as if parried with the sword.

Grace didn’t resist the deflected momentum. Just as in training with Theodore. She let her body go with the flow, slipping through to the rear. As if to prevent pursuit, Sheila charged in exchange.

Belzelius met Sheila’s two swords with the sword in its hand and a shield of sand that solidified from miasma. After several metallic clashes, sand erupted explosively from its feet.

Whether sensing the explosion’s signs with all five senses, Sheila had leaped back moments before. As Belzelius took a stance with its sword showing pursuit, Grace charged in from the side.

This time, she wouldn’t let it deflect. She pressed in with her axe as if throwing her entire body into the charge. Fighting spirit and miasma. Their weapons clashed, scattering sparks. But only for a moment. A torrent of sand surged from outside her vision, which she avoided by kicking off her Shield.

Heaven and earth reversed, offense and defense exchanged, Grace and Sheila took turns cutting in. Smashing, thrusting, sweeping, exchanging slash attacks. Deflecting, flowing, receiving, sweeping. The muddy sand current surged with undulations.

A terrifying brilliance in martial arts. Movements that suggested years of considerable training.

Not enough hands. While crushing surrounding sand beasts with Ignis or binding and cutting them with magic threads, Rosemary gritted her teeth at the scene.

To prevent regenerating sand beasts from targeting Grace or Sheila, Ignis and Rosemary, Irmhild and Seraphina were going around destroying them.

But still not enough. Couldn’t handle them all. Sand beasts that slipped through to the rear were being dealt with by Ashley and Marlene at the defensive positions, plus Elmer and Donovan, and even the Marquis casting magic, but that was it.

Considering those who needed protection, the rearguard couldn’t advance. The Marquis and others could fight, but not to the extent of battling the demon itself.

The equilibrium couldn’t be broken. But then—it came.

“Sorry to keep you waiting!”

Along with Claudia’s voice, a massive magic array spread out, engulfing the surroundings. Identification-type multiple teleportation magic. To send the Marquis group to the ritual site. Magic to send Theodore’s group to the battlefield.

Ashley’s group around the defensive positions. Grace and Sheila fighting Belzelius. And even Theodore and the witch who were further away—were swallowed by white light—.

The dazzling brilliance lasted only a moment. Wrapped in light, after it subsided, they were before the Sealed Door in the Magic Light Water Vein.

A shallow area where water reached their ankles. The sound of flowing water. A massive hall located beyond the submerged cave. This was indeed the depths of the Magic Light Water Vein.

“We’re going!”

Ashley’s group, freed from defense, also moved.

Ashley on Lavigne’s back. Marlene riding Dullahan’s horse. Irmhild also stepped forward.

“Teleportation magic, you say…!”

Seeing this, Belzelius’s response was to gather the sand beasts. Consolidating most of them, it formed them into a giant centipede-like shape, then leaped onto its head to control it directly.

More than control—it was unification. Extending its own upper body from the centipede’s head, possessing both massive size and regeneration ability, it charged toward Ashley’s group while simultaneously engaging both Grace and Sheila.

Meanwhile, sand bullets scattered from the centipede’s body. Dullahan, kicking aside the bullets and charging through sand beasts blocking its path, struck the centipede’s body with a greatsword blow. But even after taking the long sword’s strike head-on, the centipede showed no reaction. As if in return, countless sand spears shot out from its back. Cutting them aside with the greatsword, batting them away with Saucers, it disengaged.

The wounds received from the greatsword closed instantly. A slash attack that would have torn apart ordinary creatures—that’s what it should have been.

“If it’s sand—then how about this!?”

Ashley, galloping with Lavigne, made her Magic Circle shine.

Sixth-class water-wind composite magic. Call Storm. Along with swirling storm winds, a fierce rain poured down as if buckets of water had been overturned.

Water soaked into the sand with tremendous force. The sand beasts’ movements visibly slowed. Perhaps the effect on the giant centipede was slower, as its movements remained unchanged.

But it was only a matter of time before deception became impossible. Whether Belzelius recognized Ashley as a powerful enemy with poor compatibility against itself, it turned the centipede’s head toward her and charged.

“I see. Compatibility—. Then I shall step forward.”

Seeing this, Rosemary smiled and stood blocking its path with Ignis. Then, she connected her magic threads to Ignis’s limbs.

“Let’s go…”

While feeling her own magical power being drawn into Ignis, Rosemary stepped forward with her doll. It enhanced reaction speed through direct doll control, plus by supplying magical power from Rosemary, it provided further output and strength amplification effects. The trump card Rosemary had envisioned since discovering puppet string magic.

Together with Ignis, she charged toward Belzelius with tremendous force.

Even the massive metal lump approaching with a roar was effortlessly deflected by Belzelius with a sand shield. Ignis’s body flowed aside, leaving Rosemary’s front completely open.

“What match is an artificial knight!?”

Belzelius roared.

Yes. Even if Rosemary herself directly crossed swords with Belzelius, she probably wouldn’t last more than a few exchanges. Even if Ignis stood at the forefront, controlling it with threads would still place Rosemary within Belzelius’s striking range.

As it gathered miasma in its hand to strike with sand spears and tried to block escape routes with the centipede’s massive body—an impact struck Belzelius’s head.

“Wha—!?”

“Artificial—what was that?”

Rosemary laughed mockingly. Ignis, still in the deflected posture, was positioned as if turning its back diagonally behind Belzelius. But using non-human joint mobility, it swung the great hammer from a direction Belzelius never anticipated, striking its head.

Belzelius’s eyes widened, and it instantly released miasma bullets. What scattered them as they flew toward Rosemary were Irmhild’s arrows and Marlene’s Saucers.

Rosemary smiled briefly toward the two, then took a position as if hiding behind Ignis’s back. As if not permitting even counterattacks with miasma bullets this time, Saucers orbited around her body.

“—Indeed. Compared to Grace or Sheila, I’m completely incompetent in close combat. Against you, who possesses enough martial skill and quantity to contend with those two… I shouldn’t normally stand a chance. But, as long as I have enough power and speed to resist, precisely because it’s an artificial doll, you cannot read its movements.”

That’s compatibility. Rosemary hid her mouth with her feather fan and laughed.

Ignis, with increased magical power supply, approached Belzelius while shining from its entire body. It swung down the massive hammer like a piece of wood, sweeping with its left claw.

Deflecting, blocking with sand shields—but it couldn’t cut through. The hammer that passed by rotated with its upper body and approached again from the side. Precisely because it somewhat resembles human form. Precisely because of training. The reaction inevitably delayed.

Struck in the flank, its upper body was swept away. Shallow. It had barely blocked with a sand shield at the last moment. But its posture was broken. Seeing an opportunity, Rosemary fired Fireballs toward Belzelius while controlling Ignis to pursue.

Ignis broke through the explosion blast, holding its left claw at its hip as it approached.

“Too naive!”

The thrust claw cut uselessly through empty air. It was like a hollow shell made of sand.

Belzelius slipped past Ignis and approached Rosemary.

Toward Rosemary, who stared wide-eyed, unable to react and frozen, Belzelius swung its sword. It should have caught Rosemary’s neck.

Metallic sound. In that hand was a crude great hammer. The figure that should have been Rosemary blurred, and Ignis appeared from beneath the illusion.

The distance, the cutting angle, everything was thrown off. Therefore, Belzelius couldn’t avoid the claw strike fired from point-blank range.

The explosion blast from the Fireball. The flow from that diversion, everything was groundwork. Both Rosemary and Belzelius, and Marlene too. Practitioners who employ something to fight. Precisely because the main body becomes the weakness no matter how one struggles, Belzelius must have trained extensively, and that’s why they understood each other’s aims.

“Explode!”

Rosemary poured all her remaining magical power, enhancing the doll’s output. The moment a small metallic sound was heard from the clamped claws—the next instant. With an explosion sound, the Pile Bunker detonated.

The Mithril Silver stake pierced a hole through Belzelius’s chest. Shattering the chest shell, piercing through the flesh and bone beneath—and there, where it was pinned, the stake itself released an explosion blast.

“Gah!?”

With the wound destroyed from inside, Belzelius’s body fell. The sand centipede also lost power, collapsing.

Rosemary, having had most of her magical power drained by that single strike, felt dizziness akin to oxygen deprivation, her expression clouding.

“As expected, the efficiency… is poor.”

Because she was amplifying output by channeling magical power through intermediate magic. She had understood the drawback to some extent.

When she looked toward the falling Belzelius—she could see miasma concentrating inside its oral cavity.

“Even if just one—!”

Couldn’t move. Having expended most of her refined magical power on the doll’s single strike, Rosemary had no reserve power to avoid it. Rosemary’s body—was pulled away from the line of fire in an unintended direction. Sheila’s sticky threads.

“It’s not just one person, is it?”

Rosemary closed her eyes and smiled. Her openings—someone would cover them. That’s why she could use such inefficient trump cards.

And the released miasma flash—. Grace had cleanly split it with a bamboo-splitter strike using her axe wrapped in fighting spirit.

“Oh—”

One flash. Leaving a purple-glowing fighting spirit trajectory in the Magic Light Water Vein’s great hall, Grace landed in the water. Moments later, Belzelius, split in two after having an axe struck into the Pile Bunker’s wound, fell into the water.

# **228 – The Devouring Princess Alvelinde**

A witch. Her true nature as a demon manifests as butterfly wings that shimmer with vibrant colors, along with gem-like, glowing oval decorations embedded throughout her body.

Fragments of light flicker around her form… Much like the silver smoke illusions created by that demon Zarbash we encountered before.

I can’t deny the possibility that her wing scales contain poison. As I deploy a wind defense field to cover my body, she actually deepens her smile with apparent delight, solidifying miasma into a sword wreathed in phosphorescence.

“Lady Alvelinde. I shall handle that one—”

“…No.”

Though her demon escort offers to fight me, the witch—Alvelinde—shakes her head, then laughs as she declares she’ll be my opponent herself.

It seems Alvelinde has determined me to be an enemy. She laughs while brimming with killing intent and fighting spirit.

The demon escort—Berzelius—will fight Grace and the others, while Alvelinde handles me. Both sides’ intentions align perfectly.

A one-on-one fight suits me just fine as well. We rise to face each other at eye level, glaring across the distance.

Caduceus will handle emergency support for our allies, communications to various positions.

And after Claudia activates her Teleportation Magic, he’ll secure our retreat route. That’s reassuring for me.

I shift my thoughts to combat readiness and begin refining my magical power.

Alvelinde. I did some research on demons… If I recall correctly, she’s the demon known by the epithet Corrosion Princess. They say she corroded and destroyed some kingdom from within during the era before barrier magic was established. Hence her title.

Since only her epithet has been passed down, I can’t gauge her abilities or true strength… But if she’s the same individual, she must be a considerably ancient demon.

We step forward simultaneously. Ouroboros and her sword clash, intertwining as they scatter Spark Light.

The next instant, I catch a glimmer of light at the edge of my vision. I twist my body reflexively, and immediately something like a ribbon from the lower part of her butterfly wings passes before my nose with tremendous force.

A Slash Attack. It likely possesses considerable sharpness. Using the momentum from my twist, I thrust with the opposite end of Ouroboros. Seeing her block it with a Miasma Wall, I immediately release a Magical Shockwave, knocking her arm aside. She makes a surprised face.

But Alvelinde didn’t resist the motion of being knocked back. She gracefully arcs backward as if dancing, using the momentum. Simultaneously, her sword comes sweeping upward as if to scoop me.

I twist to evade and pivot, closing the distance to sweep with Ouroboros, which her wing ribbons intercept.

Turning to face me, Alvelinde bares her teeth in a smile, then stands her ground to receive my attack. Using my staff and Chimera Coat, I counter her sword and wings. We engage in countless exchanges of Strikes and Slash Attacks at close range.

We trace afterimage trajectories across the night sky, magical power and miasma colliding to scatter explosive sparks as we spiral upward. Our bodies crash together. We rebound off each other and pivot. Exchanging low-tier magic and Miasma Bullets while closing in, we trade attacks as we pass by each other.

Her wings are essentially miasma formed into high-density butterfly wings. They lack substance, or more precisely, the wings themselves seem to lack pain receptors—even when I land impact-based Techniques, I see no effect.

Whether she realizes this or not, she’s shifted to using her wings as her primary attack method. She uses her sword to block attacks from Nemea and Capella, or alternatively, she’s begun employing methods where she wraps miasma around it, then releases Slash Attacks or Thrusts like Miasma Bullets when creating distance.

Just as we were about to charge directly at each other—Claudia’s Teleportation Magic arrived. Our surroundings were enveloped in white light, and we were transported to the Magic Light Water Vein.

For us, this went according to plan. For them, it was an unexpected development. Well then, I’ll just charge forward regardless.

I swing down from a High Stance. At that moment, she displayed another different movement. While leaping backward, her butterfly wings enveloped her body, and then her form disappeared as if blending into the scenery. The movement of an object, the flow of air. This isn’t teleportation!

Swinging Ouroboros on instinct, a metallic sound rings out. She too had been swinging her sword trying to take my head.

Baring her teeth in a smile, she slams a Miasma Bullet at me from point-blank range. When I block it with a Shield, an explosion occurs, and the recoil creates distance between us.

“I never imagined I’d be outnumbered in techniques. Those various skills. And the one who performed the teleportation was the Labyrinth’s master. I see, so it was you…”

Judging from her earlier response and words—she knows the true nature and properties of the techniques Gardinis used.

There’s undoubtedly a connection with those demons, but that raises the question of how much the Crown Prince knows, or whether the Crown Prince himself is even human. But I doubt she’d answer such questions honestly if I asked.

Alvelinde spreads both arms wide. Wing scales spilling from her wings gather and condense. Crystal-like formations float here and there.

The crystals—show no movement. They simply float in place. Probably a setup for something.

Shining miasma gathers above Alvelinde’s head—Here it comes!

I dodge at the last possible moment. A glowing bluish-green ray—or perhaps it would be better to call it a heat ray. Something carrying intense heat passes right by my body. Yes. Probably that kind of technique—.

When it hits a crystal, it reflects and comes rushing toward me. I deploy a Shield along the anticipated trajectory to defend. Even after generating mist with Dark Magic and Water Magic inside, only scorching heat comes through.

The power has likely been significantly attenuated—but she too possesses attack methods that can ignore Magic Shields. Creating mist to aim for attenuation—would be unwise. It would likely create a field advantageous to her.

That earlier technique where she disappeared is similar too. She probably has techniques that transform miasma into light-like properties, then reflect or refract it. With mist, even if I aim for attenuation, I can’t completely neutralize the power, and if she turns it against me by projecting illusions like a screen, it would be troublesome.

I raise Ouroboros into a Stance and begin amplifying my magical power. I wrap excess magical power around my body. Two, then three spheres of light float above her head.

Time to commit. Either way, engaging in a shooting battle would put me at a disadvantage. Those reflection crystals—she can probably produce them endlessly, and destroying them would be meaningless. Then it’s the same as before. She too must avoid self-destruction from reflections. Close quarters with limited firing lines is my only path forward.

“Here I come!”

Combining my strength with Chimera Coat’s, I charge straight in, kicking from Shield to Shield to perform rapid reflection movements. She responds at maximum speed as well.

We exchange magic and Miasma Bullets while flying at high speed. Strikes as we pass each other. That much is the same as before.

In the scenery flowing by at ridiculous speeds, I grasp each position. Me and her. And the crystal coordinates. The moment I detect the precursor of the light spheres floating above Alvelinde about to be fired, I deploy Shields along the firing lines. Regardless of whether they’re aimed at me or not.

From crystal to crystal. Each time a light Spear flashes, Shields instantly appear around my body. From crystal to crystal. Reflection upon reflection. In this roulette of swirling light trajectories, one particular crystal becomes the main battery aiming for me.

A flash coming straight at me. Heat at my flank. I might get burned, but since it’s attenuated, it won’t be a Fatal Wound. As long as it doesn’t have knockback properties, I can ignore the pain. I exchange perfect defense for amplifying magical power.

When I close the distance and step in, her wings swing. One, two—I slip through her Slash Attacks. The distance and angles were unique so I was somewhat confused—but I’m growing accustomed to these wing movements too. Using Nemea and Capella not for offense and defense, but adding to my mobility to suddenly plunge into close range, I slam an impact through the Shield. Then, her face contorts for a moment. While her expression twists, Alvelinde still laughs.

“You do unbelievable things!”

She spins her body. While unleashing numerous Slash Attacks with her wings, the glowing spheres above her head flash—three, four. At this range, she can’t shoot from behind!

I fly upward to disengage. A moment later, reflected light from the crystals pierces through where I was from left and right.

“Ooooh!”

Alvelinde generates a massive crystal in her palm. Making light explode from it, the light spreads radially upward. A move that anticipated me flying upward.

But while the range is wide, it lacks convergence. I deploy a Shield forward and charge straight toward the light source. Breaking through, I swing Ouroboros down. A direct hit. As she grits her teeth to endure, she slams not with her sword but directly with a Palm Strike. I block with a Shield and try to counter with a magical shock—but faster than that, Alvelinde makes light explode. Scorching heat. I too slam a magical shock into her palm regardless.

“Gah!”

We both create distance. I’m somewhat scorched too, but I’ve properly damaged her left arm. It probably won’t be usable in offense and defense for a while. Though her weapons are her wings more than her limbs.

“Are you truly human? Surely you’re not one of our kind?”

“Save your sleep-talking for when you’re asleep.”

After this brief exchange, we charge at each other as if by mutual agreement. Light Spears reflect repeatedly here and there. I too fly around with high-speed reflections from Shield to Shield as I charge in.

By dedicating Nemea and Capella to mobility, I exceed her maximum speed. Reading her movement direction, I fly alongside, forcibly bringing us to close combat. We slam staff and sword against each other, I evade her wing Slash Attacks by a hair’s breadth.

Flank. Shin. Jaw. I swing Ouroboros around and land three attacks, causing enormous miasma to erupt from her body.

“Ooooooooh aaaaaaaah!”

A roar, and chaotic reflections of light. Light Spears crisscross above and below like a cage. Spreading both arms wide, she unleashes wing Slash Attacks from left and right as if to crush me. When I block the Slash Attacks with Nemea and Capella, wing ribbons wrap around them as if to capture both. There’s—only one intention behind this. If her Martial Arts and speed surpass mine, then I should abandon defense and unleash a major Technique.

“I’ve caught you!”

Light particles converge before Alvelinde, who’s gritting her teeth. A maximum-level attack. I’ve already deployed a Magic Circle too. My only option is to counter with magic.

Water Magic 9th Tier: Abyss Serpent. From an enormous Magic Circle, a Water Dragon’s maw of corresponding size emerges. And then—overwhelming white light slams into it.

“I’ll evaporate you right here!”

Alvelinde roars. Even through the Water Dragon’s head, I feel a burning sensation from the light’s heat. The water dragon bubbles and swells from within. I cover my face with my arm to protect my retinas from burning.

It’s fine. I’m clearly tracking her form through Caduceus’s vision. I won’t let her escape anywhere.

“Wha—?”

At that sight, Alvelinde’s eyes widen, and I laugh. Yes. The compatibility isn’t bad. The only flaw is that completion takes a little time. But in this location, I can definitely finish her off.

All the water of the Magic Light Water Vein gathers toward the created Serpent. Compressing and condensing at high density, the Serpent grows monstrously large. Of course. I’ve poured in magical power equivalent to two High-Tier Magic spells.

“Take this!”

“O—oooooooh!”

The Serpent opens its massive maw and advances toward Alvelinde, who’s still emitting light. Its great jaws seize her.

It shreds the butterfly wings like paper scraps, then crushes Alvelinde with its enormous fangs. She deploys a Miasma Wall around her body to endure, but that too is futile. It effortlessly crushes her with water pressure, concentrating immense hydraulic force into a single point as it charges straight—toward the Magic Light Water Vein’s wall.

A great waterfall in the shape of a dragon moving sideways. All that water pressure converges solely upon whoever is swallowed.

The Serpent’s body contracts momentarily to apply final pressure, then expands. Following the Spell Formula’s completion, it triggers a massive water explosion.

+++
